For planets distant by 60 parts in the Ecliptic see each other by a sextile, by 90 parts by a square, by 120 parts by a trine, by 180 parts by an opposition. If you do not find this exact number of parts, first look at Saturn, and consider which of the other planets, or if the aspect of any planet, precedes it, within the orbs of rays, noted above according to Ptolemy's opinion, or if the opinions of others delight you, within the half-orb, as they call it, for it is said to apply to the same. Similarly, if you find a planet or aspect following Saturn within the said limits, you will pronounce the same planet to be separating or defluxing from Saturn. In the proposed example, Venus applies to Saturn by a sinister sextile. And Jupiter, separating from Saturn by a dexter sextile, applies to the Moon by a trine and to the body of Mercury, etc. After Saturn is completed, the remaining heavier planets are to be similarly compared to the lighter ones. What we should attribute to the latitudes of the stars in judging aspects, we have discussed at length above. 336 DIFFERENCE. And when it is 2. Kenodromia, or the empty course of a planet, is when it is not mixed with other stars, etc., that is, when it is separated from the conjunction of any other, and is not joined to another by body or aspect, and as long as the planet is in the same sign, it is said to be empty in course, which is to be understood according to the orbs of rays, which we have just defined. This accident is observed especially in the Moon (an example is in Ptolemy, book 3, chapter on parents), and is almost neglected in others. For example, let the Moon be in conjunction with Jupiter, and after its separation from Jupiter, let there be no planet in Sagittarius to which it can be joined within the prescribed limits, nor any ray of anyone it can aspect; the Moon will be said to be empty in course until, having passed Sagittarius, it is joined to someone by body or aspect. And when it is, 3. A feral planet is named when it is alone in a sign, separated from the conjunction of others and from their aspecting rays, thus named from the likeness of a man alienated from society, or a wild beast living in solitude. In this way, the strength of planets becomes languid and is significantly weakened, especially if they are also peregrine at the same time. A planet is called peregrine when it is not in any of its essential dignities, as Saturn in the 6th part, because it has no dignity, it is considered peregrine. The difference between kenodromia and feralitas is that in the former, the star in the sign it traverses has a companion ray from which it separates; in the latter, however, it is deprived of all light from others. And when it separates, etc. 4. Translation of light or nature is what occurs when there are three planets, and the lightest is in the middle between the others and within the orbs: Then the lightest is said to transfer the light of the anterior to the subsequent: Therefore, the meaning of the author's words is, when the light planet separates from the heavy one and, before the complete separation, joins another by body or aspect: then that light planet transfers the light and nature of the first to the second: for example, let Jupiter be in the 4th part of Pisces, the Moon in the 15th part of Pisces, Mars in the 21st part of Leo. Here the Moon separates from Jupiter corporally, and before the complete separation, applying itself from a square to Mars, it transfers the light of Jupiter to him. For the light of Jupiter is 12 parts, and that of Mars is 7 parts, as we have placed above. Another example, let Venus be in the 8th part of Gemini, the Moon in the 10th part of Gemini, Jupiter in the 10th part of Pisces. Here Venus separates from the sextile aspect of Mercury, and is partially joined to Jupiter by a square, and transfers the light of Mercury to Jupiter himself. However, it does not prohibit Mercury from conjunction with Jupiter. For Gemini and Pisces are disjunct signs. I add this so that no one would think that the translation of light and the prohibition from aspect, which will be discussed later, do not differ. Another mode of translation of light, very similar to the former, follows. When, he says, a light planet joins a heavier one by any conjunction, and that heavier one in turn joins another still heavier one: then the middle one is said to transfer the nature of the lightest to the heaviest. Example, let Jupiter be in the 15th part of Leo, the Moon in the 14th part of Taurus, Saturn in the 16th part of Taurus. Here Jupiter, mixed with the Moon by a sextile aspect, makes Saturn partake of the nature of the Moon, although the Moon itself is plainly unconjoined with Saturn. Otherwise and better. When three planets are in one sign, if the heavier is in more parts, and the lighter in fewer, and not within the orbs, but the middle one is within the orb of application to the slower, and within the orb by which the lighter applies to it: then the middle one is said to transfer the power of the lighter to the slower: as if the Sun is in the 29th part of Leo, Jupiter in the 28th part of Leo, Saturn in the 18th part of Leo. Here Jupiter transfers power to Saturn. This is the general way of translations, which some moderns restrict to a few cases. For they call the translation of light and virtue to occur only when a light planet separates from a heavier one, and applies to another of the same quality: as if the Sun is in the 1st part of Aries, the Moon in the 1st part of Gemini, Mars in the 8th part of Gemini. In this case, the Moon, separating from the Sun, and applying to the body of Mars, transfers heat to Mars, who is also hot. For the Sun bestows its power, which the Moon received from it by aspect, to Mars. 6. Reddi.

[Calculating Conception Time and House Cusps]
However, the hour and remaining minutes of conception are inquired as follows: From the ascension of the climate, beginning from the start of Aries, of the place which the Moon held at the estimated time of birth, subtract the right ascension, beginning from Capricorn, of the Sun's place for the completed day of conception. For what remains, if converted into time, will show the hours and minutes of conception. Or, alternatively, enter with the Sun's place for the estimated time of conception into the table of houses for your climate under the title of the tenth house, and note the corresponding time in the margin. Then, similarly, by the motion of the estimated day of birth, extract the time from the same table under the title of the first house. Having done this, subtract the time from the time (assuming 24 hours if subtraction cannot be performed), and the hours and minutes of the true conception will remain, which are to be added to the previously found completed days. To the time thus formed, the true place is to be sought, which is judged to be the true degree of the rising cardinal point in the genesis according to this method. In our example, the lunar epoch's oblique ascension calculated from Aries is 341 degrees, 318 minutes. The Sun's true place at midday of the given day is found to be 28 degrees, 12 minutes of Leo, and the ascension of the same place, beginning from Capricorn, is 240 degrees, 231 minutes. Subtracting this from the oblique ascension of the Moon's place leaves 100 degrees, 4013 minutes, which is 6 hours, 43 minutes, 12 seconds. The same time is more easily collected from the table of houses constructed for latitude 41 degrees, thus: Hours, minutes, seconds. Time of Moon's birth under the title of the first house: 16. Time of Sun's conception under the title of the tenth house: 10. Post-meridian hours of conception: 6 hours, 45 minutes, 2 seconds, 43 minutes. Therefore, according to this calculation, conception occurred in the year of Christ 1526, on August 12, at 6 hours, 43 minutes, 1 second. At this time, the Moon's true place is 24 degrees, 101 minutes of Libra, and this is the same part of the sky horoscoping at the time of birth, explored by the balance of Hermes. How, once the horoscope or midheaven is known, the other cusps become known. If the midheaven is known, its right ascension and the oblique ascensions of the other cusps will not be hidden by what we said above in the first difference concerning the construction of the celestial domiciles. But if you have examined the horoscope, then from its ascension in the climate, subtract 90 degrees, accommodating a full revolution if necessary, and the ascension of the midheaven will remain. Knowing this, by continuous addition of 30 degrees, you inquire into the ascensions of the remaining five subsequent cusps, and for each ascension, you extract the corresponding degrees of the Ecliptic from the tables suitable for each cusp, as explained above. Furthermore, how, given the ascendant or midheaven, the other cusps are to be described from the table of the equation of houses, is sufficiently apparent from the table itself, which contains the position of the hemisphere on the sides of each cardinal point. All these things are clearer in themselves than to need elucidation by examples. Finally, you will investigate the time of true birth in this way: Find the oblique ascension of the ascendant degree, both estimated and corrected, and subtract the smaller from the larger. Convert the difference into time, and add it to the estimated time if the oblique ascension of the corrected horoscope was greater than that of the estimated one, that is, if the true birth preceded the estimated one, or subtract it if the opposite occurred. But if you use tables for equating houses, compare the time written in the table of equations next to the degree of the estimated midheaven with the time written in the same table next to the degree of the corrected midheaven, and subtract the smaller from the larger. Add the difference to the estimated time if the horoscoping degree at the estimated time preceded the true horoscope, or subtract it from the same if the opposite occurred, and the time of true birth will result. To this, if we also describe the motions of the stars with the nodes of the Moon and perhaps the parts of fortune, we will obtain a celestial figure complete in all respects. And from this, the Hylech, that is, the place of life in nativities, whose knowledge is such that you first look at the hour of birth. If it is in the day, you begin with the Sun: if it is within 5 degrees or less before the degree of the ascendant sign, or if it is in the 10th or 11th house, whether the sign is masculine or feminine, it will be suitable to be the Hylech. But if it is in these three places, namely in the 7th, 8th, or 9th house in a masculine sign, it will similarly be suitable to be the Hylech. If, however, it is in these three places in a feminine sign, it will not be suitable to be the Hylech. Next, you look at the Moon: if it is in the ascendant or in the 2nd or 3rd house, or in the 7th or 8th house, it will be suitable to be the Hylech, whether the sign is masculine or feminine. And if it is within 5 degrees or less before the degree of the ascendant sign: or if it is in the 10th or 11th house, or in the 4th or 5th house, or in the 7th house in a feminine sign, it will be suitable to be the Hylech. But if it is in any of these in a masculine sign, it will not be suitable to be the Hylech, if the birth was in the day. If, however, the birth was at night, we begin with the Moon: if it is in any of the aforementioned places, according to what we have said, it will be suitable to be the Hylech. But if the Moon is not in them, you then look at the Sun, which if it is within 5 degrees or less before the degree of the 7th house, or if it is in the 4th or 5th house, it will be suitable to be the Hylech, whether the sign is masculine or feminine. But if it is within 5 degrees or less before the ascendant: or in the ascendant, or in the second masculine sign, then it will also be suitable to be the Hylech. But if it is in any of these places in a feminine sign, it will not be suitable to be the Hylech. If neither of the luminaries is suitable to be the Hylech: Then look at the day of birth, whether it is conjunct or pre-conjunct, that is, whether it is after the conjunction or before the conjunction. If the birth was conjunct, and the degree of conjunction was in any of the angles: or in a succeeding angle: it will be in a suitable place for the Hylech. But if the aforementioned degree was falling from these eight places, i.e., from the angles and from the succeeding angles, it will not be the Hylech. Then you look at the degree of the Part of Fortune: if it is in any of the angles, or in the succeeding angles: it will be in a suitable place for the Hylech. But if it was falling from these eight places: you then look at the degree of the ascendant and establish it as the Hylech. If, however, the birth was pre-conjunct, you begin with the degree of the pre-conjunction, and you look at it as you did before with the degree of conjunction: and after it, the degree of the Part of Fortune: after it, the degree of the ascendant in the order we mentioned for the degree of conjunction. You will not care about the gender of the signs, i.e., you will not look whether those signs are masculine or feminine, except only in the luminaries, that is, in the degree of conjunction, or pre-conjunction and ascendant and Part of Fortune, you do not consider whether they are in masculine or feminine signs, both in the angles and in the succeeding angles: but these four will only be suitable to be the Hylech when they are in these eight places, that is, in the angles or their succedents: but if they are in receding places, that is, falling from the angles, they will not be suitable to be the Hylech. It appears therefore that the Sun is suitable to be the Hylech by day, and by night above the earth, and below the earth in 11 places, above the earth in 6 places and below the earth in 5. The Moon will also be suitable to be the Hylech by day, and by night above the earth, and below the earth similarly in 11 places, above the earth in 10 and below the earth in 6. And with

[Malefic Squares and Anareta]
squares into the beginning of Gemini: these square rays of the malefic can oppress the Apheta Sun, even if Saturn does not aspect it from the beginning. But the same condition is also required in the obedient, whom malefics rule like tyrants. Therefore, when the place of the Apheta obeys the place of the Anareta, then the Anareta, led to the Apheta, destroys it. But indeed, since bodies worn out by old age are easily dissipated by a slight cause, the antiscia of evils in the elderly can oppress the lord of life through itself without the aforementioned condition. Hence, the trines of malefics from short ascension signs, when afflicted, kill; and conversely, the corrupted sextiles from long ascension signs kill for the same reason. To easily discern these radiations, look at the aspecting place and the place into which the rays fall, and if the houses of these places aspect each other by a sextile, the nature of that ray will be sextile; and if the houses aspect each other by a square, the nature of the ray will be square; and if by a trine, a trine. Hence, the Imum Coeli always aspects the Ascendant by a square in equinoctial signs, as if Taurus, an equinoctial sign, is understood to be in the Imum Coeli when Gemini ascends, even though by zodiacal reckoning, the sign of Gemini is found there. Such squares also kill because signs aspecting each other by a square are universally of contrary nature. Finally, when one enters a moderate life, the place of the Sun also kills, namely, when oppressed by the conjunction of some malefic, it is helped or freed by no benefic. Therefore, since a malefic is the cause, so that a focus falling upon the Moon, being the Apheta, kills, it follows that if a benefic is placed in the place of the malefic with the Sun, it will by no means kill the place of the Sun. The Arabs add the sixth, seventh, and eighth cusps to the Anaretas we have enumerated, and the lords of those cusps. Similarly, also the fourth cusp, when it is found to be watery and unfortunate. Also dark places, nebulous places, places of Eclipses, places of Comets appearing at the time of birth, the Heart of Scorpio, the Heart of Leo, also the Moon, the part of Mars, the part of Azemena; finally, they say that the rays of Mercury also impede.

[Profections of the World's Years]
Regarding the profections of the world's years, whose epochs are taken from great conjunctions, we have deliberately omitted a broader and more detailed explanation. This is partly because the entire matter seems suspicious to us in general, and full of absurd errors for the reasons previously stated. It is also because it is inherently simple and sufficiently clear from what we have said about the profections of nativities, except that Alcabitius introduces some difficulty by adapting the profections of the world's years not to Solar years, but to Persian years.

[On the Direction of the Significator]
From this follows the atazir, that is, the direction: this means that you direct a certain significator to a certain place of the signs, and you know what is between them in degrees of direction, and you will take one year for each degree. Therefore, when you wish to know this, and that significator is in the ascendant, which you wish to direct to some part of the circle, subtract the ascensions of the degree in which the significator you wish to direct is, by the ascensions of the region from the ascensions of that degree to which you wish to direct it: and what remains will be the degree of direction. But if the significator is in the degree of the seventh house: you will subtract the ascensions of the nadir, that is, the opposite of the degree in which the significator is, from the ascensions of the nadir of that degree to which you wish to direct it in that region. But if the significator is in the Midheaven or in the Imum Coeli: you will subtract the ascensions of the significator's degree from the ascensions of that degree to which you wish to direct it by the ascensions of the direct circle: and what remains will be the degree of direction.

[Significator Outside Angles]
If, however, the significator you wish to direct is in some place outside the four angles: you will look at its longitude from one of these angles, which are the angle of the Midheaven and the angle of the Imum Coeli: that is, you will look at the significator, and if it is between the ascendant and the Midheaven, you will subtract the ascensions of the degree of the Midheaven by the direct circle from the ascensions of the significator's degree. And if it is between the seventh house and the Midheaven: you will subtract the ascensions of the significator's degree from the ascensions of the Midheaven's degree by the direct circle: and what remains, from whichever of these places it may be, you will divide by the parts of the hours of that day of the degree in which the significator is: and what comes out will be the hours of longitude from the angle. And if it is between the ascendant and the Imum Coeli: you will subtract the ascensions of the significator's degree by the direct circle from the ascensions of the degree of the Imum Coeli. Again, if the significator is between the Imum Coeli and the seventh house: you will subtract the ascensions of the degree of the Imum Coeli by the direct circle from the ascensions of the significator's degree: and what remains from whichever of these places, you will divide by the time, that is, by the hours of the day of the nadir, that is, the opposite of the significator's degree: and what comes out will be the hours of longitude from the angle. When you have known the hours of longitude from the angle, and you wish to direct the significator to some place of the circle of signs: and the significator is in the middle of the eastern circle, which is from the Midheaven to the Imum Coeli, of those that succeed the ascendant: subtract the ascensions of that degree in which the significator is from the ascensions of that degree to which you wish to direct it by the direct circle: and what remains will be the significator of the direct circle: keep it. After this, you will subtract the ascensions of that degree in which the significator is by the ascensions of the region from the ascensions of that degree to which you wish to direct it: and what remains will be the significator of the region: after this, look at the remainder, which is between the significator of the direct circle and the significator of the region, and you will take its sixth part, and multiply it by the hours of longitude from the angle, and what results will be the equation: and if the significator of the direct circle is less than the significator of the region: add the equation to the significator of the direct circle. And if the significator of the direct circle is greater, subtract the equation from it: and what remains will be the degree of direction.

[Significator in Western Circle]
Likewise, if the significator you wish to direct is in the middle of the western circle: which is from the Imum Coeli to the Midheaven of what succeeds the seventh house: you will subtract the ascensions of the nadir of the significator's degree, which you wish to direct, from the ascensions of the nadir of that degree to which you wish to direct it, by the direct circle: and what remains will be the significator of the direct circle. After this, you will subtract the ascensions of the nadir of the significator's degree by the ascensions of the region from the ascensions of the nadir of that degree to which you wish to direct it: and what remains will be the significator of the region: then you will take the remainder, which is between the significator of the direct circle and the significator of the region, and you will take its sixth part, and multiply it by the hours of longitude from the angle: and what results will be the equation. After this, you will look at the significator of the direct circle, if it is less than the significator of the region, you will add the equation to the significator of the direct circle: and if the significator of the direct circle...

[Calculating Solar Arc to Setting]
The fourth part. 415. The diurnal temporal hours of the same are 18 parts, 27 scruples, 14 seconds. The setting, however, is distant from the midheaven by six temporal hours, which, when multiplied by the diurnal temporal hours of the Sun, produce 110 parts, 42 scruples, 14 seconds of temporal hours, by which the Sun's place is distant from the culmination when it sets. According to the first position, it was distant towards the same part of the times by 56 parts, 57 scruples, 14 seconds, which, when subtracted from the second distance, namely from 110 parts, 42 scruples, 14 seconds, leave 53 parts, 45 scruples, 18 seconds of time, during which the Sun, found above the earth, moves towards its setting. And in plainly the same times, the arc intercepted between the Sun's place and the setting descends almost, in the latitude of the place, 41 parts. Having thus calculated these, I consider the radiations falling between the Sun's place and the west, and I find them to be of the Moon, and Mars, the Sun, and Venus. None of these rays destroys the Apheta by its opposition, but some of them add strength to the Apheta, while others weaken it. Indeed, as much as the sextile of Venus adds, the square of the Moon seems to subtract. Again, as much as the opposition of Mars subtracts, the sextile of the Sun seems to add. But nevertheless, for this calculation to have a place in our example, let us suppose that only the diametral radiation of Mars remains below the earth, residing in 28 parts, 21 scruples, 1 second of Scorpio, which can subtract some years from the direction of the Apheta towards the western part. Therefore, to know how much it subtracts, take the nocturnal temporal parts of Mars's place residing in 28 parts, 21 scruples, 1 second of Scorpio, which under an elevation of the pole of 41 parts are 16 parts, 50 scruples, 14 seconds. Not, indeed, because the nativity is nocturnal do we take nocturnal temporal hours, but because the planet whose rays these are is below the earth. If it were above the earth, we would have to take diurnal temporal hours, even if the nativity were nocturnal. Having thus considered these, next inquire how many nocturnal hours Mars is distant from the west, and you will find almost exactly ten hours. Now proceed according to the rule of proportions in this manner: 12 hours subtract 16 parts, 50 scruples, 14 seconds; how much will 10 hours subtract? Multiply the second number by the third, that is, multiply 10 hours by 16 parts, 50 scruples, 14 seconds, and you will produce 62 parts, 48 scruples, 20 seconds, that is, 168 parts, 20 scruples, 14 seconds, which, divided by the first number, that is, by 12, yield approximately 14 parts, 2 scruples, 14 seconds, to be subtracted from 53 parts, 45 scruples, 14 seconds, by which the Sun moves towards its setting. 416. By which fact, there remain 39 parts, 43 scruples, 1 second of this direction. That this is Ptolemy's true opinion concerning this form of direction can be understood from his own words, which are found in the third Apotelesmatic, where, speaking of measuring the span of life, he wrote thus: "The destructive degrees in the moderation of life, which is perfected through the preceding signs, are none, except only the western limiting line, because it hides the lord of life. Moreover, the parts of the stars occurring in this manner, either corporeally or by aspect, only subtract or add years to those collected from the apheta up to its setting, and do not destroy, because these do not impinge upon the aphetic place, but rather that place moves into theirs. And the benefics add, but the malefics subtract. Mercury, again, as usual, adds strength to those with whom it is configured. The number of time to be added or subtracted is observed from the position of each part. For as many temporal hours as there are for each part, diurnal during the day, nocturnal during the night, so many years are signified, but in such a way that for those remaining at the rising, this entire number is preserved, and afterwards, according to the proportion of their departure from the rising, it is attenuated until it vanishes at the setting." Since we have reviewed the etymology, definition, and species of directions, and moreover, in an example, have made clear the treatment of the aphesis in the preceding signs, it remains for us to explain the methods by which the aphetic places are led through the consequent signs. The first and easiest is by the solid sphere, which you can see in treatises on the use of the solid sphere. The second is by an astrolabe or planisphere of great amplitude, where the outer limb is divided into 3600 parts. The third, and most exact, is that which the most learned man Johannes Regiomontanus expounded in his tables of directions and progressions. The fourth is the author's, derived from Ptolemy's opinion. The fifth and older method is proper to Ptolemy, which is easier and shorter than others: for everything can be accomplished by the Sun's tables of right ascensions and by the table of the quantity of days. And although most astrologers of our age approve the method of directing according to the doctrine and tables of Regiomontanus, nevertheless, for the reasons stated above when we were dealing with bodily conjunctions, Ptolemy's method satisfies us, and seems to agree more simply with his precepts of the art, and therefore with truth. For we could not find a single word in the Quadripartitum by which the most diligent and wisest of mortals, Ptolemy, could seem to us to have even insinuated that in the deductions of aphetic places, by which only the times of events are defined, the observation of deviations from the ecliptic is useful. Cardan also, a great master, preferred this ancient method of directing handed down by Ptolemy, and in his old age, almost disdaining and neglecting that exact method of Regiomontanus, which he had practiced in his youth, because of its extreme difficulty and labor. His words on this matter in his commentaries on Ptolemy's Book 3 are these: "The most exact method of directing is by the tables of Johannes de Regiomonte, who in our age undertook this most illustrious and difficult labor; but if the difficulty of execution brought equal utility to the labors, it would certainly be altogether preferable to use them." And a little further on, he prefers the use of suitable instruments to these tables. "Stars," he says, "are said to co-ascend whenever they are in the same semicircle of position; and if you wish to find this, it can be done by a planisphere, or even better by a solid sphere. I do not forbid you to do it by the tables of Johannes Monteregius, and they are more exact than instruments, unless the instruments are very large. However, the use of tables is very tedious, laborious, and prone to error, and especially because Monteregius did badly in this, 8.

[Planetary Position and Horary Times]
The diametrically opposite point is removed from the Midheaven, and the nocturnal hour below the earth is equal to the diurnal hour of the diametrically opposite point above the earth. Furthermore, how the horary times of the Sun and other places, both diurnal and nocturnal, can easily be found, has been abundantly demonstrated above at the end of the second difference in the chapter on hours. If you ever doubt whether a star is above or below the earth, or whether it is in the western or eastern half, you will most easily be certain of these occurrences from the points with which the star rises or descends, and with which it culminates. For if the point with which the star rises is in the eastern part, but has not yet risen, know that the star has not yet risen. Again, if the point with which the star descends is in the western part, but has not yet set, it is certain that the star has not yet set. Similarly, from the point with which the star culminates, we will deduce whether the star is in the eastern or western half: for if the point with which the star crosses the meridian is above the earth, but has not yet crossed the meridian, know that the star itself is in the eastern part. But if the same point is below the earth, but has not yet crossed the Imum Coeli, we will conclude that the star is also in the western half. In this way, from the position of the point with which the star rises, sets, and culminates, it is clearly deduced whether the star itself is above or below the earth, or occupies the eastern or western half, or finally falls on the ascendant/descendant or meridian. Finally, the said points, since they correspond to the ascensions and descensions of the stars, cannot be hidden. But there is still another and easier way to find the point with which a star sets. For if you add its diurnal arc to the oblique ascension of the star itself, the oblique ascension of the rising point will emerge while the star sets: once this is known, the point diametrically opposite to it, with which the proposed star must set, will by no means be hidden. With these preparations, bring the Apheta or significator, as if it were on the cusps, twice to the promittor. And first, by the ascensions or descensions of the sphere, you will collect the arc of direction, which the author here calls the significator of the direct circle. Secondly, by the ascensions or descensions of the climate, calculate the second arc of direction, which the author calls the significator of the region: having done this, subtract the smaller arc of direction from the larger, and divide the remainder by 6 (for one quadrant, as is clear from the above, contains 6 temporal hours), and multiply the resulting sixth part by the number of hours by which the Apheta or significator was previously calculated to be distant from the meridian: what is generated from this multiplication the author calls the equation, which is to be added to the direction of the sphere if the direction of the climate was smaller, or subtracted from it if the opposite occurred, for the remaining or composite number will show the sought-after times of direction. And one must work by ascensions when the Apheta is in the ascending half: but by descensions, or by the ascensions of opposite points, when the same significator holds the descending half. The sum of this passage is therefore: if the Apheta is above the earth, the difference of the right ascension from the Midheaven must be taken, and divided by the diurnal horary times: but if it is below the earth, the difference of the right ascension from the Imum Coeli must be taken, and divided by the nocturnal horary times of the Apheta, so that the temporal hours by which the Apheta is distant from the culmination of the heavens emerge. Therefore, if the Apheta is between the Midheaven and the Ascendant, the temporal hours of the subsequent distance will emerge: but if between the Midheaven and the western Cardine, of the preceding distance, similarly if the Apheta is between the horoscope and the Imum Coeli, the hours of the preceding distance will emerge, which is in all respects equal to the diurnal preceding distance of the opposite point in the upper hemisphere. Finally, if it is between the Imum Coeli and the western ascendant/descendant, the hours of the subsequent distance will emerge, and similarly in all respects equal to the subsequent distance in the upper hemisphere and in the diametrically opposite point, because opposite quadrants of the heavens correspond entirely to each other. Once such a distance is known, immediately the difference of the two directions, collected in the manner we have explained, by a double operation, namely of the sphere and of the climate, and thus collected, must be divided by six, so that the number of the προπαφαιρίσεως, that is, which is to be added to or subtracted from the direction of the sphere, emerges. An example of the significator in the ascending half, and in.

[Fifth Difference: Commemoration of All Parts]
FIFTH DIFFERENCE in the commemoration of all parts. And since we have completed the explanations of those things that follow from the names of the astrologers, let us now execute the commemoration of all parts. And when we have noted in the place of the parts: take from that place to that place, project this from the ascendant or from another place. We say that you add to that which was between both places the degrees of the ascendant, and project from the ascendant or from the beginning of the sign from which you project. An example of this is the operation of the Part of Fortune: because you take whatever is between the Sun and the Moon in degrees: you add to these the degrees of the ascendant sign: and what is collected, you project it from 30 to 30 degrees, and you begin to project from the beginning of the ascendant sign. Where the number ends, there is the Part of Fortune: and at night, conversely, from the Moon to the Sun: and you add the degrees above the ascendant sign, and project this from 30 to 30 degrees. Begin to project from the beginning of the ascendant sign. Let us begin here, therefore, after the Part of Fortune, the parts of the 12 houses, and let us begin from the ascendant. The First House is the Part of Life, and it is taken by day from Jupiter to Saturn: and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Hyleg is taken from the degree of conjunction or prevention, which was before the nativity up to the degree of the Moon: and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Future Events, that is, the Part of the Sun, is taken by day from the Moon to the Sun: and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Love and Concord, that is, the Part of Venus: is taken by day from the Part of Fortune to the Part of Future Events: and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Stability and Trust of the duration of the native's ascendant, is like the Part of Concord and Love. The Part of Courage and Audacity, that is, the Part of Mars, is taken by day from Mars to the degree of the Part of Fortune and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Second House is the Part of Substance: and it is taken by day and night from the lord of the house of substance, to the degree and minute of the house of substance, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Poverty and Smallness of Ingenuity, that is, the Part of Mercury, is taken by day from the Part of Future Events to the Part of Fortune: and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Beatitude and Triumph and Victory, that is, the Part of Jupiter, is taken by day from the Part of Future Events to Jupiter, at night conversely, and is projected from the ascendant. The Third House is the Part of Brothers: and it is taken by day from Saturn to Jupiter: and at night conversely, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of the Benevolence of Brothers is taken by day from the Sun to Saturn and at night conversely, and is projected from the ascendant: but if Saturn is under the Sun's rays: it is taken by day from the Sun to Jupiter, and at night conversely, and is projected from the ascendant. The Fourth House is the Part of Fathers, it is taken by day from the Sun to Saturn: and at night conversely: and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of the Father's Death is taken by day from Saturn to Jupiter. And at night conversely: and it is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Years is taken by day from the lord of the house of the Sun to Saturn: and at night conversely: and it is projected from the ascendant. And if the Sun is in its own house, or in any of Saturn's houses: take by day from the Sun to Saturn: at night conversely, and project from the ascendant, and do not consider whether Saturn is visible or under the Sun's rays. The Part of Inheritances and Possessions is taken by day and night from Saturn to the Moon: and is projected from the ascendant. The Part of the Nobility of the Native, and of him about whom there is doubt, whether he is the son of that father to whom he is attributed, or of another: is taken by day from the degree of the Sun to the degree of its exaltation: and is projected from the ascendant. But if the Sun is in the degree of its exaltation by day, and the Moon at night in the degree of its exaltation, the part will be in the degree of the ascendant, and it will be the signification of the degree of the ascendant. The Part of the End of Things is taken by day and night from Saturn up to the lord of the house of conjunction, or prevention, and the degrees of the ascendant are added above it, and it is projected from the ascendant. The Fifth House is the Part of Children and is taken by day from Jupiter to Saturn, at night conversely, and is projected from the ascendant. The Part which signifies the time, in which a child should be born, and their number, whether male or female, and what the woman will bear, is taken by day and night from Mars to Jupiter and is projected from the ascendant. The Part of the Knowledge of a Male and Female Child is taken by day and night from the Moon to Jupiter, and is projected from the ascendant. The Part by which the native, about whom the question is asked, is known, whether male or female, is taken by day from the lord of the house of the Moon to the Moon: and at night conversely, and is projected from the ascendant. The Part signifying the child when Jupiter reaches it, that is, to the degree of the part signifying the child, is taken by day and night from Mars to Jupiter, and is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Love and Joy is taken by day and night from Venus to Saturn, and is projected from the ascendant. The Part of the Knowledge of the Existence of Children is taken by day and night from the Moon to Venus, and is projected from the ascendant. The Sixth House is the Part of Infirmity and Azemena, that is, inseparable weakness of some member: it is taken by day from Saturn to Mars, at night conversely, and is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Servants is taken by day from Mercury to the Moon, and at night conversely, and is projected from the ascendant. And Alendez said, it is taken by day from Mercury to the Part of Fortune: and at night conversely. And he said: it is necessary that we use both parts together. The Seventh House is the Part of the Betrothal of Men or Marriage: and it is taken by day and night from the Sun to Venus, and is projected from the ascendant. And this part is similar to the father of rumored commands. And the part of the betrothal of women or marriage according to Hermes is taken by day and night from Venus to Saturn, and is projected from the ascendant. And this part corresponds to the father of the cultivation of the earth. Likewise, the part of the betrothal of women according to Velius, is taken by day and night from the Sun to Mars, and is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Love and Pleasure is taken by day and night from Venus to the degree of the seventh, and is projected from the ascendant. The Part of Marriages is taken by day and night from Saturn to Venus, and is projected from the ascendant.
