Now, if it is further asked by what occasion a native thus born will obtain an abundance of fields and such fortune, he answers that this is to be inferred from the nature of the house in which the said significator, that is, the lord of the fourth house, is found. For if it is found present in the fourth house itself, which is that of fathers, such wealth is signified to accrue from inheritance or another occasion of fathers or ancient things; and if it is in the first house, which contains the native's body and soul, such goods are signified to come through the native's own ingenuity and industry; and if it is found in the tenth, which is that of kings and magistracy or actions, from which men seek a living in common society, the possession of fields is signified by occasion of the king and magistracy; finally, if it is found in the seventh house, which is that of wives and partnerships, it is to be inferred that the native will obtain estates from wives or negotiation, and such occasions as are congruent with the properties of the seventh house. In a similar way, judgment is to be made concerning all other significators.

[How to Find the Dominant Planet]
And when you wish to know the dominant planet of a thing, look at which of the planets has the greatest authority in the house of the thing, and the planet that signifies the nature of that thing, as we will say in the natures of the planets. Therefore, see which of the planets is stronger in the house of the thing, and in its part, from the strengths we have already mentioned, that is, from the number we have already mentioned, when we were discussing the strength and power of the planets. And whoever is stronger than all in the place of the thing, he will be its dominator. For example, if the question is about substance, and you wish to know who is its dominator, and the second house, which signifies substance, is, for example, the fifth degree of the sign of Aries: because the house is Mars', Mars has five strengths in this place; the exaltation is also of the Sun, and it has four strengths there. It is also the Sun's triplicity, and it has three strengths there, so the Sun has seven strengths there. And it is the term of Jupiter, and it has two strengths there. And it is also the face of Mars, and it has one strength there. Therefore, Mars has six strengths there, five from the house, one from the face, the Sun seven, and such a planet is called Almubta, that is, conquering. Therefore, the Sun takes the principality there, because it has seven strengths there, if it itself dominates there in the house of substance. Similarly, you will take Jupiter as a participant there in the place of the part of substance and the part of fortune, which is naturally the significator of substance, you will mix the testimonies of the 15 parts of the planets. And you will do this for all houses, and you will know their dominator. In the present chapter, it teaches the method of finding the dominant planets of things, that is, those having greater power than others in determining the outcome of any matter. Hence, some terms need to be explained. The lord and the host differ, as do the dominator or governor of the place, although the same planet may be found to be simultaneously dominator, lord, and also host. The lord of a sign is called in Greek κυριος, and sometimes also οἰκοδεσπότης, and is he who has his domicile in the same sign. For example, the lord of the sign of Aries is Mars, and the lady of Taurus is Venus, and the lord of Gemini is Mercury, etc. Therefore, if the sign of Aries falls into the rising angle, Mars will be the lord of the first house, Venus of the second, Mercury of the third, Jupiter of the fourth (etc., if Aries is rising, the sign of Taurus will fall into the second place, and Gemini into the third place, and Cancer into the fourth place according to the equal distribution of the sky approved by the Arabs). Firmicus calls the lord of the sign a host, and sometimes also a dominator. In this way, when the host of the interlunium is named, the lord of the place in which the interlunium occurred is understood. A planet is also more properly called the host of another planet and, as it were, the head of the household, when receiving it into its house, it undertakes its care and patronage by right of hospitality. For example, if Mercury is constituted in Taurus, we say that Mercury is the host of Venus, because Taurus is the house of Venus. Similarly, if the Sun is in Aries, then Mars, as the head of the household, receives the patronage of the Sun by right of hospitality in its own house. But the dominator or governor and disposer of the place is called in Arabic Almutes, and in Greek planeta επικρατήτωρ, because in the sign and degree of the sign it obtains epicratesin, that is, dominion and superior prerogatives among other planets. For example, in a diurnal nativity, the 6th part ascends. Venus has five powers there by reason of its domicile.

[Significations of Signs and Planets]
78. Argo is of both natures. Others are terrestrial, and of these, some are called anthropomorphic, which are known; others are irrational. Again, of the irrational, some are quadrupeds, which, as has been said, are divided into wild and domestic; others are reptiles, like serpents and similar creatures; others are venomous, like the Scorpion and serpents; others are mutilated; others are bound; others are otherwise named. CONCERNING THE SIGNIFICATIONS OF THE SIGNS. And each sign has its own signification in those things which it signifies from the creation of the members, the customs of men, and regions, and seeds, and trees, etc. Aries has from the human body the head and face; and from regions, Bebil and Serim, that is, Babylon and Arabia and Falastim and Palestine. Taurus has trees that are planted; and from the human body it has the neck and the throat node; and from regions, Ezetimet and Almech and Sandem and Araterad. Gemini is a generous sign, of good spirit, it has from the human body the shoulders and arms and hands; and from regions, Urgeti and Armenia, Nuthrabigem Etele nimstet, that is, Egypt and Bartha. Cancer has from trees those that are equal in length, and from the human body the chest, heart, stomach, ribs, spleen, and lung; and from regions, Lesser Armenia, and the Eastern region Buthabem and Massem Acin; it has participation in Barach and Atrabicen. Leo has tall trees, that is, long ones, cunning, astute, and much distress and sadness; and it has from the human body the stomach, heart, back, side; from regions, Artitri up to the end of the habitable region. Virgo has whatever is sown from seeds, and is generous, of good spirit. And it has from the human body the belly, namely the internal membrane, that is, the diaphragm and intestines; from regions, arguments and assent, that is, a certain region around Jerusalem, and Alforas, that is, the Euphrates; the island of Spain and Festix or Aseum. Libra has tall trees, and is generous, of good spirit. And it has from the human body the loins and lower belly, navel and groin and genitals, hips and flanks and buttocks; and from regions, the land of the Romans or Greeks, and those adjacent to them up to Africa; it also has Araffe or Azim up to the end of Ethiopia Barthan; it also has Carmen and Fegestem Thebes or Thebil Tabrasten Barah Ambarath. Scorpio has trees of equal length, generous, of good spirit; and it has from the human body the genitals, testicles, bladder, thighs; and from regions, Helehiget, the rural areas of the Arabs, its borders up to Allegem; and it has participation in Alchach. Sagittarius is ingenious, cunning, has from the human body the thighs; and from regions, Ethiopia and Maharahen and Achiut or Acenit or Achichit, which is India. Capricorn is of good life, irascible, cautious and cunning, much sadness; having from the human body the knees; and from regions, Ethiopia, Annaban, Alcon and Alcuth, Mahamen up to the two seas Aetahante Achiut, which is India. Aquarius has from the human body the legs up to the lower ankles, that is, the talus; and from regions, Azenes, that is, blackness, and Althupha and its parts, and the land of Elfices, and part of the land of Egypt, and the Western region of the land of Achiut. Pisces, cunning and cautious, mixed, multi-colored, having from the human body the feet; and from regions, Carabrarem and the Northern region of the land of Jurgem, and participation in the Romans up to Effen, it has the island and Egypt, and Alexandria and the Lycian Sea. All things enclosed beneath the lunar heaven are subject to the superior stars and celestial signs, and they agree with their powers, sympathize, and are moved around more manifestly than can be persuaded by verbose proof. For we note in this lower and sublunar world certain solar bodies, such as gold among metals, hyacinth among stones, heliotrope and lupine among plants, and among these the phoenix, etc., to which the Sun communicates something of its virtue more than to others: Certain lunar things, such as silver, crystal, palm, hyssop, geese, seals, and such things, which are especially nourished and preserved and affected more evidently by the Moon. In the same way, we must think and judge about Saturnine, Jovial, Venereal, Mercurial things, and finally about each celestial sign particularly agreeing. Therefore, just as the author above explained the places of the heaven and the stars, so in this chapter he intends to narrate the sympathy of these same places of the heaven with certain inferior things and those adjacent to the earth, that is, he wants to show which places of the heaven or dodecatemoria, to which regions, provinces, cities, trees, plants, parts of the human body, and such things especially agree and consent, and to which they attribute their power more than to others: all of which are so plainly narrated here that they require no explanation, except that a large part of the places are obscured by barbarous and unknown words. Therefore, I will add from Ptolemy which nations are placed under which signs, to whose brief catalog other places observed by younger authors may be added. These are to be observed because all the significations of the heaven appear more in those places which are subjected to the parts of the heaven decreeing something. Therefore, Aries has Britain, Brachate Gaul, Germany, the Bastarnae, Coele-Syria, Palestine, Idumea, Judea. Taurus has Parthia, central Persia, the Cyclades islands, the island of Cyprus, maritime places of Asia Minor. Gemini has Hyrcania, Armenia, Martiana, Cyrene, Marmarica, lower Egypt. Cancer has the Numidians, Carthaginians, Africans, Bithynia, Phrygia, Colchis. Leo has Italy, Togate Gaul, Sicily, Apulia, the Phoenicians, Chaldeans, Ochiniam. Virgo has Mesopotamia, Babylon, Assyria, Greece, Achaia, Crete. Libra has Bactra, Casperia, the Seres, Thebaid, Oasis, the Troglodytes. Scorpio has Metagonitida, the Moors, Gaetulians, Syria, Commagene, the Cappadocians. Sagittarius has the Tyrrhenians, Celts, Spain, happy Arabia. Capricorn has India, Arrianen, Gedrosia, Thrace, the Macedonians, Illyricum. Aquarius has the Sauromatae, Oxianen, Sogdianen, Arabia, Azania, central Ethiopia. Pisces has Phazaia, Nazamonitis, Garamantice, Lydia, Cilicia, Pamphylia. This is the sympathy of the twelve signs with the regions. Now we will also describe which parts of the human body the same signs hold, for this is very beneficial for judgments, especially when we want to find the place of health or defect. MEMBERS OF THE SIGNS. Head, neck, shoulders and arms, chest from the collarbone, belly from the breastbone to the lower parts, buttocks, genitals, bladder, hips, knees, legs and shins, feet, thighs. Refer here to the 20th statement of the Centiloquium, by which surgeons are warned not to cut veins or excise tumors when that sign of the heaven passes through to which the member to be cut is attributed. That is, do not strike a member with iron when the Moon holds the sign which rules that member. For the Moon, mistress of humors, is accustomed to fill that member which is subject to the sign through which she passes, more than others, with humors. Therefore, if it is opened with iron at that time, from the excessive influx of humors, putrid ulcers, nerve distensions, and such evils can follow, which both injure the member and make the cure dangerous. From this it is also clear why those wounds which are inflicted when the Moon illuminates the sign which rules the wounded part are healed with more difficulty and scarcely without harm to the member. And these two, namely the sympathy or consent of the parts of the earth and the members of the human body with the places of the heaven, are the main things which we are bound to observe in this chapter. CONCERNING THE SIGNIFICATION OF THE PLANETS IN THE SIGNS ACCORDING TO THE MEMBERS OF MAN. And if indeed the planets signify pain, they have in each sign a member proper to them. Therefore, let us treat of the pains of the planets in the signs. And first let us begin with Aries. Saturn in Aries has the chest, Jupiter the belly, Mars the head, Sun the thighs, Venus the feet, Mercury the legs, Moon the knees. In Taurus, Saturn the belly, Jupiter the back, Mars the neck, Sun the knees, Venus the head, Mercury the feet, Moon the legs. In Gemini, Saturn the belly, Jupiter the genitals.

[Fixed Stars in Virgo, Libra, Scorpio]
The length of the preceding star is 161 degrees, 10 minutes, with a northern latitude of 25 degrees. The length of the following star, in the shape of an ivy leaf, is 169 degrees, 10 minutes, 13 seconds, with a northern latitude of 25 degrees, 30 minutes, 12 seconds. The winged star of Virgo is depicted in the starry globes. The stars that are in the head of Virgo, and one at the extremity of the southern wing, imitate the nature of Mercury and somewhat of Mars. The other bright stars of the same wing, and those in the girdle, follow the nature of Mercury and a little of Venus. The other northern wing is marked by two famous stars. First, there is found in it a bright star of the third magnitude, which our people call Vindemiator, the Greeks call it Protrugetes, and in Chaldean, Almucedie Alaraph. Its longitude is 182 degrees, 50 minutes, 12 seconds. Its northern latitude is 15 degrees, 10 minutes, 13 seconds. Then another star of the same wing, of the first magnitude, which our people call Spica Virginis, the Greeks call it Stachys, and the Chaldeans Alzimon Alazel, has a longitude of 197 degrees, 20 minutes, 13 seconds, that is, it belongs to the 17th degree, 20 minutes, 18 seconds of the dodecatemory of Libra, with a southern latitude of 2 degrees. Its nature is that of Venus and somewhat of Mars. Finally, the stars that are at the ends of the feet and in the hem of the garment have the same effect as Mercury and Mars, and somewhat of Venus. The asterism of the Claws (Libra) is figured by 8 stars, of which two are of the second magnitude, four of the fourth, and two of the fifth. Their nature, described by Ptolemy, is in these words: "Those in the extremities of the claws are disposed similarly to Jupiter and Venus. Those in the middle are like Saturn, and gently like Mercury." In the forehead of Scorpio, there are three bright stars of the third magnitude, of the nature of Mars and somewhat of Saturn. The longitude of the northernmost is 237 degrees, that is, it is in the 27th degree of the dodecatemory of Scorpio, with a northern latitude of 1 degree, 20 minutes, 1 second. The longitude of the middle star is 236 degrees, 20 minutes, 18 seconds, with a southern latitude of 1 degree, 40 minutes, 12 seconds. The longitude of the southernmost is likewise 236 degrees, 20 minutes, 1 second, with a southern latitude of 5 degrees. Three bright stars in the body are of the nature of Mars and somewhat of Jupiter. But the preceding of these is of the third magnitude, and has a longitude of 241 degrees, 20 minutes, 1 second, with a southern latitude of 3 degrees, 45 minutes, 12 seconds. The middle one, bright and reddish, called Cor Scorpii by moderns, and Antares by the Greeks, is of the second magnitude, falling in the 3rd degree, 20 minutes of Sagittarius, with a southern latitude of 4 degrees. The following of the three is of the third magnitude, and has a longitude of 245 degrees, 10 minutes, 1 second, with a southern latitude of 5 degrees, 1 minute. Of those in the vertebrae, most are of the third magnitude, imitating the nature of Saturn and a little of Venus. The one in the first vertebra falls in the 9th degree of Sagittarius, with a southern latitude of 11 degrees. The one in the seventh vertebra and closest to the sting is found in the 19th degree, 40 minutes of Sagittarius, with a southern latitude of 15 degrees. Of the two in the sting, the preceding is of the fourth magnitude, and has a longitude of 257 degrees, with a southern latitude of 13 degrees. The following is of the third magnitude, and has a longitude of 258 degrees, with a southern latitude of 13 degrees. They have the same effect as Mars and Saturn. The so-called nebulous cluster, that is, the nebulous circle around Scorpio, is of the nature of Mars and the Moon, and belongs to the 21st degree, 50 minutes, 12 seconds of Sagittarius, with a southern latitude of 13 degrees. The arrow of Sagittarius is Martian and Lunar. Around the bow and the part of the nerve held by the hand, are stars of Jupiter and Mars. In the face, the nebulous cluster, that is, the double nebula, has the same effect as Mars and the Moon, and belongs to the 3rd degree, 40 minutes, 12 seconds of Capricorn, with a northern latitude of 0 degrees, 45 minutes, 1 second. Those in the band and back follow the nature of Jupiter and a little of Venus. The feet are of Jupiter and Mars. The Terebellum, that is, the four-sided old woman, is like Jupiter, and gently like Mercury. The horns of Capricorn are of the nature of Saturn and a little of Venus. The stars of the mouth are Saturnian, and at the same time partake somewhat of the nature of Mercury. The feet and belly are Martian and a little of Venus. Finally, the tail follows the nature of Saturn and Jupiter. The stars in the shoulders of Aquarius, likewise in the garment and left hand, refer to the nature of Saturn and Mercury. The thighs imitate more Saturn than Jupiter. Those in the flowing water are Saturnian and partly Jovian. The last asterism of the zodiac is formed by two Fish, one southern, the other northern, which are connected by a thread, which some call a line, others a small line, others a ligament. The stars in the head of the southern Fish are of the nature of Jupiter and somewhat of Mercury. Those in the body are Jovian and Mercurial. In the tail and southern thread, they refer to Saturn and a little of Mars. Those in the body and spine of the northern Fish are Martian and somewhat also Venerean. Those in the northern thread imitate the nature of Saturn and Jupiter. Finally, the bright star in the knot has the nature of Saturn and somewhat of Mercury. The asterisms of the remaining signs outside the zodiac follow. And first, the 21st northern figure. The Little Bear or Cynosura, which the Phoenicians observe at sea, because it is closer to the pole and moves less. The star at the end of its tail, because it is closest to the axis, they call the pole: yet it is almost four parts distant from the true vertex of the world. The bright stars of this bear have the quality of Saturn, and somewhat of Venus. The Great Bear or Helice, which the Greeks, because it has more prominent stars, observe at sea. For this reason, in Homer, the Achaeans are called 'helico-eyed'. The stars of this bear resemble Jupiter, and under its tail, the Coma Berenices has the temperament of Jupiter and Venus. Therefore, these stars are as if very moist hair, and portend suffocations from waters or phlegm. Both bears are interwoven with seven principal stars, which they call the Septentriones. The common people and poets call them wagons from the shape of horses and wheels. Homer in Iliad 6: 'the bear, which they also call by the name of wagon'. The bright stars of Draco, which winds around the two bears like a river with a sinuous bend, are of the nature of Saturn, Mars, and Jupiter. Cepheus, the husband of Cassiopeia, which constellation the Babylonians called Ficares, and some among us called 'inflamed' and 'lord of flame', contains stars of Jupiter and Saturn. Bootes, that is, the herdsman, is a constellation that follows Helice or the Great Bear, also called Arctophylax and guardian of the Erimanthian bear. Ovid in Fasti 3: 'Whether it is Arctophylax, or that lazy Bootes.' The stars of the Bear set with difficulty, the Southern stars rise with difficulty, therefore Bootes is often called slow and lazy by the poets because of his long stay. Thus Homer in the Odyssey called him 'the setting Bootes'. Lucan in Pharsalia book 3 called him swift, but that must be referred to the position of the southern parts of the earth, where Bootes does not remain in the upper hemisphere for as long as in northern places: his words are these: 'Then Roman fury moved the distant Oretas and German leaders, whose sky, deflected to the south, does not see the entire bear submerged, yet it shines, and swift Bootes is there for a short night.' The stars of Bootes have the qualities of Saturn and Mercury, except that the reddish and shining star of the first magnitude located between Bootes' feet, which the Chaldeans call Azemer Aramer, and our people Arcturus, that is, the tail of the bear, retains the qualities of Mars and Jupiter. It falls in the 18th degree, 40 minutes of Libra, with a northern latitude of 31 degrees. The Northern Crown of Ariadne, which they say Bacchus placed among the stars, whence it is also called Gnosia: the Chaldeans call it Malfelcare. It contains stars that act like Venus, Mercury, and Jupiter. One, brighter than the others, is called by some Hercules, by others Theseus, by others Thamyris: it is the one.

[Fixed Stars and Planetary Natures]
208. The Hare, with a southern latitude of 53 parts. The rest are Saturnine. IV. Lepus. V. Canis. VI. Procyon. VII. Argo. Canopus. VIII. Hydra. IX. Crater. X. Corvus. XI. Centaurus. XII. Boötes. XIII. Thuribulum. XIV. Corona Australis. XV. Piscis Austrinus. The Hare, under the feet of Orion, has Mercurial stars. Canis Major has all Venusian stars, except for the immense and largest star that shines in its mouth, and Canicula, also accustomed to be called Sirius, which is Jovial and also has a little of Mars. Its longitude is 98 parts, with a southern latitude of 39 parts. This star, rising in the morning, is seen even at midday in a mirror, with water placed against the Sun, and wonderfully increases the Sun's heat. Procyon, the Lesser Dog or Antecanis, is so called because it rises before Sirius. Its bright star is of the first magnitude, of the nature of Mercury and also has a little of Mars, and has a longitude of 109 parts with a southern latitude of 164 parts. The bright stars of Argo, which they also call Jason's ship and Noah's ark, are of the nature of Jupiter and Mars. Furthermore, the star of the first magnitude at the top of Argo's rudder is called Canopus, but it does not rise for us, for it has a southern latitude of 75 parts. The bright stars of Hydra or the Serpent are Saturnine and partly Venusian. Some of the more recent authors have called this constellation magnanimous. Crater, the cup or urn, has Venusian stars and partly Mercurial. Corvus has Martian and Saturnine stars. Centaurus, Chiron, who is also called the beast-bearer. The stars located in the human part of the body have the efficacy of Jupiter and Venus. The splendid stars in the equine part are of the nature of Jupiter and Venus. The beast, or wolf, or monster that the Centaur carries, also named Leopard by some, has bright stars, partaking of the nature of Jupiter and a little of Mars. The Thuribulum, that is, the altar or censer, has Venusian stars, and also a little of Saturnine. The bright stars in the Southern Crown imitate the quality of Jupiter and Venus. This constellation is also called the Raven and Ixion's Wheel. Piscis Austrinus, the marine or great fish, which is said to have been translated to the heavens because it once received Venus in her flight from Typhon, has in its mouth a bright star of the first magnitude, of the nature of Jupiter and Mercury, and its longitude is 327 parts, with a southern latitude of 23 parts. So much for the fixed stars: now the forces of the planets are to be revealed. But first, the hesitation that arises here must be recited and examined. For it may reasonably be doubted whether stars that are said to have mixed qualities of malefics and benefics retain both simultaneously, even if contrary, or whether, one quality being abolished, they follow the other. For example, Basiliscus is said to have the forces of Jupiter and Mars. If, therefore, the Heart of Leo ascends in a nativity, it may be doubted whether it makes people sometimes just, as Jupiter usually does, sometimes unjust, as Mars, or whether it makes them simultaneously just and unjust, and finally, whether it makes them intermediate between just and unjust? The answer does not seem absurd to me if we say that these constellations reflect the qualities of that planet with which they are conjoined, that is, joined by body or aspect. In this matter, he who is found present in the asterism, or who sees it more closely, will always be preferred. But if neither of the cognate planets, but some third foreign planet, is joined to the constellation, the constellation seems to defend the nature of that planet to which it is friendly by aspect, and with which it agrees in nature. So if neither Jupiter nor Venus, but Mars, who abounds in Martian quality because of heat, sees Basiliscus, it will not unreasonably seem to retain only the qualities of Mars, the Jovial nature being suppressed. But Cardano has another opinion, who thinks that the mixed natures of the planets should be retained in the constellations, because Ptolemy also used to mix the forces of the planets, so that similar things are increased by similar things, but from contrary qualities, either both are removed, if they are equal, or the stronger is weakened by the weaker, if qualities of unequal forces are compared. According to this method, the star in the tail of Ursa Major, of the nature of Saturn and Venus, will be very humid, because both of these planets are very humid: but moderate in heat, warmer than the Moon and colder than Venus. In the same way, stars of the nature of Mars and Saturn will be very dry, for both planets are dry. But in heat, as it were, tempered, but they will incline to cold, because the cold of Mars is greater than its heat. They will be angry because of Mars, and tenacious in anger because of Saturn, and fierce and audacious in that anger, and finally, timid because of the Sun when it is fervent. Finally, we must also observe that fixed stars, some of which have receded to the south, and some further to the north from the Ecliptic, do not rise or set in every climate in the same way with the Sun or another part of the Ecliptic. For example, a curved line extended from the vernal intersection to both poles of the world, although in a right sphere, in which both poles touch the horizon, it ascends entirely in one moment, yet for us northerners, it does not all rise at once, but where the northern part has risen, the southern will still lie hidden depressed. Therefore, when the Sun or another star rises in the vernal intersection, that is, in the first part, a fixed star placed in the same line to the south will not rise with it, but some degrees later. On the contrary, a star situated to the north, having risen earlier, will precede the Sun, and will neither rise nor set simultaneously with the Sun. Therefore, lest the positions of the stars deceive you, you must diligently provide for them through a solid sphere, or through the tables of Regiomontanus. In the books of Ephemerides also, tables are arranged for some elevations of the pole for this purpose, which show which more unworthy stars rise, set, and culminate with which parts of the Ecliptic. The text follows concerning the power, authority, and signification of the seven wandering stars. 1. Saturn is masculine, malefic, diurnal. 2. And it is the significator of fathers, if the child's nativity is at night. 3. And it signifies extreme old age if it is occidental: but the beginning of old age if it is oriental. And it signifies the gravity of cold and dryness. 4. And it signifies, that is, in the complexion of bodies, melancholic, its increase and distillation. And perhaps it will sometimes be a cold, humid, ponderous, and fetid complexion, and much eating and true love. 5. And it signifies depth of counsel, and multitude of silence. 6. And from the arts, ancient precious things. Indeed, the two members which you see enclosed in parentheses, if they are joined by translation, the reading will be more orderly and arranged: since in both the quality of the art is noted. Hence it will also follow that the paragraph: And it signifies depth of counsel, etc., will be correctly continued with the paragraph: And if he is fortunate, there will be true love, etc. For in both, the quality of the soul is discussed. If he is fortunate, he signifies the cultivation of fields, the devastation of lands and rivers. On the contrary, however, vile and laborious things, such as rubbings in baths, fullers, and sailors, if he is malefic. And if he is fortunate, he will be spacious and patient in true love, if he is malefic, he will be indiscreet, stable, sad and mournful, prone to evil suspicion, very suspicious, and moving men to whispers. (In addition, if he is the sole significator without the complexion of any other planet, he signifies works of leather or his own. But if Jupiter is conjoined with him, he signifies the work of parchment, in which divine books are written. And if Mars is conjoined with him, he signifies the soles of shoes and their preparations. And if the Sun is conjoined with him, he signifies the work of shoemakers' leathers. And if Venus is conjoined with him, he signifies the work of leathers from which drums and other instruments that we use in games are made. And if Mercury is conjoined with him, he signifies the work of leathers in which testaments and numbers of stipends are written. And if the Moon is conjoined with him, he signifies the preparation of leathers of wild animals and mountain animals, and similar things.) 7. And if he is fortunate, he signifies from the substance ancient durable inheritances, and cultivated land, Almauerith, that is, the substances of the dead. And if he is

[Saturn's Malefic Influences]
If it is malefic, it signifies dirty and bad-tasting waters, old and changeable. And from infirmities, phlegmatic and melancholic diseases, viscous, congealed, and acute, such as leprosy, morphea, gout, cancers, and other similar things. And it signifies distant peregrinations, prisons, chains, labor, slowness, and affliction. And it signifies among sects that which confesses unity, if it is fortunate; and if it is malefic, it signifies the faith of unity, yet with much hesitation or doubt. And Messahala, whom God willed to be exalted, who was an Astrologer clear in the science of judgments, whence he was so called, said that it signifies the Jewish faith, because it is from the most ancient, and because all confess it, and it confesses no other. Just as Saturn, to whom all are joined, and he to none. It also signifies black garments. And some others said that Saturn signifies the inner parts of the ear, the spleen, and the stomach. And it has blackness from colors; and from tastes, astringent and sour; from days, Saturday; finally, from nights, that which precedes Wednesday. And the quantity of its orb is nine degrees. And the years of its fridaria are XI, the greatest are CCCCLXVI, the major LVII, the medium XLIII, and the minor XXX. Its strength in the regions of the circle is in the right of the north. And Messahala said that it signifies among human figures, a man between black and yellow, who when he walks casts his eyes to the ground, heavy, joining his feet in his gait, thin, stooped, having small eyes, and dry skin, veiny, having a sparse beard on his jaws, thick lips, cunning, ingenious, a seducer, a killer. And Dorotheus said: This signifies a man with a very hairy body, with joined eyebrows. And it has from regions Ascine and India, all the land of black people. And from parts, having a part of strength and stability. And it signifies lands or earthly things and inheritances: and those who are in charge of works, and audacity and labor, talents and causes of death: and it has from the parts of the world Achiud and Alchiut, the confines of the guilty, and the lands of black people and their mountains.

[Jupiter's Benefic Influences]
Jupiter, fortunate, masculine, diurnal: it is a significator of substance, and it operates heat and temperate humidity, airy, sanguine, and from ages it signifies youth up to the perfection of age: and from crafts that pertain to the law: such as judging just judgments, and bringing peace among men, and striving for good things. And of substance it signifies abundance, and from businesses those that are done without deception, and it signifies the soul and life, joy and truth, and religion and patience, and every beautiful and precious precept, and the abundance of Venus: and from infirmities that arise from blood by an increase of quantity, which is not superfluous beyond nature, nor from burnt and changeable blood: it is the planet of wisdom and intellect and use. If Saturn is conjoined with it, it signifies necromancy and incantations and exorcisms, etc. And if Mars is conjoined with it, it signifies the science of medicine. And if the Sun is conjoined with it, it signifies the science of sects, and prudence in contentions and disputes. And if Venus is conjoined with it, it signifies the composition of sounds and other delightful things. And if Mercury is conjoined with it, it signifies the science of Arithmetic and writing: also Astronomy and Philosophy and Geometry. If the Moon is conjoined with it, it signifies the science of the dispositions of waters and their measure, as well as of lands. And from the quality of the soul it signifies generosity and modesty and justice, and from sects plurality and simulation. Some, however, said that it signifies the liver and stomach, and the left ear and arms and belly: also the lower parts of the chest and intestines: and from colors it has ash color and green, and similar to these: and from tastes it has sweet: and the quantity of its orb is IX degrees. And from days it has Thursday, and from nights the night of Monday: and the years of its fridaria, that is, of its dominion, are XII. And the greatest years are CCCCXXVIII, the major LXXIX, the medium XLV and a half: and the minor XII. And its strength from the regions of the circle is in the west. And Messahala said that among human images it signifies a white man, having redness in his face: having eyes not entirely black, uneven and short ships, bald: having blackness in some teeth, of beautiful stature, good spirit, good manners, beautiful body. And Dorotheus said that it signifies a man having large eyes: and a wide pupil, a curly beard. And it has from regions Alchirath and Babylon and Asen and Persia, and Alaormes and Arcadia. And from parts, having a part of the habit of progress, and it signifies faith and desire for good things: and from works, health, security and participation.

[Mars's Malefic Influences]
Mars, masculine, nocturnal, malefic, operates heat and dryness. And it is a significator of brothers and peregrinations: and it has from ages youth up to the end of youth: and its nature is choleric with a bitter taste. And from crafts it has every fiery craft, and that which is done by iron and fire, such as the striking of swords with hammers. And when Saturn is conjoined with it, it signifies the striking of iron: If Jupiter, it signifies the striking of bronze: If the Sun, it signifies the striking of gold coins: If Venus, it signifies the craft of ornaments: If Mercury, the striking of needles: If the Moon, it signifies the striking of spears and books. It also signifies, when it alone takes on the signification, the work of medicine: If no planet is conjoined with it, it signifies diminution, and wounding, and opening, and similar things. And if Saturn is conjoined with it, it signifies the work of medicine and wounds: and if Jupiter, it signifies the work of natures: and if the Sun, it signifies the care of the eyes: if Venus, it signifies the work of ornament, such as cutting hair and beards, and cutting nails: and if Mercury, it signifies the cutting of veins: if the Moon, it signifies the eradication of teeth and the cleaning of ears. And by itself it signifies the injuries of the miserable, the effusion of blood, and oppressions by force, and the cutting off of roads and anger, and the leading of an army, and haste and shamelessness, and peregrination outside the homeland, and the foulness of coitus, and the falling of children, that is, abortions: and middle brothers and sisters, the knowledge and discretion of the care of beasts. And from infirmities, hot and sanguine fevers, and sanguine pustules, alabraha, which is redness of the body with roughness and foulness and consumption of flesh with putrefaction: and headache of half the head, and sacred fire and terror, and horrible thoughts, which disturb men and move and impede and render them empty, and whatever is with inflammation of heat. And from the quality of the soul, namely commotion of the soul and disturbance, if Saturn aspects it, it signifies hatred and greatest envy: and from sects that in which there is war: and unity and swiftness of change from faith, and multitude of hesitation, and change from testament to testament: yet all these will be under unity. Some said that it has from the members the gall, kidneys, and veins, and the flow of semen and the back: and it has from colors redness, and from tastes bitter: and the quantity of its orb is VIII degrees. And from days it has Tuesday, and from nights the night of Saturday: and the years of its fridaria are seven, and its greatest years are CCLXIIII, the major are LXVI, the medium XL and a half: and the minor XV. And its strength in the regions of the circle is in the south. And Messahala said that among human images it signifies a red man, having reddish hair, and a slightly round face dishonoring men, having yellow eyes, of horrible aspect, audacious, sometimes having a mark or spot on his foot. And Dorotheus said that it signifies one having a sharp.

[Mercury's Significations]
of travelers away from home. And it signifies spiritual infirmities of the soul, that is, horrible thoughts, and restlessness of mind, that is, doubts, and other similar things. It also signifies the quality of the mind, and other similar things according to its complexion and conjunction: when it is fortunate, there will be good things according to the kind of fortune that makes it fortunate, and according to the place in which Mercury is fortunate: and when it is evil, there will be iniquities according to the evil that makes it evil, and according to the place in which it was made evil. And it signifies from the sects the worship of unity, and similar things, secretly with hypocrisy and simulation. And some have said that it signifies the thighs, the navel, the comb, the legs, the nerves, and the veins. And from colors it has every mixed and varied color, and alexmenium, which is the color of the wild lily flower: and from tastes, sour. And the quantity of its orb is 7 degrees, and it has from the days the day of Mercury, and from the nights the night of Sunday. Its Fridaria years are 13. Its greater years are 76, its maximum 460, its medium 48, its minor 20. Its strength in the regions of the circle is in the north. And some have said that Mercury from the middle of its retrogradation until the second station signifies childhood: and from the second station until the conjunction of the Sun, youth: and from the conjunction of the Sun until the first station, middle age: and from its first station until the middle of retrogradation, it signifies old age and contrariety: and in its conjunction by direction until the first station, it signifies affection, friendship, imitation of love: and from its second station going to conjunction, it signifies the inquiry of affection and concord: and from its first station going again to retrogradation, it signifies the inquiry of contrariety and dissimulation, slowness, little shame, and occupation and stupor in things: and in the middle of retrogradation, it signifies moderate speed because of the weakness of the intellect: at the second station it signifies stupor, occupation, slowness of intellect, egress: to these, speed, openness of intellects: its conjunction with the Sun by direction, signifies the speed and passion of intellects and their breadth or augmentation. Similarly, it happens to Venus in these places and to the higher planets. And Messahala said: Mercury signifies from the figures of men, a man not very white nor black in color, having a high, long forehead, a long face, a sparse beard on the cheeks, and beautiful eyes, not entirely black, also having long fingers. And from the parts it has the part of negotiation, and it signifies fear and infestation, war and enmities and seductions and contrarieties: it also signifies perfect mastery and subtlety in work and inquiry, and in other things that are done in exact men and contentions. And from the lands it has Adelech, Alcuiden and especially in the south, the lands of the Indians. The Moon is fortunate, feminine, nocturnal, operating with coldness and humidity. And it is the significator of mothers, if the nativity is nocturnal: there is in it a temperate phlegm. And it signifies the infantile age, the beginning of growth. And from its works it has embassies, mandates, works of waters and lands according to the quantity of fortune or misfortune or evil: if it is good, it signifies good, and vice versa. It also signifies principality, if it presides or is dominant over some things pertaining to the king, if it is fortunate from the Sun in a good aspect and in a good place. And from substance it signifies silver, and cultivated land, if it has authority in the fourth. And from faith, religion. And from infirmities, epilepsy, paralysis, falling sickness, facial distortion, dislocation of limbs, commotion, and whatever is similar in coldness and humidity. And the quality of the mind according to its conjunction with the planets. If fortune embraces it, and fortune itself is Venus, it signifies courtesy and kindness, and sweetness of mind, honesty of manners, and swiftness of movement, and divine service: if it is Jupiter, it signifies honesty, caution, and society and kindness and beauty of life: and if it is embraced by evils, if it is Mars, it signifies the study of whispering among men, use in such things: if Saturn, hatred, simulation and envy: if it is the Sun from a praiseworthy aspect, it signifies a royal disposition: if it is Mercury, it signifies rhetoric, that is, eloquence and goodness of tongue and writing. And some have said that it signifies thought, novelty of mind and weakness of sense, and heaviness of tongue, and honest women, nourishment of children, mothers and aunts, preparation of foods. And others have said that it signifies the brain properly and the lung. And from colors it has saffron, and from tastes, salty. And the quantity of its orb is 12 degrees. And it signifies in men the left eye, and in women the right. And from the days it has the day of the Moon, and from the nights the night of Venus. And its Fridaria years are nine: its greater years are 108, its maximum 520, its medium 66 and a half, and according to some 39 and a half: its minor years are 25. And its strength from the regions of the circle is in the right of the west. And Messahala said that it signifies from the figures of men a white man, tinged with redness, with joined eyebrows, benevolent, having eyes not entirely black, a round face, a beautiful stature: and in his face a sign. And from the lands it has Arcoch and Timana and Aldeilam. And some have said that it signifies childhood from the beginning of the month until 7 days, and from 7 days until 14 days youth: and it signifies the age of perfection, that is, middle age, until 21 days and nights: old age until the conjunction, that is, until the end of the month, when it conjoins the sun. And when it is under the Sun's rays, it signifies secrets and hidden things: similarly every planet. And at the beginning of the month when it grows, it signifies everything that is to be done: and in its fullness what is to be destroyed, because it decreases: and at the beginning of the month it and the Sun signify accusers: and at the end of the month the accused: and it signifies at the beginning of the month gain and continence, at the end of the month stipends and dispersions. And it signifies in opposition contrariety, and at the beginning of the change to opposition, that is, when there are 15 degrees between it and the opposition, it signifies the beginning of contrariety and its cause: and when it is separated from the opposition, it signifies the causes of exception from contrariety: and in its exit from under the Sun's rays, it signifies exit from concealment, and similar things: and in its entrance under the rays, it signifies adaptation to concealment: and the hour of division from the Sun, it signifies adaptation of its exit from concealment: and the hour of its exit from under the rays, it signifies appearance and arrival from absence: and while it is in the fourth aspect of the Sun, it signifies diminution of a thing or descent from high to low. Similarly in the second fourth aspect, but in the first fourth aspect it signifies the appearance of things, and gain and increase of continence: and in the second fourth aspect of the Sun, it signifies the opposite of these.

[Planetary Qualities and Ages]
And some have said that the Moon, from conjunction up to the first half of its light, will have a humid nature; from the middle of its light up to its fullness, its nature will be hot; and from its fullness up to the second half of its light, its nature will be dry; and from the second half of its light up to conjunction, its nature will be cold. The other planets, from their rising until their first station, will be of a humid nature and signify childhood; from their first station until opposition to the Sun, their nature will be hot and signify youth; and from this point until their second station, their nature will be dry and signify perfect age; and from their second station until their first occultation, their nature will be cold and signify cold old age. And some have said that the Sun signifies the spirit, that is, the vital soul; the Moon, thought and sensation; Saturn, sorrow and sadness, vileness and evil; Jupiter, wisdom and reason; Mars, anger, fury, and swiftness; Venus, play and joy; Mercury, rationality or dialectical discipline. And because we have spoken in this chapter about the signification of the planets when they embrace another planet, similarly, it must also be considered in other things that the planets signify. The power of the wandering stars is known in four principal ways. First, when their inherent force and primary quality are explored. Second, when the places of the heavens, which they occupy by reason of longitude and latitude, are considered. Third, when we compare them either to their epicycles and deferents, or to the luminaries and to each other. Finally, when they are referred to the position of a particular region. For when they appear in the tenth house in one region, it is possible that they are seen by others in the eleventh, or twelfth, first, second, or another house. Concerning the second and fourth modes, that is, concerning the strength of the planets in the dodecatemoria, and concerning their signification in the cusps, he spoke in part in the first difference; but he pursues the first mode in this second difference, and the third in the third difference. However, we will conveniently divide the first mode into three parts, namely, into sex, quality, and nature. For once these three are rightly understood, the greatest and most necessary part of this second difference will become clear. The Sex of the Planets. In every genus, males are more efficacious than females; therefore, they call the more powerful planets masculine. However, the sex of the planets, as Ptolemy taught, is distinguished in three ways. First, by nature: by which reasoning, those in whom humidity does not overcome heat, as in Saturn and Jupiter, are masculine; while those in whom heat is overcome by humidity, as in Venus and the Moon, are called feminine. But Mercury, as elsewhere, is considered to be of an ambivalent nature here, as it produces equal dryness and humidity. Second, by comparison to the Sun. For oriental planets are called masculine, occidental feminine: that is, a planet that is above the earth when the Sun is rising is masculine; one that is below the earth is feminine. Third, by comparison to the world. For those dwelling in the first or third quadrant are masculine; in the second and fourth, they become feminine. Ptolemy's words concerning masculine and feminine stars are these: "It is fitting that they have given the Moon and Venus as feminine stars, because they have more humidity in their essence; and Saturn, Jupiter, and Mars as masculine. Mercury is common to both sexes, as it is equally productive of dry and humid essence. They say that stars are made masculine and feminine by their positions relative to the Sun; for those that are oriental and preceding are made masculine, while those that are occidental and following are made feminine. And also by their positions relative to the horizon. For those in the positions from the east to the midheaven, and from the west to the opposite midheaven, are made masculine as oriental; while those in the other two quadrants are made feminine as occidental." The Quality of the Planets. Here we understand quality as the nature of the planet congruent with the time, and we call a planet that rejoices by day diurnal, and one that rejoices by night nocturnal. In this matter, it is especially to be observed, as Ptolemy teaches, that the temperaments of the planets are attributed to the time abounding in the same qualities: so that Jupiter and the Sun, because of their temperate mixture, in which heat dominates humidity, are accommodated to diurnal light; thus, the Moon and Venus are attributed to night for no other reason than that they consist of a temperament in which, as in the mixture of night, humidity easily overcomes heat. From the intemperate, however, day is accommodated to Saturn to temper his cold, and night to Mars to temper his dryness; since in a bad mixture, it is always necessary to correct worse qualities with their opposites. Hence it follows that neither Saturn will be too cold, nor Mars excessively dry, if the former happens to rule by day, and the latter by night. Therefore, neither will harm as much as usual. From these, it is clear that there are three diurnal planets, namely, the diurnal luminary with Jupiter and Saturn, both of which are most powerful, and for this reason, one is called a malefic, the other a great benefic. And there are found as many nocturnal planets, namely, the nocturnal luminary with Mars and Venus, of which the former is called a malefic, the latter a lesser benefic. But Mercury, since it accommodates itself to both qualities, is sometimes diurnal, especially in its morning rising, and sometimes nocturnal, and especially in the evening, for then it is colder and less hot. According to this reasoning, therefore, the planets are best disposed: the diurnal ones, if they are above the earth and oriental by day; the nocturnal ones, if they are likewise above the earth and oriental by night. For universally, just as the Sun and Moon, so any other of the stars is more efficacious above the earth than below it, which the Arabs denied, who argued that nocturnal planets are more efficacious below the earth by day, and diurnal planets above the earth by night. But it will perhaps seem absurd to someone also that it is said that the power of diurnal planets is more excited above the earth by day, when it is acknowledged that all stars become more languid in diurnal light, when their power is dissipated and diffused by the presence of the Sun's rays? To this hesitation, Cardan responds, according to Ptolemy's opinion, that all these things refer not so much to the presence of the Sun, but rather to the nature of the time, so that diurnal planets are understood to be best tempered by themselves and by this condition of time during the day, whether they are found above or below the earth, whether they are morning or evening stars. But if they have the Sun present in the meantime, nothing absurd will be admitted if we believe that the Sun's presence does not promote but rather disturbs the constitution and strength of the stars. For example, the star of Jupiter is best tempered by diurnal light. But its efficacy will be even greater, and beyond that condition, if it is carried above the earth, especially if it is oriental and free from the Sun's rays. And conversely, its condition will be disturbed if it lies hidden below the earth, and much more so if it is occidental and enveloped in the Sun's rays. In the same way, the condition of the others is to be considered as being helped or diminished. Finally, it is worthy of observation that planets agreeing in quality or condition of time are called of the same sect, and this especially if they also agree in sex. It remains for us to transcribe Ptolemy's words concerning diurnal and nocturnal: "Similarly," he says, "since of the times, these two most manifest intervals occur, that of day, being more masculine because of the heat and activity in it, and that of night, being more feminine because of the humidity and rest in it: they have accordingly given the Moon and Venus as nocturnal stars, and the Sun and Jupiter as diurnal. Mercury is common to these. And if it is a morning star, it is diurnal; if an evening star, it is nocturnal. We have added, however, that the principle of the two sects is not of a corrupting essence. For it is not according to the same natural causes, but according to the opposite ones. For to those of a good temperament, similar things mixed with it produce greater benefit. But to the corrupting ones, unsuitable things mixed with them greatly weaken and disturb the temperament."

[Planetary Natures and Qualities]
This means: Since there are two evident distinctions of times, namely day and night, and day is more congruent with masculine nature, both because there is greater heat during the day and because of the opportunity for action; and night is more congruent with feminine nature, because of humidity and suitability for rest: Therefore, they appropriately handed down that the nocturnal stars are Mars and Saturn, and the diurnal stars are Jupiter and the Sun. Mercury is of both conditions, diurnal when eastern, and nocturnal when western. Finally, they attributed one of the malefics to each condition, following not the similarity of quality, but diversity. For when similar qualities are familiarly coupled with stars of good temperament, they increase their goodness. But dissimilar qualities mixed with destructive ones restrain the vehemence of their malice. Hence, they joined Saturn, who is cold, to diurnal heat, and Mars, who is dry, to nocturnal humidity. In this way, each, having attained a symmetry of qualities from a contrary constitution, achieves a temperate condition. CONCERNING THE NATURE OF THE PLANETS. In explaining the nature of the planets, two things are especially to be observed. First, the primary qualities, that is, which planets are hot, cold, humid, or dry. Second, how, from the measure of the primary qualities, proceeding from the magnitude of heat, the genera of consonant effects are distributed to individual planets. Pliny and Ptolemy are authorities that the star of Saturn is of a cold and rigid nature: hence it has the power of cooling and slightly drying, and as the author says, it signifies the gravity of cold and dryness, which is sufficiently confirmed by experience, that when placed in a hot sign it diminishes heat, and in a cold sign it increases frost, condenses the air, and fills it with pestilential clouds. Ptolemy's words about its nature are these: 'The quality in the star of Saturn is cooling and somewhat drying. Because it is, as it seems, very far both from the heat of the Sun and from the moist vapors of the earth.' Since stars shine with a double light, namely their own inherent substance, and then the light of the Sun, which is reflected from a polished and solid astral body, both of which are most evident from the illuminations and defects of the Moon: Therefore, Ptolemy's reasons are clear, why he said Saturn cools and somewhat dries. For since Saturn's own substance is more impure and less subtle, and because of its great distance from the Sun it is less illuminated than others by that very subtle, clear, and penetrating light, it can heat very little, and by heating little, it cools. For we prove here the opinion of Cardano, who in his books on subtle matters, and in his commentaries on Ptolemy, written against common astrologers and the entire crowd of Peripatetics, declared that all celestial bodies are hot not only potentially, as Aristotle wished, but also actually. But Saturn's heat, because it is weaker, is suitable only for metals, herbs, trees, and certain animals, such as scorpions. He says that it severely harms human limbs, not indeed by itself or simply, but because its heat is less than what is suitable for the more intense heat that human temperament desires. For just as if you mix lukewarm water with hot, you will produce water less hot than the original hot water: so the small heat of Saturn joined to the more abundant heat of man, teaches to cool. In the same way, we understand that Saturn, and especially when coupled with the Moon in winter, because its heat is weaker than the Moon's heat, becomes a cause of cold. Finally, if it ever happens that Saturn alone dominates without other stars, it will nevertheless increase cold. For air by its nature is not, as is supposed, hot, but very cold, and whatever heat it acquires, it borrows from the stars. For there are only two qualities, namely celestial heat and elemental humidity. Coldness, however, is nothing other than the absence of celestial heat from the elements, just as dryness is the privation of humidity. Therefore, since Saturn heats less than any other star, it is always a cause of cold, whenever it becomes powerful and mixes itself with the actions of others that produce heat. For just as wine diluted with an abundance of watery wine is reduced to a worse form, that is, closer to watery than to airy: so the exuberant force of Saturn, mixed with the less effective forces of others, will produce effects in the air most congruent with its nature, that is, it will heat the air little, which, since by its nature it is rigid with eternal frost and deprived of all heat, therefore, being heated little, will still retain immense cold. From these, the reason is clear why Ptolemy said Saturn's quality is cooling. In this way, we also say that the other stars, both wandering and fixed in the sky, have their heat, but are named hot, cold, or endowed with other qualities because of their effects on man. It remains to show the reason why he said Saturn's quality is somewhat dry. Dry and humid arise from one quality, that is, from celestial heat, but differing both in matter and in quantity. For just as in our fire we note that its subtle spirits penetrating the vessels induce heat into the vapors, but its thick soot, not penetrating but merely adhering to the vessels, heats them: so in the same way, the difference of celestial heat, whether great, small, subtle, or thick, must be considered. If it is very great and subtle, it will most easily penetrate the humid air of the region, and by quickly penetrating the air, it will not dry it, but rather resolve it into watery vapors and moisten it. And conversely, if the heat is thick, it penetrates the air with difficulty, especially if it is small. Therefore, since Saturn's heat is small, as we said, and its substance is more impure and unfit for penetration: it is rightly said to dry slightly. But since Mars's substance is still more impure, it will penetrate less, but will dry more due to the abundance of heat. Finally, the bodies of Jupiter and Venus, the Sun and the Moon, due to the subtlety and multitude of light, heat and moisten, but unequally. For the Sun surpasses all in heat. Hence Jupiter is hotter than Venus, and Venus is hotter than the Moon: and conversely, the Moon easily exceeds Venus, and Venus exceeds Jupiter in humidity. Therefore, Jupiter, or as we should rather recite Ptolemy's words in Greek, 'the star of Jupiter has a temperate productive power, being in the middle of its motion, and that according to the times.'

[Planetary Natures and Influences]
Jupiter's star is of a temperate nature, as it is carried between Saturn, which cools, and Mars, which burns. It both heats and moistens. Because the power of heating prevails due to the underlying spheres, it is productive of fertile spirits. And it could not be otherwise than that Jupiter would be called fertile. For where the warm dominates the moist, there is temperance, fertility, and the best life, which seems to be the reason why the ancients named this star Ziva from living, and Jupiter as if a helping father. From the same source, it can be understood that he is the author of winds. For warmth joined with moisture, with the heat prevailing, as we note in 4, generates spirits; with the moisture prevailing, as in f, vapors. Mars' star both dries and burns, just as it corresponds to its fiery color and its proximity to the Sun, since the solar sphere is subject to it. The Sun's heat is very moist and very subtle. Therefore, by its nature, it heats more languidly, and at least dries according to quality. For Ptolemy says: The Sun is found to have the nature of heat and gradually of dryness. We perceive this much more certainly than in other stars, both because of its magnitude and the evident changes of the seasons: for the closer it approaches our vertical place, the more we experience what we have said. Venus's star, according to Ptolemy's opinion, has the same nature as Jupiter, but conversely. For it gently heats and excellently moistens. But Venus, he says, is the same as Jupiter in its temperate nature, but conversely, it is productive, for it heats gently due to its proximity to the Sun, but it moistens most vehemently, like the Moon, due to the magnitude of its own light, attracting moist exhalation from the surrounding waters of the earth. Pliny, in book 2, chapter 8, wrote that by the nature of this star, all things are generated on earth. For in either of its risings, sprinkling with generative dew, it not only fills the conceptions of the earth but also stimulates all living beings. And in chapter 16 of the same book, he says that Venus's star, wandering 8 parts from the Ecliptic, causes certain animals to be born even in the deserts of the world. When it is seen in the morning before sunrise, it is called Eosphoros and Phosphoros, the morning star, as if announcing and accelerating the light; but when it shines after sunset and prolongs the light and sets after it, it is called Hesperos, that is, the evening star, which word Virgil used in his verse: Hesperus comes, go, Goats, that is, it begins to be seen, it does not rise. For Hesperus is never seen in the east, nor Lucifer in the west. It is also called Vesperugo. Vitruvius, in book 9, says that when Venus's star follows the Sun, appearing after its setting in the sky and shining very brightly, it is called Vesperugo. They call Mercury Silbonta from radiating or flashing. This star has such a versatile nature that it imitates the qualities of the stars with which it is conjoined: as if it is joined with Saturn, it will be dry and malefic; if it agrees with the testimony of familiarity, it will be cold and intemperate. But if it is conjoined with Jupiter or Venus, it will be warm and moist, and therefore temperate and benefic. This seems to have given occasion to poets to teach that he is the messenger and minister of the gods: since he is overcome and changed by the forces of the luminaries and all other planets, and indeed even by the greater fixed stars, and passes into their nature by which he is overcome. This happens for three reasons. The first is that among all stars, he is the smallest, so much so that he is barely perceived by the senses. The second is that among the planets, he is the lightest, and being carried around very quickly, he produces a less effective influx, which easily succumbs to the stronger influx of slower stars. Finally, because the star is endowed with such a nature that it is ready to pass into and be changed into either nature. Ptolemy states that it dries and moistens equally. And it dries indeed because it never departs far from the Sun, that is, more than 28 degrees: but it moistens because it touches the moist sphere of the Moon. But it produces sudden changes in both directions, inflated or excited as if by the speed with which it is carried around. It is also the greatest author of winds, both because it revolves around the Sun, and because in its short circle, which they call epicycle, it shakes the air very quickly, like a whistling rod. These are Ptolemy's words: Mercury is generally found to be equally drying and moistening, but never far from the heat, and moistening because it is placed in the outermost sphere: and it makes quick changes in both directions, as if animated by the swift motion around it. Finally, the Moon vehemently moistens and gently heats, an indication of which is that those sleeping outdoors are filled with foreign moisture. And flesh exposed to the light of the Moon, being moist and warm, but with moisture overcoming heat, immediately putrefies. Hence Ptolemy said that it primarily causes bodies to putrefy, and rightly so: For since putrefaction is prevented either when heat dominates moisture, or when moisture is deficient, or finally when heat is deficient: and when the Moon dominates, none of these can happen: it follows that the Moon, by its excessive moisture and slight heat, is the principal cause of putrefaction. He states that it abounds in moisture because it is closest to the seat of the elements: but it is endowed with slight heat because it shines illuminated by foreign, that is, the Sun's rays. His words are these: The Moon has more power to moisten, obviously because of its proximity, and because of the moist exhalation, and thus it softens and putrefies most of the bodies subject to it. But it also partakes of heating due to the Sun's illumination.

[Differences in Planetary Rulerships]
88. DIFFERENCE. The causes, and whether it is a passion, and both are able to receive the indicated part, and the forms and causes of the nature of the stars or their symptoms. Since the most important parts of man are ruled by Saturn, namely the right ear, bladder, spleen, phlegm, and bones. Jupiter rules touch, lungs, arteries, and semen. Mars rules the left ear, kidneys, veins, and genitals. The Sun rules sight, the brain, heart, nerves, and all right-sided parts. Venus rules smell, the liver, and flesh. Mercury rules speech, intellect, tongue, bile, and the seat. The Moon rules taste, the throat, stomach, intestines, uterus, and all left-sided parts. That is: In this place, so that we may grasp a universal rule, it is necessary to contemplate the two cardinal points of the terminator, of which one is in the ascendant, the other in the descendant: but if the one in the descendant is to be especially considered, and the preceding place, which is not at all connected to the ascendant. Afterwards, it must be observed how the malefic planets aspect these places. For if the malefics are situated in the parts succeeding the said places, either by body or by tetragonal or opposite rays, or if both malefics, or one of them, inflict defects and diseases upon the native. These effects will be most evident when one or both luminaries are situated in the centers, as we have said, so that they are either together or opposite. For then, not only if any of the malefics succeeds, but also if it precedes the luminaries, provided it holds the angle exactly, it can inflict an injury or disease, such as the place of the terminator, the nature of the signs, the nature of the malefic or affected stars themselves, and finally the nature of the stars configured to them, will have indicated. For the parts of any sign surrounding the affected place of the terminator will signify the part of the body that will suffer, and whether the offended part will receive an injury or a disease, or rather both. The natures of the stars, however, reveal the types and causes of these events. For among the most important parts of man, Saturn rules the right ear, bladder, spleen, phlegm, and bones: Jupiter rules touch, lungs, arteries, and semen. Mars has the left ear, kidneys, veins, and genitals: The Sun has sight, the brain, heart, nerves, and all right-sided parts: Venus has smell, the liver, and flesh: Mercury has speech, reason, tongue, bile, and the seat: The Moon has taste, the throat, stomach, intestines, uterus, and all left-sided parts. In this text, Ptolemy perfectly shows us four significant points to be diligently observed. First, he declares the matter or subjects upon which injuries and diseases are usually impressed, namely the seventh house, then the first, then the sixth, which is not conjoined to the horoscope. It is reasonable, and Cardan says it has been observed, that the first and seventh always receive defects, but the sixth receives diseases. Secondly, he describes the efficient causes of such plagues, namely the bodies of the malefics, and their hostile rays. Therefore, when these causes concur with the subject matter, they offend the bodies of natives in many ways: especially if the luminaries are simultaneously afflicted, either by opposition or by square aspect. Thirdly, he teaches that which we are principally discussing in this place, namely that the nature and quality of illnesses must be deduced from four main circumstances. First, from the nature of the terminator or the places of the world, namely the first or seventh house, the sixth or twelfth, for we said a little earlier that these often show diseases, while those show defects or injuries. Then from the double nature of the places in the zodiac, namely from the images of the stars, which they call morphomata, and from the dodecatemoria, which are counted from the vernal intersection. Then from the nature of the malefic or affected stars themselves. Finally, from the nature of the stars configured to them. Moreover, the parts of any sign surrounding the affected places externally declare the parts of the body that will suffer, just as the head and neck, and the remaining signs indicate the remaining parts of the human body according to the superior distribution. By the members signified by the planets, the author understands the humors and internal members, just as they are distributed to each star in Ptolemy's text. Haly believes that Ptolemy means by the parts of the signs the planetary bounds or terms, which are in the eastern horizon or in the center of the seventh house. For example, if the affected part of the horoscope is the term of Jupiter, since it signifies the arteries and lungs, it portends evil for the lungs and arteries. He says these things beautifully, but he is off the mark and does not satisfy Ptolemy's words, which speak not of bounds, but of the natures of the malefic and affected stars. Furthermore, Ptolemy attributes this power of affecting members even to the luminaries, which do not have bounds, but embrace entire signs in place of bounds. From this, it is easily apparent that he wanted planets to signify one thing and the parts and bounds of signs another. Fourthly and finally, from this text we must note which parts of the human body principally correspond to which planets, for knowing this correctly greatly helps in judging future diseases, since that member is vitiated or becomes diseased which is ruled by an afflicted planet in the fate or nativity: just as the right or left eye or both are affected when the luminaries are badly disposed. Thus, diseases of the ears and teeth accompany the affliction of Saturn. And Venus badly placed corrupts the seminal vessels, and for this reason makes people infertile, impotent for Venus, and hectic. Mercury afflicted takes away the use of the tongue and speech, similarly we find the chest or lung vitiated, or the liver, or the spleen, or the heart, or something corrupted from the intestines. Furthermore, in the distribution by which the internal members are divided among the planets, Cardan differs somewhat from Ptolemy, and he thinks that in this matter, reason and experience should be adhered to rather than Ptolemy's authority. To what extent they differ, you can easily estimate from a collation of both distributions, which I will present here as in a table. Saturn has, according to Ptolemy: Right ear, bladder, spleen, phlegm, and bones. According to Cardan: Right ear, bladder, spleen, melancholy, and crude, unnatural phlegm, cartilages. Jupiter has, according to Ptolemy: Touch, lungs, arteries, blood, and semen. According to Cardan: Touch, lungs, liver, and flesh. Mars has, according to Ptolemy: Left ear, kidneys, veins, and genitals. According to Cardan: Left ear and ligaments, kidneys, veins, and genitals, bile, intestines. The Sun has, according to Ptolemy: Sight, brain, heart, nerves, and all right-sided parts. According to Cardan: Right eye and seat, heart, arteries, and blood contained in the arteries, nerves, mind, mind, reason, reason. Venus has, according to Ptolemy: Smell, liver, flesh. According to Cardan: Smell, memory, fingers, taste, semen, seat, spirit. The Moon has, according to Ptolemy: Taste, throat, stomach, intestines, uterus, and all left-sided parts. According to Cardan: Taste, brain, stomach, left eye, uterus, and natural phlegm. And when it is full of light, it signifies much, insipid, and sweet phlegm: and if it is mixed with Saturn, it is acidic: But empty of light, little. Therefore, if Mars is mixed, it easily becomes bitter or salty, for little cause is infected. Here.

[Sun and Moon Qualities]
The rest of them differ in the quality of their generation, such as the Sun and the Moon.

[Differences in Degrees]
It should be noted that most body parts are governed by two or three planets: for example, the brain, in terms of its substance, by the Moon; in terms of its arteries, by the Sun; and finally, in terms of its spirit and faculties, by Mercury. And thus far, we have explained the natural properties of the celestial places, and their sympathy with both celestial and inferior bodies. The following more subtle properties of places, with the exception of antiscia, since they were left aside and scorned by Ptolemy as curious and lacking physical reasons, should also be deservedly suspect to us. CONCERNING MASCULINE AND FEMININE DEGREES OF THE SIGNS. There are also degrees in each sign that are properly called masculine and feminine. For from the beginning of Aries up to the 8th degree, they are said to be masculine; from the 8th to the 9th, feminine; and from the 9th to the 15th, masculine; and from the 15th up to the 22nd, feminine; and from the 22nd up to the end of Aries, masculine. And in this way, we depict the table, so that the work may be made easier, with God's help. Aries: Masculine 8, Feminine 1; Masculine 6, Feminine 7; Masculine 8. Leo: Masculine 5, Feminine 3; Masculine 7, Feminine 8; Masculine 7. Sagittarius: Masculine 3, Feminine 3; Masculine 7, Feminine 12; Masculine 6. Taurus: Feminine 5, Masculine 6; Feminine 8, Masculine 11; Feminine 3. Virgo: Feminine 8, Masculine 11; Feminine 6, Masculine 4; Feminine 12. Capricorn: Masculine 11, Feminine 4; Masculine 10, Feminine 8; Masculine 10. Gemini: Feminine 5, Masculine 11; Feminine 6, Masculine 5; Feminine 7. Libra: Masculine 5, Feminine 10; Masculine 5, Feminine 4; Masculine 3. Aquarius: Masculine 5, Feminine 10; Masculine 6, Feminine 4; Masculine 2. Cancer: Masculine 2, Feminine 6; Masculine 2, Feminine 2; Masculine 11. Scorpio: Masculine 4, Feminine 10; Masculine 3, Feminine 8; Masculine 5. Pisces: Masculine 10, Feminine 10; Masculine 3, Feminine 5; Masculine 1. Ptolemy sought gender not in parts, but in whole signs, according to whose opinion both masculine and feminine signs are diurnal, from which feminine signs continuously follow masculine signs in a series. For example, Aries is masculine, Taurus feminine, Gemini masculine, Cancer feminine, Leo masculine, Virgo feminine, and so on to the end of the zodiac. CONCERNING BRIGHT, DARK, SMOKY, AND EMPTY DEGREES. And in each of these signs, there are degrees that are called bright, and degrees that are called dark, degrees that are called smoky, and degrees that are called empty. For some say that from the beginning of Aries up to the third degree are dark, and from the third to the eighth, bright, and from the eighth to the sixteenth, dark, and from the sixteenth to the twentieth, bright, and from the twentieth up to the twenty-third, empty, and from the twenty-third up to the twenty-ninth, bright, and from the twenty-ninth to the end of Aries, empty: concerning which we will make a table, if God wills. Aries: Dark 1-3, Bright 3-8, Dark 8-16, Bright 16-20, Empty 20-23, Bright 23-29, Empty 29-30. Leo: Dark 1-10, Bright 10-19, Smoky 19-23, Empty 23-24, Bright 24-29, Empty 29-30. Sagittarius: Bright 1-9, Dark 9-12, Bright 12-20, Smoky 20-24, Bright 24-30. Taurus: Dark 1-3, Bright 3-7, Empty 7-12, Bright 12-15, Empty 15-20, Dark 20-28, Empty 28-30. Virgo: Dark 1-7, Bright 7-10, Empty 10-15, Bright 15-22, Empty 22-27, Dark 27-30. Capricorn: Bright 1-3, Empty 3-11, Smoky 11-19, Bright 19-22, Empty 22-25, Dark 25-30. Gemini: Bright 1-4, Dark 4-7, Bright 7-19, Empty 19-21, Bright 21-27, Empty 27-30. Libra: Bright 1-5, Dark 5-10, Bright 10-16, Empty 16-20, Bright 20-25, Empty 25-30. Aquarius: Smoky 1-4, Dark 4-13, Bright 13-22, Empty 22-27, Dark 27-30. Cancer: Bright 1-12, Dark 12-14, Empty 14-18, Dark 18-20, Bright 20-28, Empty 28-30. Scorpio: Dark 1-3, Bright 3-12, Empty 12-18, Smoky 18-20, Bright 20-22, Empty 22-27, Dark 27-30. Pisces: Dark 1-6, Bright 6-12, Empty 12-14, Bright 14-23, Empty 23-25, Dark 25-30. CONCERNING PIT DEGREES. And in the signs, there are certain degrees that are called pits. When a planet is in any of them, it is said to be in a pit, such as the sixth degree of Aries and others, as will be shown in the following table. Aries: 6, 11, 16, 23, 29. Taurus: 5, 12, 24, 25.
