If on the estimated day of conception you find the Moon's place in the sign, at the time when the infant is said to have been born, rising, as happened in our example, or even in its opposite, know that you have reached the true goal with a certain calculation. For, as was said a little earlier, in what sign it was found at conception, that same or its opposite ascends at birth. But if the Moon was absent from the said signs by a two-day motion or less, its motion for the next following days must be taken: And conversely, if the Moon exceeded the same places, the Moon's motion of the preceding days must be observed until the Moon's place reaches the next smaller place of the angle: for thus it will happen that the true nativity, as is consistent with reason, always...

[Moon in Sun's Rays]
And if the Moon is in these places under the Sun's rays, it will not be suitable as Hyleg. You will look for the Hyleg in the angles and their succedent houses, according to how the twelve houses of the circle are equalized by the degrees of the ascending hours, as its operation is explained in the canon of the planets, that is, in the book of the courses of the planets. And when you have equalized the houses in this way: every planet that is five degrees or less before the degree of the ascending sign, or of any house, its strength will be valid in the house that succeeds it. And every place among the places we have mentioned is suitable for Hyleg: if any of its lords, who is the lord of the house, or the lord of its exaltation, or the lord of its terms, or of its triplicity, or the lord of its face, aspects it; and if not, it will not be suitable for Hyleg. Regarding Alcochoden. And from this Alcochoden, who is the significator of life, that is, the giver of years or the lesser giver of years: when you wish to know him, and when you have known the Hyleg in the order I have described, you will look at the lord of the Hyleg's house, or the lord of its exaltation, or the lord of its term, or the lord of its triplicity, or of its face, which of these is stronger and more authoritative in the place of the Hyleg: and if he aspects the Hyleg, he will be more worthy of being Alcochoden: but if he does not aspect the Hyleg, whoever has more authority: you will look at the one with less authority, until you find one of them who aspects it: but if he does not aspect the Hyleg, that place will not be able to be the Hyleg. And you will seek another Hyleg, and again you will seek the Alcochoden from the same second Hyleg in the order we have described: but if two planets are equal in authority to the degree of the Hyleg, and aspect the Hyleg, the one who is stronger in place will be more worthy of being Alcochoden. But if they are equal in strength of place, that is, where the planets themselves are, the one who is closer to the degree of the Hyleg will be the Alcochoden. To some, it seemed better to look at the lord of the house: if he aspected the Hyleg, they would make him Alcochoden, and would not consider another: and if they did not find the lord of the house aspecting the Hyleg, they would take the lord of the exaltation: if they saw him aspecting the Hyleg, they would make him Alcochoden, and would not consider another: and similarly they would do with the lord of the triplicity, terms, and face in order: and Dorotheus preferred the lord of the term over the lord of the house in this matter: And some said that if two planets, or three, or more, are equal in dignity, and in proximity of aspect to the degree of the Hyleg, the one who is in a laudable place from the Sun will be the Alcochoden: that is, the one who is with the Sun in one degree by sixteen minutes, or less: or closer to the degree of the angle: or in the beginnings of its rising, that is, when it appears in the morning: or is in its second station; or is in some laudable state from the Sun, as we have said, he will be the Alcochoden. But if the degree of the Sun is in the Hyleg, and it is in Aries or Leo, the Sun will be Hyleg and Alcochoden together: and no other Alcochoden will be considered besides it. Similarly, if the degree of the Moon is Hyleg and it is in Taurus or Cancer, you will take it as Hyleg and Alcochoden together, and you will not consider any other Alcochoden besides it. Almut is he who presides over the nativity: from him is signified the being born after the Hyleg and Alcochoden, and he is of greater authority than the other planets, in the ascendant and in the places of the luminaries and in the place of the Part of Fortune, and also in the place of conjunction or prevention, which is before the nativity. But if any planet presides over two places or three, or four, or more by the multitude of its power, it will be the Almut, that is, the author and significator of life after the Hyleg and Alcochoden, and through him is signified the being born. And some consider him as Alcochoden for giving life. The following two chapters pertain to the greatest and principal astrological question, by which the lifespan of the native is explained. And although, according to Ptolemy, the explanation of this question is not simple or easy, nor is it easy, and finally it requires great labor and uncommon prudence to see when the power of the giver of life is extinguished, and which star is the destroyer of life or the killer of the native, to perceive: Nevertheless, the precepts taught here are neither so obscure nor difficult, and are concluded in three principal places. For this treatise depends entirely on the apprehension of the Aphetic places, and the stars ruling them, and finally the stars and places that destroy. One of these, and how each is to be judged from the tradition of Ptolemy, I will first indicate chapter by chapter, and afterwards I will add the opinion of the author and other Arabs. Regarding Aphetic places. Concerning these, Ptolemy says thus: Aphetic places are those in which it is absolutely necessary for him to be found who wishes to obtain jurisdiction over the moderation of life. He enumerates, just as he does prorogators, so also the places in which prorogators, when placed, determine life, five, whose series is this: The first place, and which is preferred to the others in power and authority here, is the Midheaven. The second, and first in proximity of power, is the Ascendant. The third is the eleventh house, the Good Spirit. The fourth is the seventh house. The fifth, and weaker than the others, is the ninth house, God. The remaining seven houses are useless. For first, Ptolemy rightly teaches that everything that is subterranean is to be postponed in this excellent kind of dominion, with the sole exception that when it comes to light with the horoscope, that is, the 25 degrees that follow the eastern cardinal point. Then, from those places that are above ground, it is not appropriate to accept the eighth place, called idle, which is not connected to the ascendant by any bond of familiarity, nor the twelfth, which is called the place of the evil daemon. For besides being cast down from the angle, and being smoky and dark to the horoscope, born from earthly vapors, it disturbs and as it were abolishes the efflux of the stars dwelling there; for which reason they do not appear in their colors or magnitudes. But the places which he posits as Aphetic, all except the 25 parts succeeding the center of the east, are above ground, and to the horoscope in the equinoctial, the eleventh is configured by a sextile, the tenth by a square, the ninth by a trine, and the seventh by an opposite aspect. Finally, it must be diligently observed here that each place comprises thirty equinoctial parts, of which five precede the cusp, and 25 succeeding ones follow it. Therefore, although the eleventh place extends up to the twelfth by 30 degrees of the equinoctial: nevertheless, those last five degrees of the eleventh, although they are not entirely devoid of virtue, do not have the power to make a star dwelling there the lord of life. But when a suitable place succeeds a suitable place, then those last five degrees are not removed, because although they are not good by reason of the place of which they are a part, nevertheless they are considered suitable by reason of the succeeding place. As the last 5 parts of the ninth place, although they are good by reason of the proper place, they are not.

[Aphetic Places and Alcocoden]
They also say that the Moon opposing the Ascendant kills, especially if it has dignity in the eighth house. This is Ptolemy's opinion on this matter. It remains for us to briefly depict, as if in a table, which authors teach us to choose the significators of life from the opinions of others. In diurnal nativities, look within 5 degrees that have risen above the horizon at the end of the twelfth house. First, in the tenth, which, if it is in the eleventh, if it is in the seventh, eighth, ninth. Ascendant, second, third, seventh. Second, look within 5 degrees that have risen above the horizon, which, if it is in the tenth, in the eleventh, in the fourth, fifth, in any masculine sign, the Sun will be there. If the Moon is in any feminine sign only, within 5 degrees preceding the cusp of the seventh. In nocturnal nativities, look within 5 degrees that have risen above the horizon. First, in the tenth, which, if it is in the eleventh, if it is in the seventh, in the eighth, in the ninth. In its masculine sign, the Moon will be there, only if it is masculine. Second, within 5 degrees before the cusp of the seventh house, below the earth, in any sign, the Sun, which, if it is in the fifth, will be there. In the Ascendant, in a masculine sign, in the second. If neither luminary is found suitable for the Hyleg, and the degree of conjunction precedes the nativity and is in an angle or succedent house. Opposition of the opposition: If these places are not found suitable enough for the Hyleg, then the Part of Fortune will moderate life, if it is found in angles or succedent houses; if not, the degree of the Horoscopus will prolong life. But the types of signs are not to be considered here, but only in the luminaries. According to this reasoning, the Sun has six Aphetic places above the earth, namely, 5 degrees above the horizon, the tenth, eleventh, seventh, eighth, and ninth. Below the earth, five: namely, five degrees before the seventh, the fourth, fifth, the Horoscopus, and the second house. The Moon, however, has five Aphetic places above the earth: namely, five degrees preceding the Horoscopus, the tenth, eleventh, seventh, and eighth. Below the earth, six: namely, the Ascendant, the second house, the third, fourth, fifth, and five degrees preceding the cusp of the west. First caution: A combust Moon cannot be a Hyleg; indeed, no combust planet can be a significator of life. Concerning the arcs of emergence and occultation, within which stars oppressed by the Sun's rays are combust, enough has been said above. You will also look at the Hyleg, etc. Second caution, how this is to be understood can be seen from what we have said above concerning the distribution of the 12 houses according to the opinion of John of Regiomontanus and others. Third caution, which also agrees with Ptolemy's doctrine, but in Ptolemy, one house extends over a space of 30 parts of the equinoctial circle, of which five before the cusp of the house and twenty-five immediately following obtain the virtue of one house. But the author seems to be speaking of parts of the zodiac. Fourth caution, which dissents from Ptolemy's doctrine. No Hyleg can be assigned unless the Alcocoden also concurs, that is, the planet that rules in the place of the Hyleg and aspects it with some aspect. For whatever planet has the greater prerogative in the place of the Hyleg and aspects that same place, they call it the Alcocoden. If it happens that several attest at the same time, the one superior in both aspect and dignity is to be preferred: for he who has more dignities and is closer to it in degrees will be the Alcocoden. Finally, if the Apheta is in its own domicile or exaltation, then it will be both Hyleg and Alcocoden, when, that is, it has no aspecting planet from the lords of essential dignities. The Arabs derive conjectures about the longevity or brevity of life from the Alcocoden. For the Alcocoden found in an angle is said to signify its greater years, in a succedent house, its middle years, in a cadent house, its lesser years. I will not adduce any examples of this, because it is clear enough by itself, and because these conjectures are very weak and dissent from Ptolemy's doctrine, nor do they seem to present any physical reason. Indeed, if the lord of the place powerfully aspects the place itself, and especially with a good aspect, it renders the Apheta stronger, and thereby provides a stronger and longer life to the native, as Ptolemy testifies, who taught that in Aphetic and killing places, with what suffrages they are supported, must be diligently weighed. Therefore, a planet friendly to the Aphetic sign, if it shines upon the Apheta with its ray, although it adds much strength to it, so that it does not succumb for a slight cause, and that it may more easily overcome the Aneratas that oppose it: nevertheless, it will hardly be able to indicate a certain number of years of life, which must be sought with greater industry and labor, without the grossest errors. The Arabs call the Victor or Lord of the nativity the Almuten of the nativity, the Greeks κύριος γενέσεως: it is the planet that obtains more and better prerogatives in the five Aphetic places, namely, the place of the Sun, the place of the Moon, the place of the eastern angle, the place of the Part of Fortune, and the place of the luminaries closest to the nativity. Therefore, whichever of the planets obtains the greater and more powerful abundance of suffrages in the said places, that one will obtain the lordship of the nativity. By suffrages here we understand the rulership of the house, exaltation, trigon, and terms. Finally, conjunction and any other aspect, indeed, even ruling and commanding. Julius Firmicus, in Book 4, Chapter 12, believes that the lord of the nativity is the one whose sign the Moon will first enter after the person is born. For example, if someone had the Moon in Aries at the first hour of birth, because the Moon makes its transit to Taurus in the second place, it will obtain the lordship of the nativity, because it is the sign of Taurus, and so in the other signs. In this way, it must be observed that neither the Sun nor the Moon can be made lords in any nativity. Therefore, if the Moon is found in Taurus on the day a person is born, then neither in Taurus, that is, in its own house, nor in the house of the Sun, will it signify the lord of the nativity: but when it has passed these signs and come to another sign, then it will indicate the lord of the nativity. Because Taurus is the house of Venus, Venus will be made the lord of the nativity. However, just as many other precepts of Firmicus, so also this one dissents from the true doctrine of Ptolemy, even if it seems to have some similarity with Ptolemy's rule, by which he teaches to observe the place of the planet or the ray upon which the significator first fell by diurnal motion, as we will see below. But this is another reason. Concerning the profection of signs. And from this, the sign of profection in the years of nativities and of the world. For in the years of nativities, the knowledge is to look at how many years have passed for the native from the perfect solar years, and you will look at one sign each year, starting from the Ascendant of the native by the succession of signs, until the number is finished. The sign that succeeds is the sign of profection from the Ascendant, namely, the sign of the entered year, which you have not included in the number. This will be in the same degree as it was in the Ascendant of the nativity: and its lord is called the Alcochoden, whose interpretation is the lord of the year. Similarly, you will count from the sign of the Sun one sign for each year, and from this will come the sign of profection from the Sun. Similarly, from the sign of the Moon and from the Midheaven, from the Part of Fortune in the likeness of the degree of the radix, that is, the point of nativity. An example of this is that someone was born with Capricorn rising, namely, in its 17th degree: the Sun was in Pisces in the 15th degree: and the Midheaven was in Scorpio in the 8th degree. The Moon was in Libra in the 15th degree, and the Part of Fortune in Leo in the 17th degree. And now three perfect years have passed for the native, and the fourth year will arrive from the Ascendant in Aries, which is the fourth from Capricorn up to the 17th degree of that same Aries, and Mars will be the Alcochoden: the place of the Sun arrives at Gemini up to the 15th degree of that same sign: and the Moon arrives at Capricorn at the 15th degree. The profection from the Midheaven arrives at the 8th degree of Aquarius, the profection from the Part of Fortune arrives at the 17th degree of Scorpio. And when the year arrives at the degree of profection, as at the 17th degree.

[Profection of the World's Years]
In this example of Aries: and if it were between the 393rd degree between itself and a similar degree of the succeeding sign, to which the following year ought to arrive, in the same house a planet or its rays: and you wish to know when the profection will reach that planet or its rays: you will look at what is between the degree to which the year will arrive, and the planet or its rays, in degrees and minutes: you will multiply that by 12. And the sixth part of that number, which you multiply, or in 12 degrees, 6 minutes of one degree, whatever results, will be the days of that year in which you are, in which the profection will arrive from the degree in which it begins, up to the degree to which you have counted, after which the profection of that planet will occur. Alchindus said that the profection from the years of the world is that which was between the year of the conjunction that signified the Saracen sect, and the year of Albegerat in which Muhammad first began to preach, which was the first of the Arab years, 52 years and 57 days: and the ascendant of that year of the conjunction of the aforesaid sect was the sign of Gemini: the profection of that same year arrived at Virgo, and between the first of the Arab years and the first of the years of King Iezdygird of the Persians, there were 3624 perfect days. Therefore, when you wish to have knowledge of this matter: take the years of Iezdygird, convert them into days, as has already been explained in the Azig, that is, in the book of the courses of the planets: add the days that are between the first of the Arab years and Iezdygird: then divide this by 365 days and a quarter of a day: as many divisions as come out, so many will be the Solar years: and what remains of months and days will be from the imperfect year: when this has been collected from the years, these are the Solar years from the beginning of the Arab years, therefore cast out one sign for each year and begin from Virgo, to whatever sign the number leads you, that will be the sign to which the year of the world arrives from the ascendant of the conjunction of the aforesaid sect. Others, however, outside of Alchindus, thought it right to add to the perfect years of Iezdygird 61 years, 2 months, 12 days, 16 hours, from the Persian years: which are without fraction, that is, without a quarter of a day, and they would extend these years into days, and convert the days into Solar years, as we have said, and begin to cast out from the beginning of Libra. But if you wish the profection from the sign of the conjunction of the sect, let the profection be from Scorpio: but if you wish the profection from the ascendant of the kingdom, subtract from the years of Iezdygird those 317 perfect years, and convert them into Solar years as we have said: and begin to cast out from Virgo. Again, if you wish the profection from the ascendant of the profection of the change of conjunction from the watery triplicity to the fiery triplicity, subtract from the perfect years of Iezdygird 176 years, and convert those that remain into Solar years, begin to cast out from Leo, and to whatever sign the number arrives, that will be the profection of each beginning of those things we have mentioned. And from this, the Aphetic places at the time of the origin of things, found in certain parts of the zodiac, do not remain fixed, but are moved annually, monthly, and daily by revolutions of 30 degrees of the zodiac into succeeding signs. The author here places two kinds of such progression of these places, commonly called profection. One is the profection of nativities, the other of the years of the world. For the annual profection of the five Aphetic places in the nativity of men is that in which generally for each Solar year, the space of one sign, that is, 30 parts, is allotted. The planet, however, which rules such a sign, they call the lord of the year or the annual Chronocrator. But if the aforesaid 30 parts are concluded by the boundaries of two distinct signs, as often happens, then also the annual dominion is distributed to different planets by parts of time. For example: If in someone's nativity 12 parts fall into the eastern angle, the first year will have the space of the zodiac which extends from the 12th part to the 12th part. And so for the first 7 months and 9 days, they will preside for 18 parts. The remainder of the year, that is, 4 months and 26 days, will be governed by and, which same planets will dispose of the first part of the following year, so that the dominion of the last part of the same following year devolves to the lord of Gemini. At the end of the third year, the profection will reach part 12, and its Chronocrator will be with 4: and so consequently according to the order of the succeeding signs, we will arrange the annual arbiters of times, up to the twelfth year, which being completed, in the thirteenth year the profection will return to the epoch or to the radical place, that is, to the degree of the eastern angle, and the lord and will return again, and will proceed in the same way: and in this manner, as has been said, each Aphetic place, traversing these places of the sky orbicularly to the end of life, will complete one period every twelfth year. Therefore, if you wish to know, after many years of a native's life have passed, what place the profection of the horoscope ambulates, divide the completed years of the native by 12, and extend the remaining number from the horoscope in the manner we have advised. For example, let a native live, whose horoscope was part 14, in the 40th year. Therefore, he will have 39 completed years, which divided by 12 leave 3 completed years, the first of which we assign to Leo, the second to, the third to, in the current year of the native's age, that is, in the 40th year of the native's age, we will understand the horoscope to have proceeded to part 14 of Scorpio, and we will constitute the lord of that sign, the chronocrator and the principal lord of such a year, until the same progression is introduced, which will happen after about 194 days of revolution: since the annual profection traverses 4 first scruples and besides 56 secondary scruples every day, then 4, the lord of Sagittarius, will succeed Mars in annual dominion. But these things which have been said about the profection of the horoscope, from whose application to the more benevolent or more malevolent radiations of the planets good or bad accidents in the native's body in that year are foreseen, are to be understood in exactly the same way and manner concerning the culminating degree for mastery, concerning the degree for dignity and honor, and concerning the remaining parts of the lots for other accidents. But all these things in nativities, which we wish to examine more accurately, it will be better to distribute by a table, which you will construct in this way. In the first series, place the years of the native from 1 to 12. In the second from 13 to 24. In the third from 25 to 36. In the fourth from 37 to 48. And so on up to the last years of the native's life. Afterwards, at the top of the years of age and in the first series, write the current years of Christ, which contain the beginning of the nativity, to which immediately add 12, and what arises from this, place at the top of the second series, or above the 13th year of age, and so on, adding 12 years, until the last series of the native's years of age is reached: this done, opposite the 1st year of age, the epoch of the horoscope is to be placed in the sign and degree, then the epoch of the Moon: third the epoch: fourth the epoch of the MC: fifth and last the epoch of the part of fortune. If these vertical signs are led down to the foot of the table according to their natural series, the table of annual profections will be completed, as can be seen in the assumed nativity, whose epochs and profections of the five Aphetic places we have here presented to you tabularly as an example. [Direction of Significators in Quadrants]
If the significator is in one quadrant, and the place to which you direct it is in another quadrant, you will direct the significator to the succeeding angle. After this, you will direct from the angle to the place, just as I showed you the direction from the angle, and you will combine both directions.

[Calculating Direction in Years]
When you know the significator and wish to know where the direction from the circle of signs will arrive in a certain number of years: if the significator is in the ascendant: you will add the number of years to the ascensions of the degree of the ascendant: and you will make it an arc in the ascension of the region: and where the arc of degrees from the circle of signs comes out, there the direction will arrive in the same year. But if the significator is in the 7th house, you will add the number of years to the ascensions in the 7th house, you will add the number of years to the nadir of the degree of the significator: and you will arc it also in the ascensions of the region: and what comes out of the circle of signs, to its nadir the direction will arrive in the same year. But if the significator is in the 10th or 4th house, you will add to the ascensions of the degree of the significator in the direct circle the number of years: and you will arc it in the ascensions of the direct circle, and what comes out of the circle of signs, there the direction will arrive in the same year. But if the significator is outside these four places which are the angles: you will know the hours of longitude from the angle, as I said before: if the significator is in the eastern half: you will add to the ascensions of the degree of the significator through the direct circle the number of years you wish: and you will arc this in the ascensions of the direct circle, and what comes out, will be the significator of the direct circle, keep it. After this, you will also add the number of years to the ascensions of the degree of the significator in the region: you will arc this in the ascension of the region: and what it is, will be the significator of the region. After this, you will take the sixth part of the remainder between the significator of the direct circle and the significator of the region: and you will multiply it by the hours of longitude from the angle: what it is, will be the equation. But if the significator of the direct circle is less than the significator of the region: you will add the equation to the significator of the direct circle: if it is more, you will subtract it from it: and what remains, there the direction will arrive from the circle of signs in the same year. But if the significator is in the western half, you will make it the nadir of the degree of the significator, as you did with the degree of the significator in the work before it: and what it is, there the direction will arrive from the circle of signs in the same year.

[Locus Divisionis and Divisor]
And the place to which the direction arrives is called the place of division: the lord of the term of that place is called the divisor: if another planet or its rays or near the place before it is in the degree of division: this planet or the lord of the rays is said to be a participant of the divisor in the division.

[Five Significators for Direction]
The significators which are directed are five places, that is, the degree of the ascendant, and the degree of the Sun, the degree of the Moon, the degree of Apheta, also the Part of Fortune, and the degree of the Midheaven. The climacteric degree of the ascendant is directed to discern accidents, which happen to the body: and the degree of the Sun to causes of dignity and exaltation: also of honor and kingdom: the Moon for the essence of the soul and body and marriage, the Part of Fortune for acquisitions and the smallness or generosity of profits, and the Midheaven for mastery and other particular dispositions and their essence.

[Direction in Revolutions]
But if it is the ascendant of the revolution of any years of the world or nativities, its significators are directed according to this direction, namely, one day for each degree. Some think that the significators of the year are directed in this way, namely, for every 59 minutes and 8 seconds, one day: for the direction of kings and princes is directed to them from the degree of the Midheaven through the ascensions of the direct circle, for every 59 minutes and 8 seconds, one day, until it reaches good or bad planets. And the essence of kings in health or illness is directed from the degree of the ascendant to good or bad planets for every 59 minutes and 8 seconds, one day through the ascensions of the region. And the direction in the revolution of the years of the world and to predict the essence of the common people or rustics from the degree of the ascendant: similarly and to predict the essence of the king from the degree of the Midheaven, and in the revolution of the years of nativities to predict the essence of the native from the degree of the ascendant of the revolution, for every 59 minutes and 8 seconds through the ascensions of the region, one day.

[On Directions or Deductions of Significators]
And from this, to direct in Latin is what the Greeks call ευθύνομ, ἢ ἰθύνου το σκάλιους, which means: to correct what is crooked and make it straight: and a straight path is that which does not deviate into windings, but proceeds directly, and as the Greeks say, επ' ευθείας. Hence I believe it has been accepted that the reduction of the oblique and unequal ascensions of the zodiac to a regular and equal measure is called direction. For since in both the right and oblique sphere, the parts of the Ecliptic rise and set unequally, so that sometimes more, sometimes less time is consumed in ascending and descending, therefore this anomaly or unequal progression of the Ecliptic, sometimes proceeding obliquely, sometimes directly, must be corrected, and compared to the certain and regular motion of the equinoctial, which precisely raises and lowers 15 parts in every hour in every position of the sphere, so that the times of events, measured by the progression of the parts of the sky, can be certainly known. For when individual parts are said to announce individual years in this doctrine, this is not to be understood of the Ecliptic, as Albumasar thought, but of the parts of the equinoctial. For example, the sign of Leo almost consumes 2 hours, 49 minutes, and 14 seconds before it entirely ascends in Cologne. But Aquarius rises completely in 1 hour and 10 minutes and 14 seconds, so that no one fails to understand that the parts of Leo produce a longer tract than the parts of Aquarius. For the sign of Leo, in ascending, draws 42 parts, 23 minutes, and 14 seconds of the equinoctial in that place, while the sign of Aquarius draws only 17 parts, 25 minutes, and 14 seconds. Therefore, since in the Ecliptic the parts of one sign easily unify the length of the co-rising parts of the equinoctial, while those of another are further from the same (for individual degrees of Aquarius do not complete years, but each degree of Leo occupies more than one year), both must be examined to a uniform and equal measure of the equinoctial. Such a correction of oblique and unequal progression is commonly called direction, a term which Pontanus often rejects as inappropriate, and prescribes that it should be called ambulation or progression: the Greeks called it wίπαμ& ἄφεσι. Some want wίπα to be a generic term, signifying any progression of any place: ἄφεσιμ, however, is a specific kind of ambulation, which we are discussing here, by which the prorogator and lord of life, called Ilech in Arabic, or any other progressing significator, is led to opposing planets or their aspects by equinoctial or diurnal motion, or rather, not the prorogator itself, but rather, according to Ptolemy, the intervening parts, with the prorogator fixed immovably in the Ecliptic of the ninth sphere, and sustaining the circle of position, are led to Apheta. Therefore, whenever the prorogator, remaining in its seat, which it held in the position of the nativity, is invaded by the bodies of malefics, or their square or opposite rays, it is called διέρχεθ, which is commonly called cutting off. For when malefics or their threatening rays encounter the moderator of life or the horoscope in this way, they cut off life, or at least bring danger to the body. But the parts which, by their approach to the lord of life, usually bring death or danger to life, are called μοίρας αναιρετικά's, that is, lethal and intervening parts, from the malignancy of the place, as was said above. These can be distinguished in this way according to Ptolemy's opinion: but we, in the exposition of the author, for the sake of teaching, will retain his and the other appellations of those who wrote after Ptolemy, by which universal progressions are not so badly, it seems, designated by peculiar appellations.

[Direction and Profection]
They are distinguished. They call the method of 21 ἀφέσεωμ, by which the chronocrators are taken from the times of the equinoctial Catholic circle, a direction. The other method of progression, by which the annual, monthly, and daily disposers of times are ordered, they call profection. And profections were discussed in the previous chapter: In this chapter, however, the author explains the laws of directions, of which this is the description. To direct is to artificially investigate the arc of the equinoctial intercepted between the significator and the promittor, co-ascending or co-descending with the arc of the Ecliptic, with respect to the circle of position, in which one of them lies, that is: To direct is nothing other than to see how many degrees of the world the midheaven or the horizon of the climate, and another circle of position, pass, while a star or a first place is led to another star or to the rays of another, or to some other second place. We call here, as above, the circle of position by the intersections of the meridian and the horizon and the path of the star. We call the significator or Apheta the first place, to which the second is led, and which obtains the role of the subject, about to receive some change at a certain time from the promittor. The other, however, who progresses to the former, and who plays the role of the active cause, is called the promittor and Anareta. For, as I warned a little earlier, in direct direction according to Ptolemy's opinion, the Anareta is led to the aphetic place, not the Apheta to the Anareta, as is commonly thought. I will shortly subjoin his words concerning the anaretic parts, which occur in the converse direction of the apheta, from which it will be clear that in converse direction, the Apheta invades the destroying parts, whence it immediately follows that in the other or direct direction, the anaretas seek the apheta by their influence. The time, however, which elapses while some place of the sky moves to the seat of another place, either measures the period of the native's life, or defines the outcome of some other event, if it is resolved into parts or times of the equinoctial, for there will be as many future years as there are equal times of direction. Therefore, five scruples will show a month, and single scruples will show six days and two hours. Furthermore, there are two kinds of direction: One Regiomontanus in problem 25 calls direct direction, in which the second place, that is, the promittor or anareta, is understood to be led to the position of the first, that is, to the seat of the significator or apheta. This is done in the subsequent signs, according to the ascensions of the apheta itself, and by Ptolemy it is called ἀκινοβολία, that is, the projection of rays, because by the mere deduction of a ray to a similar position, it simply collects the time of a future event. The other, εἰς τὰ προαγόμλra, that is, into the preceding signs, he calls converse direction, in which the Aphetic place is transferred to the place of the anareta according to the ascensions of the anareta itself in the preceding signs. Some diviners use this direction for horoscopes and other lots, and for leading retrograde planets. But I see Ptolemy making this method proper to the significator of life constituted between the cusp of the tenth and seventh houses. Ptolemy wants, however, when the significator of life from such a position is to be led εἰς τὰ προκγόμενα, that only that place which is in the western terminator should be destroyed, and for that reason, the giver of life in western places, that is, found from the culmination of the sky and between the western cardinal point, acts both in subsequent and preceding signs. But in this case, when the Apheta is led by diurnal motion to a similar position of a star or ray existing in the preceding signs, the time that elapses in the meantime does not measure the delay of a future event, but the time by which the apheta is carried to the center of the setting, increases or decreases, by reason of the horary times of the place of the planet, which, or whose rays, retard or more quickly propel the descending apheta, and by reason of the distance by which the same planet is distant from the western cardinal point. For the rays or bodies of planets, which are before the Apheta and between the western cardinal point, do not set, but if they are benefic and opposing, then they inhibit the fall of the apheta progressing to the west, and add years, months, and days to it. Conversely, if they are malefic, they more quickly and prematurely push the apheta tending to the western cardinal point, and subtract years, months, and days from it: Mercury, however, to whichever it is joined, will help them. This direction is called ὡριμαία, because besides the time of progression, it also observes the gifts and spoils of the places opposing the falling Apheta. But how much they add or subtract is gathered from the parts of each position. For as many horary times as there are for each part, that is, of the planet adding or subtracting, diurnal by day, nocturnal by night, so many years are signified: which number, indeed, when a benefic planet is found in the ascendant, is to be added entirely to the years collected by the progression of the Apheta to the west: or is to be subtracted from them, if it is malefic and found in the ascendant. But if such a planet is not in the east, as many hours as the adding or subtracting planet is distant from the ascendant, so many parts of the horary times recede or accede, so that at the setting it comes to nothing, which is to be added to the predicted time, or to be subtracted from it: which matter, otherwise obscure, we will make clearer by an exemplary discussion. In our example, since the Sun is found in the eighth place and in a masculine sign, and finally in a paternal hexagon of Saturn exercising the right of the diurnal triplicity in the part of the Sun, according to the opinion of the Arabs, we could not undeservedly pronounce it the Apheta, unless we thought the horoscoping part to be far preferable in this dominion, and that by the authority of Ptolemy, who expressly denies the dominion of life to planets residing in the eighth house as an idle place. However, for the sake of teaching, let us imagine it to be the moderator of life placed in the western hemisphere, since in examples we look not so much at the truth of the matter as at a clear exposition of the rules. First, therefore, according to Ptolemy's rule to be explained below, the equinoctial times by which the Sun revolves to the setting must be inquired. The distance of the Sun from the culmination of the sky is 56 parts, 17 scruples, 14, and the horary times...

[Critique of Regiomontanus's Method]
The difference here is that he did not provide the rationale for the operations, which we see in Alfonso's tables. Consequently, unless one is a very skilled mathematician, one must perpetually adhere to Regiomontanus's rule and tables, which he deliberately did so that people would be servants of his book, for which he was justly criticized by my father. For a person is liable to error in three ways. First, if some table is faulty in part. Second, if you somehow misunderstand the rule, which easily happens amidst so many variations of northern latitude, southern latitude, right ascension, oblique ascension, nocturnal or diurnal arcs, of the whole or of the half in the descending or ascending half, above or below the earth. For this reason, in my judgment, the best is a large solid sphere, or a large planisphere, made precisely from brass, etc. Thus, Cardan, though many praised the method of directing by the most learned Regiomontanus, scarcely approved of it due to the difficulty of operation, and in his later years, being confirmed in the truth of the art, he seems rarely or never to have used it. But to discuss these matters at greater length is not our purpose, for we aim not so much to explain what is true in this matter as to provide a clear method of directing. First, then, to begin with the author's method of directing, we are admonished here, above all, to diligently ascertain in which part of the sky the significator planet is situated, whose varied position in different places causes us to attend now to the ascensions of the sphere, now to those of the climate in which we are situated, when collecting times. For if the significator is placed in the eastern angle, according to the ascensions of the climate; if it holds the western angle, according to the descensions of the climate; if finally it occupies the midheaven or the imum coeli, the times of future events must be measured and calculated according to the right ascensions of the sphere. Therefore, if you wish to direct the significator located in the ascendant to some place of the subsequent promittor, subtract the oblique ascensions of the significator from the oblique ascensions of the promittor, that is, subtract the beginning of the arc from the end: for what remains will show the arc of direction. For example, if the Sun from Capricorn makes a square aspect to the 12th part of Aries, and Jupiter is placed in the ending degree of Cologne, holding the fifth part of Pisces, and is to be directed to the square rays of the Sun, first you will seek the oblique ascension of the promittor, that is, the 12th part of Aries, from the table calculated for latitude 51 degrees (for such is the altitude of the north pole of Cologne), and you will find it to be 5 degrees, 8 minutes. Then in a similar way, take the oblique ascension of the significator, namely the 5th part of Pisces, which is 349 degrees, 2 minutes. Third, subtract the latter ascension, namely that of the significator, which is 349 degrees, 2 minutes, from the former ascension, that is, of the promittor, which is 5 degrees, 8 minutes, accommodating a full revolution or 360 degrees; for this must always be done whenever in physical calculation the lower exceeds the higher and therefore cannot be subtracted from it. This done, there will remain 16 degrees, 6 minutes of the sought direction. But if the significator was in the angle of the west, subtract the oblique descension of the significator from the oblique descension of the promittor, and the times of direction will remain. Nor is it otherwise what the author prescribes, that the oblique ascension of the point diametrically opposite the place of the significator (for the Arabs call this the nadir) should be subtracted from the oblique ascension of the point which is diametrically opposite the place of the promittor. For in an oblique sphere, the ascension of a sign is the descension of the opposite sign, and conversely, the descension of a sign is the ascension of the opposite sign, as in the previous example: If the Sun is in the western angle, and is to be directed to a ray: first, the descension of the promittor, that is, the 12th part of Aries, must be sought, or what is the same, the oblique ascension of the 12th part of the opposite sign, that is, Libra, must be found, which is 196 degrees, 55 minutes. Then similarly, the descension of the significator, that is, the 5th part of Pisces, must be extracted, that is, the ascension of the opposite sign, the 5th part of Virgo, which is 144 degrees, 40 minutes, which, subtracted from the former, leaves the sought times of direction, 52 degrees, 15 minutes. Finally, if the significator is in the midheaven or imum coeli, the right ascension of the significator must be subtracted from the right ascension of the promittor, so that the sought times of direction emerge. Example: In the same altitude of the region, 51 degrees, the culminating point of a certain nativity was 16 degrees of Scorpio, the significator of honor and mastery, which I wish to direct to the Sun, that is, to the promittor, which was in 9 degrees of Leo. Therefore, subtract the right ascension of the significator, which is 107 degrees, 22 minutes, from the right ascension of the promittor, which is 131 degrees, 27 minutes, and there remain 24 degrees, 14 minutes, the sought direction of the Midheaven to the trine of the Sun. The operation is to be performed in precisely the same way whenever the significator holds the Imum Coeli. All approved masters agree that Aphetas existing in the angles are to be directed in this way, and Ptolemy has often admonished this. Likewise, Hermes in his 25th enunciation says: "The progression of the ruler, when it is placed in the midheaven, make it by the ascensions of the sphere; but when it is constituted in the ascendant, by the ascensions of the climate." 2. So far concerning the method of directing the significator situated in the angles. In the following, he explains what should be followed if it is found outside the angles, namely, both the ascensions of the climate and of the sphere must be taken, and at the same time mixed together by tempering. Here, above all, he warns that it must be ascertained whether the significator is above or below the earth. This done, the distance of the significator from the Midheaven or Imum Coeli must be investigated in this way: If the Apheta, being above the earth, is in the eastern quadrant, that is, if it has not yet reached the meridian, subtract the right ascension of the midheaven from the right ascension of the Apheta. But if it is in the western quadrant, that is, if it has passed the meridian, yet still remaining above the earth, subtract the right ascension of the Apheta from the right ascension of the Midheaven, and the diurnal distance of the Apheta from the meridian or Midheaven will remain, which, as the author prescribes, must be divided by the temporal hours of the Apheta, and indeed diurnal, so that the temporal hours of the Apheta by which it is distant from the Midheaven emerge. Similarly, if the Apheta is below the earth, you will calculate its distance from the meridian or Imum Coeli with equal ease. For if it is in the quadrant of the descending half, that is, if it is before the meridian below the earth, subtract the right ascension of the angle of the earth from the right ascension of the Apheta. But if it is in the quadrant of the ascending half, that is, if it has passed the angle of the earth, then subtract the right ascension of the Apheta from the right ascension of the angle, and its nocturnal distance from the meridian will remain, which must be divided by the nocturnal temporal hours of the significator, so that the number of the section shows the elongation of the Apheta from the angle of the earth in temporal hours. To the same end, and perhaps more easily, you will arrive if you operate through opposite points. For the distance of a place from the Imum Coeli is equal to the distance by which the point diametrically opposite the said place...

[Calculating Direction in the Ascending Hemisphere]
Let the apheta be constituted in the 9th part, and the square rays of Saturn, to which it is to be directed, be in the 6th part. The angle of the Midheaven is 15 degrees. The right ascension of the apheta or Sun is 311 degrees, 27 minutes. The right ascension of the Midheaven is 279 degrees, 48 minutes, which, subtracted from the right ascension of the apheta, leaves its distance from the Midheaven as 31 degrees, 39 minutes, which was to be sought first. Then I want to inquire into the hourly times of the apheta or Sun traversing the 9th part of Aquarius, and I see in the table of the quantity of days under the altitude of the pole of 51 degrees, directly opposite the 9th part, 7 hours, 35 minutes, which I multiply by 24, making the hourly times 18 hours, 58 minutes, and indeed nocturnal, because it is from the southern signs. But because we need diurnal hourly times, I subtracted these nocturnal times from 30 parts, and immediately the diurnal times of 11 degrees, 2 minutes appeared, by which I divided the distance of the apheta from the Midheaven, that is, 31 degrees, 39 minutes, and I extracted 2 temporal hours, 52 minutes, by which the apheta is distant from the Midheaven. Now, in order to have the significator of the direct circle, from the right ascension of the rays of Saturn, namely, striking the sixth part of Pisces, which is 337 degrees, 48 minutes, I subtracted the right ascension of the apheta, which is 311 degrees, 27 minutes, and there remained the significator of the direct circle, 28 degrees, 21 minutes. For the significator of the oblique circle, from the oblique ascension of the rays of Saturn, which is 349 degrees, 30 minutes, I subtracted the oblique ascension of the apheta, which is 335 degrees, 10 minutes, and there remained the significator of the region, 14 degrees, 20 minutes. Therefore, the difference of the significators is 3 parts, which, divided by 6, yielded 0 parts, 30 minutes, or half of one part, to be multiplied by the temporal hours by which the significator is distant from the meridian, that is, by 2 hours, 52 minutes. This done, the hourly times of 1 degree, 26 minutes resulted as the equation, to be subtracted from the significator of the direct circle, for the reason that it is greater than the significator of the climate. This done, the sought direction remained 27 degrees, 54 minutes. This process of the author plainly depends on the rule of proportions: For that he orders the difference of the significators to be divided by 6, and the number of the section to be multiplied by the number of temporal hours by which the significator is distant from the Midheaven, is the same as if he had proposed these numbers in the rule of proportions in the usual way, thus: In six temporal hours the direction varies (to repeat the same example) by 3 parts, how much will the same direction vary in 2 temporal hours, 52 minutes, by which the apheta recedes from the meridian? Temporal hours: 6. Difference of significators: 3 parts. Temporal hours by which apheta is distant from Midheaven: 2 hours, 52 minutes. Furthermore, since in the process of the rule of proportions we not only divide the number generated from the mutual product of the second and third by the first, but also divide the second by the first, and correctly multiply the number of the section by the third, so as to arrive at the fourth and unknown, it is clear why the author orders the difference of the significators to be divided by 6, and the number of the section to be multiplied by the temporal hours by which the apheta is distant from the cardine, so that the equation of the direction may result. But you will elicit this same equation more certainly and much more expeditiously if, in the rule of proportions, you place the semi-diurnal or semi-nocturnal arc of the significator in the first place, and in the second place you place the difference of the significators. Finally, in the third place, you establish the distance of the significator from the cardine. For with the operation of the rule completed, the fourth number will show the equation to be added to or subtracted from the significator of the sphere, as the ratio of the calculation itself demands. As in the example above, from the tables of ascensions, or even, if you please, from the table of the quantity of days, you will find the semi-diurnal arc of the apheta to be 66 degrees, 4 minutes. Say then: in the space of 66 degrees, 4 minutes, the direction varies by 3 parts; how much will it vary in 31 minutes, by which the place of the apheta is removed from the apex of the sky? It makes 1 degree, 26 minutes, as above. But if the significator is between the horoscopus and the Midheaven, the operation must be performed in exactly the same way, except that in such a case, for the apheta, just as nocturnal local hours are used, so also are semi-nocturnal arcs. Therefore, I believe no example is needed here. From these, the author's opinion regarding the direction of the significator residing in the ascending hemisphere is clear. The method of directing the apheta or significator residing in the descending hemisphere, which is the arc from the angle of the earth to the Midheaven, calculated through the seventh house, follows. The canon of operation here does not differ from the former, except that, as is also clear from the text, where we used ascensions in the ascending hemisphere, here in the descending hemisphere, descensions must be used, or, which is the same, the work must be instituted precisely by the ascensions of the opposite points. For example, let the Imum Coeli be 15 degrees, 0 minutes, and the apheta or significator be in 15 degrees, constituted to be directed to the body of Mercury placed in 15 degrees, Virgo. And since the apheta is found below the earth and in the descending hemisphere, therefore, by operating through opposite points and nocturnal hourly times, we will reach the true goal. The right ascension of the apheta is 137 degrees, 29 minutes. The right ascension of the Imum Coeli is 106 degrees, 17 minutes. The distance of the apheta from the cardine is 31 degrees, 12 minutes. But the nocturnal semi-arc of the apheta (for the apheta resides below the earth) is 68 degrees, 45 minutes, and its nocturnal hourly times are 11 degrees, 28 minutes, or in total 688 minutes, by which I divided the distance of the apheta from the Imum Coeli, which is 31 degrees, 12 minutes, that is, 1872 first minutes, and I produced 2 hours, 43 minutes, by which temporal hours the apheta is removed from the cardine. From this, I sought the difference of the significators in the following way. The right descension of the promissor, that is, the right ascension of 5 degrees, is 346 degrees, 12 minutes. The right descension of the apheta, that is, the right ascension of 15 degrees, is 317 degrees, 27 minutes. The significator of the sphere is 28 degrees, 43 minutes. The oblique descension of the promissor is 353 degrees, 34 minutes. The oblique descension of the apheta is 338 degrees, 46 minutes. The significator of the climate is 14 degrees, 48 minutes, which I subtracted from the significator of the sphere, and there remained the difference of the significators, 13 degrees, 55 minutes, which I divided by 6, and I extracted the number of the section, 2 degrees, 19 minutes, which I multiplied by the hours by which the apheta is distant from the Imum Coeli, that is, by 2 hours, 43 minutes, and I produced 6 degrees, 18 minutes, which is the equation to be subtracted from the significator of the sphere exceeding the significator of the climate. This done, the sought direction remained 22 degrees, 25 minutes. The same goal is reached by operating through the nocturnal semi-arc of the apheta. Arrangement of numbers for the Rule of Proportion: 1. The semi-nocturnal arc of the apheta is 68 degrees, 45 minutes. The difference of the significators is 13 degrees, 55 minutes. Or thus: 13. The distance of the apheta from the cardine is 31 degrees, 12 minutes. 31. 684. The second number multiplied by the third, yields 4345908, divided by 684, yields the equation of 6 degrees, 18 minutes, to be subtracted, as said, from the significator of the sphere, so that the direction of 22 degrees, 25 minutes, which we proposed to find, remains. Finally, the converse direction, or in the preceding, is done in the same way by which the direct is perfected, with this one observation: that ascensions and descensions are calculated in the circle of position of the promissor and not of the significator. For just as the promissor is carried to the place of the significator, so here the significator is understood to be led to the place of the promissor. Therefore, if the promissor is placed in the Midheaven, we will subtract the right ascensions of the promissor from the right ascensions of the significator. But if the same has been the horoscopus, we will subtract the ascensions of the climate of the promissor from the ascensions of the climate of the significator. Finally, if the promissor has held the angle of the west, we will deduce its descensions from the descensions of the significator, so that the sought direction remains. What, however, should be followed if none of the cardines holds the promissor, but the same is constituted between the said places, can be clear from those canons which are set forth in the exposition of the direct direction, namely, both ascensions or descensions are to be taken, and at the same time proportionally mixed, as we have said. From these, the author's opinion regarding the deduction of Aphetic places is clear, in which, like Ptolemy, he despised

[Planetary Latitudes and Directions]
Planetary latitudes, which are more observed in this matter, have accustomed to evidently vary the times of directions. Therefore, if anyone, following this author's method of directing, also wishes to consider latitudes, they must use the tables of Johannes Blanchinus, by the aid of which the ascensions of all places of the sky deviating from the Ecliptic are most easily found. The tables of directions by Regiomontanus also provide the same and more copiously, but their use is more difficult and admits only a well-practiced calculator. Blanchinus's tables were also composed in Italy. For other regions, as far as the right sphere is concerned, it satisfies all. As for the oblique sphere, everyone must construct one for themselves with the aid of Regiomontanus's tables for the altitude of their region. The author's method of directing is not very dissimilar from the tradition of Ptolemy, according to whose opinion the times of directions are collected in this manner. First and foremost, the Apheta and the remaining significators, whose progressions principally signify the times of events, must be observed. Similarly, the places of the planets or promissors, that is, the radiations of the stars occurring, must be described and noted. For the sake of avoiding obscurity, it was pleasing to use these words very generally in this place, so that whatever is said here about the deduction of the Apheta or the lord, you may also understand it concerning all other significators of events, so that by the name Apheta, we understand every significator, and by the name Anareta, every promissor. These things being so, then the distance of both the Apheta and the promissors from the midheaven must be taken, if the Apheta is above the earth; or their difference from the imum coeli must be investigated, if the Apheta is found below the horizon. After this, the horary times of individual places, diurnal if the place of the Apheta is above the earth, but nocturnal if below the earth, must be collected, and then the distance of the Apheta from the cardine, just found by the horary times of the Apheta, must be divided by the horary times, so that the temporal hours by which the Apheta is removed from the cardine may result: all of which will be accomplished according to the method abundantly explained in the exposition of the text. Finally, the horary times of the Anareta must be multiplied by the hours by which the Apheta is distant from the cardine of the sky, and what is produced, according to the following cautions, must be added to or subtracted from the difference or distance of the Anareta from the cardine of the sky. The number that results from this will be the number of parts and minutes of the direction, or it will be the number of years, months, and days, after which the promissor will come to the significator: indeed, each degree thus computed counts as a year, and each minute as a month, and each single second as six days and two hours. Rules of Prohairesis: If the Apheta is above the earth, subtract the produced number from the direct difference of the promissor (here we call the difference of the place from the cardine the distance) if the Apheta is between the ascendant and the Midheaven. If both are between the Midheaven and the seventh house, the direct difference of the promissor must be subtracted from the produced number. But if the Apheta is below the earth between the imum coeli and the seventh house, then, as in the first case, the product must be subtracted from the difference of the promissor. But if the Apheta is between the imum coeli and the horoscope, the difference of the promissor, as was done in the second case, is subtracted from the product. Finally, if the Apheta is in the eastern quadrant, and the promissor is in the western quadrant, whether above or below the earth, then the difference of the Apheta must be added to the product. From these, it is clear that the opposite quadrants of the sky correspond to each other completely. Therefore, when the Apheta is found below the earth, with opposite points, just as if the Apheta were above the earth, you will perform the operation to the same end, perhaps with less effort. And this is the reason why Cardanus, in this whole matter, teaches that no more than 4 or rather 3 differences, which follow, are found, which is true, if, as I said, the opposite points are attended to. If the Apheta is in the Midheaven, nothing is added to the difference of the ascensions, but simply, as has been said, the direction is made by the ascensions of the sphere. 2. Apheta between the Midheaven and the horoscope: the product is subtracted from the difference of the promissor. 3. Both Apheta and Anareta in the western quadrant: then the difference is subtracted from the product. Apheta in the eastern quadrant, Anareta in the western quadrant: then the difference is combined with the product. Example of a significator between the Midheaven and the horoscope. I wish to direct the Moon first to the trine radiation of Mars, and then to the body of Saturn, so that the Moon, initially inimical to Mars, has the first place or the place of the significator, and the rays of Mars and Saturn have the place of the promissor. Since the Moon is below the earth, we will therefore operate more conveniently through opposite places falling into the eastern quadrant of the world, that is, we will make the place of the Moon in 27 degrees 52 minutes of Leo, and the rays of Mars in 28 degrees 21 minutes of Virgo, and finally the place of Saturn in 26 degrees 42 minutes of Libra. And since the place of the Moon is understood to be between the horoscope and the Midheaven, I therefore first subtracted the right ascension of the Midheaven from the right ascension of the place which we have for the Moon's place, and there remained a difference of the Moon of 26 degrees 11 minutes, which I divided by the diurnal horary times of the Moon's place, which are 18 degrees 21 minutes, and the number of the section showed me 1 hour 27 minutes of the Moon's preceding distance from the Midheaven. Then I subtracted the right ascension of the Midheaven from the right ascension of the malefics, and there remained a direct distance, of Mars's trine 54 degrees 35 minutes, and of Saturn 80 degrees 52 minutes. Finally, I multiplied the diurnal horary times of the trine radiation of Mars, that is, 15 degrees 7 minutes, by the temporal hours 1 hour 27 minutes, by which the Moon's place is distant from the Midheaven, and the number produced was 21 degrees 57 minutes, which, since the Moon's place is above the earth in the eastern quadrant, I subtracted from the difference of Mars's trine radiation, that is, from 54 degrees 35 minutes, and there remained 32 degrees 38 minutes, that is, 32 years, 7 months, and 18 days: after which time the body of the Moon passes through the trine of Mars. We produced the times of direction of 59 degrees 34 minutes, by which the Moon moves to Saturn, by exactly the same form of computation. This is Ptolemy's formula for directing, which, somewhat changed and with one operation removed, we will achieve the same goal, and we will perform all directions most easily in the following way. To all Aphetas and Anaretas, first assign the difference of the right ascension from the right ascension of the Midheaven, from the table of right ascensions placed below. Then, similarly, add to these, opposite them, the horary times of each place from the table of the quantity of days: diurnal, if the Apheta is above the earth; but nocturnal, if the Apheta is below the earth. These things being thus arranged, multiply the direct difference of the Apheta or significator by the horary times of the Anareta or promissor, and then divide what is produced by the horary times of the significator, and subtract the number of the section from the direct difference of the promissor, or you will subtract this same from that, according to the fourfold.

[Calculating Directional Numbers]
The difference is that distinction explained above. For the number here is the number of the fourth direction. Let us repeat, for greater clarity, the previous example, in which the Moon is led to the trine of Mars and the body of Saturn. First, therefore, opposite these celestial places, I placed the differences of ascensions from the midheaven, and then, because the place of the significator is above the earth, I added to each its diurnal hourly times, as you see in the present description: Differences: 1. Part 26, scrup. 11 1. Part 54, scrup. 35 12. Hourly times: 1. Part 18, scrup. 2 1. Part 80, scrup. 52 1. Part 15, scrup. 7 1. Part 14, scrup. 40 Having thus set these, I multiplied the hourly times of the trine radiation of Mars, p.15.sc.7, by the difference of the rectified place, which is p.26.sc.11, and produced sixty 61, p.35.sc.45, or if you prefer, p.395.sc.45, which I divided by the hourly times of the place (namely p.18.sc.2), and extracted the section number p.21.sc.57. And because the places of Apheta and Angreta are between the ascendant and the midheaven, therefore I subtracted this product from the direct difference of the trine rays of Mars, which is p.54.sc.35, and there remained p.32.sc.38, to which correspond 32 years, 7 months, 18 days, no differently than in the above calculation. In the same way, multiplying the lunar difference by the hourly times of Saturn, we produced sixty 61, p.24.sc.11, which, divided by the hourly times of the Moon's place, yielded p.21.sc.18, to be subtracted from the difference of the same Saturn, so that the number of direction, namely p.59.sc.33, comes out. Another example: In the same nativity, if you wish to deduce the square of Saturn to the Sun, then, having described the differences of these places and their hourly times as instructed, multiply the difference of the Sun by the hourly times of the square radiation of Saturn, and the Differences of the hourly times: P. 56. scrup. 58 P.18.sc.22 P.37.sc.32 P.18.sc.42 produces sixty 171, p.45.sc.16, which, if you divide by the hourly times of the Sun, that is, by p.18.sc.22, you will elicit p.58 exactly, from which the difference of Saturn must be subtracted, because both places are contained between the western horizon and the culmination of the sky, so that the number of direction p.20.scrup.28 remains.

[Direction in Hemicycles]
From these examples, the method of directing is clear, if both the significator and the promissor are found in the hemicycle ascending to the culmination of the sky: then the entire direction is made by ascensions in the semicircle of the significator's position. For all circles of position in the ascending half are of ascensions. Similarly, if both hold the hemicycle of the world descending to the subterranean cusp, the entire direction is completed by ascensions in the hemicycle of Apheta or the significator: for all semicircles of position in the descending half are of descensions. But what is to be done if ascension is changed into descension, or descension into ascension? As if Apheta, being between the seventh house and the midheaven, is to be led to the promissor, which is between the ascendant and the midheaven? I answer, according to the opinion of Ptolemy and the author, that in such a case, first the midheaven must be led to Apheta by the descensions of Apheta's circle of position: then the promissor must be moved to the culmination of the midheaven by the ascensions of the right sphere: and finally, these two arcs of direction must be joined, so that the number of the entire direction comes forth. In the assumed nativity, directing the Sun, placed in the quadrant of the descending half of the world, to the square radiation of Mars, which falls in p.28.sc.21 of Leo, and in the quadrant of the ascending half of the world, we first described both the difference of each place from the midheaven and the hourly times, as you see on the side. Then, multiplying the difference of the Sun by the hourly times of the square of Mars, we produced sixty 1519, p.58.sc.56, which, divided by the hourly times of the Sun, yielded the distance of the square of Mars translated to the Sun's place from the midheaven, part 52.sc.12, which, when joined with the first distance of the same square of Mars, which is p.26.sc.36, makes the number of direction part 78.sc.48.

[Finding the Degree of the Zodiac]
The other place of this chapter follows, concerning finding the degree of the zodiac to which the direction of Apheta reaches in a given year of age. As in our example, where the eastern horizon falls in part 26.scrup. 44 of Libra, if it is proposed to find to what degree of the zodiac the direction of the ascendant reaches in the 40th year, 5 months, 6 days of the native's age, first take the oblique ascension of the significator, that is, of the ascendant part 26.sc.44, which is 213 parts, 55 scrup., and to this add 40 parts, 26 scrup., according to the elapsed time from the root, and you will collect 254 parts, 21 scrup., with which, entering the area of the oblique table (for the barbaric word 'arcuare' signifies this here), you will find that 28 parts, 21 scrup. of Scorpio correspond to them, where the epoch of Mars is. Therefore, the direction of the ascendant will reach that point of the zodiac when 40 years, 5 months, 6 days are completed. The rest of this place is easy, and not dissimilar to what has been said.

[Choosing Rulers of Time]
It follows how the Catholic arbiters of times are to be chosen. It seems, however, that here the divider, that is, the lord of the term, is preferred to the lord of the rays, which is contrary to Ptolemy, who attributes the principal dominion to the star or ray meeting Apheta, and makes the lord of the term a participant in its dominion. His words on this matter are found near the end of the Quadripartite construction: 'And first, indeed, time in each moderation will be given to him who occupies the Aphetic place by body or by rays. But if there is no one precisely in the Aphetic place, we will take the planet or ray immediately preceding it, until it looks at the next succeeding part. Then we will use this until the next, and similarly in others, taking into communication for governing the planetary lords of the terms.' The matter will be clearer with an exemplary discussion. In our example, the eastern horizon encompasses part 26.sc.44 of Libra, to which, since the opposite ray of Saturn almost exactly rests, therefore we constitute Saturn as the first arbiter of times, with Mars participating in the rule, according to Ptolemy's opinion, as the lord of the terms. But a little later, in part 27.sc.21, where the trine radiation of Jupiter and the Moon succeeds the diameter of Saturn.

[Algebugthar: Direction of the Ascendant]
438. DIFFERENCE. Concerning Algebugthar. And from this follows Algebugthar in nativities: it is the direction of the ascendant degree, that is, that you look at the degree of the ascendant in the term of which planet it is, you subtract the ascensions of the ascendant from the ascensions which are in the direct day of the end of the planet's term by the ascensions of the region, and what remains, you will take for each degree one year, and for every five minutes a month: and for every minute six days: and the lord of the term will be the disposer of the years, who is called the divider. After this, you will take the degrees of the term which succeeds it, you will also convert them into degrees of ascensions, and whatever it is, you will take for each degree one year, and for every five minutes a month, and for every minute six days, and the lord of the term will be the divider and disposer of those years. Similarly, you will proceed with every term of the lord by succession until the end of life: and if it is in the term of any planet: the planet or its rays will be participants in the division: this division is called Algebugthar. Concerning the direction of the ascendant to the planetary terms, which the Arabs call Algebuthar. Here consider the horoscoping degree, and observe to which planet's terms it refers, and how far the terms of that planet extend. Then, having found the ascensions of the climate for both the ascendant degree and the extreme part of the terms, subtract the former from the latter, and the sought direction of the horoscope to the proposed term will remain. For example, in the assumed nativity, in which we suppose the elevation of the vertex to be 41 parts, the horoscope is 26 parts, 44 minutes of Libra, which, according to Ptolemy's arrangement of terms, Mars presides over. The same Mars has dominion over the terms at the beginning of Scorpio, and extends to the end of the sixth part of the same Scorpio. The ascension of the climate of the horoscope is 213 parts, 55 minutes. The ascension of the climate at the same elevation of the extreme part of Mars's terms, 439. that is, 6 parts of Scorpio, is 225 parts, 46 minutes, from which, if the oblique ascension of the horoscope is subtracted, there remain 11 parts, 51 minutes, that is, 11 years, 10 months, 6 days, of which time Mars is the lord. The immediately succeeding terms assigned to Jupiter extend to 14 parts of Scorpio, whose oblique ascension is found to be 236 parts, 3 minutes, from which if you subtract the ascension of the extreme part of the immediately preceding terms of Mars, there will remain 10 parts, 11 minutes, that is, 6 years, 3 months, 12 days, the time of Jupiter's governance, which, combined with the time assigned to Mars a little earlier, makes the native's age 32 years, 1 month, 18 days. In this way, the direction of the ascendant to the end of life is to be continued to foresee illnesses and impediments that will occur to the native in the body. You can, if you wish, form a table from which the progression of the ascendant to the planetary terms can be most easily derived for each year, in this way: For the beginning of the first year of the nativity, assign the horoscoping degree at the head of the table. Then take the ascension of the horoscope in the climate, to which for each succeeding year you add single degrees in order, and what results from this, search for it in the area of the same table of ascensions, and observe to which place of the zodiac it corresponds: for that will claim the right of division or disposition for itself in that year. In our example, for the first current year, 26 parts, 44 minutes of Libra are to be assigned, to whose climate ascension, that is, 213 parts, 55 minutes, if you add one degree of the equinoctial, you will form the oblique ascension of 214 parts, 55 minutes for the second year, to which correspond in the table 27 parts, 31 minutes of Libra. By such a continuous addition of equinoctial parts to the ascension of the horoscope, you will easily extend the entire order of parts to be inserted into the table for each year of the native's life, with the help of your climate table, until the end of the native's life. Finally, to the parts of the zodiac found in this way, the lords of the terms, who bear the appellation of divider, are to be ascribed from Ptolemy's table of terms, or, if you prefer, from the Egyptians, as is evident in the following example. These precepts concerning the horoscope can and should be referred in a similar way to the deduction of the positions of the other significators in their circles. 440.
