[Lunar Qualities and Malefics/Benefics]
It could not be otherwise than that in the Moon, humidity would significantly exceed heat, since the humid is cast down by a double heat, namely its own and the Sun's, while the hot is cast down only by the Sun's heat. But someone might ask, since the Moon, when full of light, does not mitigate the cold of winter, but rather intensifies it, how can it be that it heats by borrowed light from the Sun? For example: When the luminaries conjoin in Capricorn, the Moon, departing from the conjunction, is continuously more illuminated by the Sun and approaches closer to our zenith, until, having completed almost a semicircle, that is, 185 parts, it is fully ignited, and traversing Cancer, it becomes closest to our dwellings. There, we observe that the Moon, absorbing the Sun's light in this manner and approaching closer and closer to our zenith, not only does not warm our air but even cools it more. Therefore, it can be doubted whether it heats by light drawn from the Sun. To this hesitation, we must respond that the presence of the illuminated Moon brings us cold not by itself, but by another circumstance. For it very often happens that people consider that to be the cause of some effect which is by no means the cause. For the waxing Moon raises many vapors from the earth, which, being very cold, it is not surprising if they make the air colder, especially since the Moon's heat always remains weaker than to be able to consume the abundance of vapors. For the same reason, the Sun, receding from the Tropic of Capricorn, cools more and makes winter more severe. Afterwards, however, advancing from Capricorn, having become higher, it projects straighter and therefore stronger rays towards us, which gradually consume more and more of the exhaled vapors, and thus produce heat. Let these things be said about the primary qualities of the stars. Next, let us show what naturally follows from these qualities. And first, the krasis or mixture of the stars causes some stars to be called benefics, and some malefics, or as they are called today, fortunates and infortunates. For those that are excessively cold, like Saturn, and those that are excessively hot, like Mars, are called intemperate, malefic, and unfortunate. But astrologers call Saturn the greater infortune because of its very bad temperament, and Mars the lesser infortune because of its lesser dyscrasia. Those stars, however, in whose krasis heat dominates humidity, are called benefics and favorable to human nature. But just as there are degrees of krasis, so there are degrees of benefics. For those in which heat perfectly dominates humidity, as in Jupiter, are most benefic because of their excellent mixture; those in which heat moderately contains humidity, as in Venus, are moderately temperate and benefic; finally, those in which overflowing humidity is minimally restrained due to the scarcity of heat, as in the Moon, are judged to be little temperate and benefic. From these, it can be clearly seen: First, why Jupiter is called the greater fortune, and Venus the lesser fortune. Secondly, that the Moon, shining with a full orb, if it then acquires enough heat in proportion to its humidity, brings the greatest felicities; but when empty and weakly heating, it portends calamities and miseries. Moreover, if Saturn is conjoined with Mars, it acquires excessive cold; if with the Sun or Mars, excessive dryness. When thus affected, it is to be judged intemperate and malefic. But the same Saturn, when conjoined with Jupiter and Venus or the Moon, becomes hot and humid. Therefore, it is then to be considered temperate and benefic. The Sun, leader, prince, and moderator of the other luminaries, the mind of the world and its temperance, although it is the greatest fortune of all that are seen in the sky because of its immense benefits and excellent temperament, is nevertheless numbered among the stars of ambiguous nature, and therefore sometimes among the malefics and infortunates. These names, indeed, never truly apply to it from a true cause, but there are four principal reasons why it is sometimes so named, as Cardan relates. First, because it obscures and impedes the other stars with its light. Pliny, Book 2, Chapter 18, says: "The Sun and conjunctions of the extreme orbit into dark obscurity." From these words, we gather three ways in which stars are obscured. First, the Sun, which is seen alone wherever it may be in the world, from which it also received its name; and of this mode, we speak here. Secondly, the points of the Ecliptic, or nodes, in which the luminaries fail. Lastly, the extreme additions of the circles, which, although they do not entirely obscure the stars, nevertheless render them more obscure due to the great distance. The second reason is that, when conjoined with malefics, it fosters their powers, as will be said below concerning the Anaretic places. The third is that, when joined with fixed stars, it sometimes tends to change its nature in some way. For example, who is unaware that the Sun's vapors are ignited at the rising of the Dog Star? The effects of which star are felt most amply on earth. The seas boil at its rising, wines ferment in cellars, things move.

[Planetary Appearances and Conjunctions]
The difference is that the Sun, revolving from the Sun to the very bottom, can be separated by a space of unknown things, and in that interval of time, when the epicycle once permeates, they are twice conjoined with the Sun, first by direct motion in the highest apogee of the epicycle, then by retrograde motion in the lowest apogee, all these four forms receive their risings and settings. First, hence, as the Moon shines forth in its evening rising, when it has proceeded a little from the conjunction of the Sun and from the highest apogee of the epicycle, and moves towards its evening station, from which afterwards, when it is about to seek another conjunction at the lowest apogee of the epicycle, it is hidden by the Sun's rays not long before the perigee of the epicycle, in its evening setting. Therefore, in the eastern semicircle of the epicycle, where they descend from its apogee to its perigee, they are called Hesperian and following, contrary to the three superior planets. Then, ascending from this place to the morning station, and not far from the perigee of the epicycle, they rise in the morning rising, having left the Sun's rays: finally, having passed the morning station, when they are again going to the highest apogee and seeking the Sun's conjunction again, they are a little distant from the apogee of the epicycle, they are hidden in the morning setting, and afterwards they proceed to the same turns. Therefore, in the meantime, while they appear through the western semicircle in the morning before the Sun's rising, they are called preceding, like the three superior planets. In an exemplary discussion, we will make the otherwise obscure matter much easier. Let the epicycle be AC EG: The highest apogee or its longest distance from the center of the world is A, where the middle of progression or direct motion is, and the first conjunction of the Sun and Venus: Evening rising. B, from where Venus descends in the epicycle, and diminishes its progression. The first or evening station C, from which it begins to retrograde. The evening setting occurs at point D. The middle of regression and the lowest point of the small circle of the apogee shows point E, under the 15th part of Taurus, where the star is again with the Sun. The morning rising is F. And the morning or second station occurs at G, from where it begins to progress. Point H is the morning setting, from which it proceeds most rapidly to the Sun and to repeat the said turns. The center of the world is T. The body is placed on the epicycle, and the quadrant of the zodiac rests on it, under which circle the center of the epicycle K, together with the line of the Sun's mean motion, revolves from west to Aries, the star running through the ambit of the epicycle. Two lines from the center of the world T through points G and G, erected to the zodiac, touching both epicycles, indicate the stations, as has been said. While the star descends from point B to point D, it is called Hesperus: while it ascends from sign F to sign H, it is called Lucifer. In the remaining spaces around the apogees, having lost both surnames, the name Venus is simply used. In the Ephemerides, the syllables Or. or Occ. are written under the notes of the five planets in the right column of the Ephemerides, showing when the planet is oriental or occidental. What position the planet has in the epicycle cannot be better judged than from the corrected anomaly of commutation, which in the five wandering stars is always counted from the top of the epicycle towards the east or through the consequent signs. For if it is nothing, it will indicate the planet culminating in the middle of its progression: if it has completed the semicircle exactly, it will indicate it pushed down to the bottom of the epicycle. Finally, it will show that it is lingering in the eastern semicircle of the epicycle: if greater, in the western. The knowledge of this matter contributes greatly to knowing whether the planet is free from the Sun's rays, or whether it is oppressed by them, as we taught a little while ago. The planet appearing before sunrise, oriental dexter, is called so not by reason of its region, but because it exists on the right side of the Sun. Similarly, in the evening, setting after sunset, it is called occidental sinister with respect to the Sun, because it sets after the Sun, and is found on the left side of the world from the Sun. Here you must observe which parts of the world are right, and which are left: concerning which distinction there are three opinions of authors. The first is that of the author and astronomers, who call the eastern part of the world left, and the western right. Pliny, book 2, chapter 8, concerning the world running to the west, says: "But the paths of all wandering stars, and that they move contrary to the world, that is, to the left, while it always rushes to the right." For astronomers, contemplating the sky, turn their faces to the south, where the course of the stars is most evident; for the motion of the stars near the poles is scarcely felt. Contrary to this is the opinion of geographers, who call the east right, and the west left. These, looking at the sky, turn their feet towards the pole, whose altitude they scrutinize. The last is that of the poets, who call the entire hemisphere from the equinox to the north right, and the other left. In the second of the Metamorphoses, Sol instructs Phaeton with these verses: "Let not the right turn to the twisted serpent: Nor let the left lead to the pressed altar." Thus Lucan writes that the southern shadows of those who came from Arabia to Pompey's aid were changed into northern ones: "Arabs, you come into an unknown world, marveling that the shadows of the trees do not go to the left." For before they had left the torrid zone, the shadows followed them, but after leaving it, they preceded them. What he says, that the two inferior planets, when they are occidental, assume three superior ones, and thus become stronger, seems to contradict Ptolemy, who taught that the five oriental planets are universally stronger. Even if this is true, nevertheless it is consistent that the inferior planets also sometimes rejoice in their setting. For since they have a mean motion common with the Sun, it can happen that they are faster than the Sun and by their nature become occidental: for this reason, the occidental Moon universally rejoices, but the three superior planets are always weakened by their setting due to the slowness of their motion. CONCERNING WHAT HAPPENS TO PLANETS TOWARDS EACH OTHER. Their being towards each other, that is, the same as conjunction, that is, when two planets are in two signs aspecting each other, and the lighter one is in its sign with fewer degrees than the heavier one is in its sign: if there are six degrees or less between them, then it is said that the lighter one goes to the conjunction of the heavier one: and when their degrees are equal, their conjunction is perfected: when it has passed it, it will be separated from it: this conjunction is called a conjunction of longitude. A conjunction of latitude, however, is when two planets are joined by latitude. And if there is an application of conjunction, their latitude must be equal in one part: and if there is a conjunction from opposition, their latitudes must be equal, so that the latitude of one is ascending in the north, and that of the other descending in the north: or one ascending in the south, and the other descending in the south: or if there is an application from any of the other aspects, that is, that the latitude of one is northern ascending, and that of the other southern descending: and vice versa in the south: and this is the application of latitude that has been mentioned. 2. And when one planet separates from another and is not joined to any other planet, as long as it is in the same sign, it is said to be void of course. 3. And when a planet is in a sign, and no other planet aspects this sign, as long as the other planet is in the same sign; it is called feral or wild. 4. And when a lighter planet separates from a heavier planet, and is joined to another, it transfers the nature of the first to the second. 5. A planet also transfers nature in another way, that is, when a lighter planet is joined to a heavier planet, and that heavier planet is again joined to another heavier planet, then the middle one transfers.

[Planetary Debilities and Afflictions]
346. Or they may be in opposition to their dignities or powers, or descending in the south or meridian; or falling from angles, or from succeeding angles, or in houses, or in cadent houses. Or they may be in the via combusta, which is the middle of the 15th degree of Libra and the first half of Scorpio, or they may be joined to a retrograde, impeded, or cadent planet, even if received. Or they may be the three superior planets occidental to the Sun, or in feminine quarters. And the debility of the Sun is when it is in feminine signs, or in feminine quarters, unless it is in the ninth house. And the debility of the three inferior planets is when they are oriental, or in masculine quarters. I. This describes a catalog of places in which planets increase or decrease their strength, are fortunate or unfortunate. And what it means can be clearly understood from the text. This astrological phrase (that they are cadent from them) should be noted here. A planet with any star, if it occupies the same sign, or is distant from it by 4, 7, or 10 signs (in the order of the signs), is said to be in an angle from it. But if it has traversed the second, fifth, eighth, or eleventh sign in order from it, it is in a succedent house; if it occupies the 3rd, 6th, 9th, or 12th, it is said to be cadent from it. Likewise, in this place, a superior planet is said to be more eminent, from which it is distant by 10 or 11 signs according to the order of the signs; as in my example, it is exalted above and traversing the sign. For my example is the tenth sign from Sagittarius. In this way, the MC angle is exalted above the ascendant. We will see the remaining forms of exaltations, or as they are called, elevations, below at the end of the following difference. This is the 2. Obsession is when two stars or two rays in some way enclose one star, with no other ray intervening, as if it is in the 10th part, 4th in the 11th, in the 12th. Jupiter is afflicted by being obsessed by two infortunes. Likewise, if Saturn is in the 6th part of Cancer, in the 8th part of the same Cancer, in the 10th part. The Moon will be said to be surrounded by the body of Saturn and the square ray of Mars. Likewise, if it is in such a figure: the Moon in, and in, which transmits its trine radiation into Leo, and its diameter into Libra, surrounds the Moon with its evil rays. In the same way, signs are also said to be obsessed, when, namely, one malefic is found at the beginning and another at the end. But when the Sun or a benefic aspects a planet or sign that is obsessed with a sextile or trine aspect, so that the aspect is within the orbs, then through such an aspect the obsession is resolved. Therefore, when malefics have obsessed the Moon or the horoscope, with no benefic shining upon the obsessed, they say that the native will have a short life. That it says nocturnal planets are stronger below the earth during the day than above the earth, we showed above in the first difference that this is contrary to Ptolemy's opinion. 3. As for the via combusta or Milky Way, Cardan in our century determines it to be in the northern part from the 19th degree of Gemini to the 30th degree of the same. And in the southern half from the 5th degree of Sagittarius to the 15th degree of the same. And again, because it is divided there from the 23rd degree of Sagittarius to the 4th degree. Of the great stars outside the zodiac, 4 are found in the vicinity of the Milky Way, namely the right side of Perseus, Capella in Auriga, Vega, the tail of Cygnus, and that which is in the 2nd degree, 18th minute, 12th second of Sagittarius with a southern latitude of 4 degrees, of the second magnitude, called Antares or the heart of Scorpio, which is important to observe. For every star in the Milky Way, or in its vicinity, somewhat disturbs the intellect and causes many other things. And so much for the text. Hyspalensis, whose opinion many follow, in examining the strengths of planets, observes only the principal places of this catalog. First, he considers whether the planet is combust or not: Second, whether it is direct, swift, or slow: Third, whether it is placed in its splendors, such as domicile, exaltation, trigon, term, or decan: Fourth, whether it is in any aspect of benefics, or in a good aspect of benefics: Fifth and finally, how it is placed in the figure of the heavens, whether it is in an angular, succedent, or cadent house. Therefore, planets free from solar rays, direct, swift, placed in their splendors, associated with good aspects and benefics, found in angles or succedent houses, are to be judged fortunate and powerful.

[Aphetic Places and Anareta]
The fourth section. 383. P. However, they are suitable by reason of the tenth house. And the five degrees of the ultimate tenth, although they are powerless and useless with respect to the same, are nevertheless judged suitable by reason of the following eleventh house. Therefore, we must consider the 9th and 10th houses without subtracting the five parts following their end, and subtract them only from the first, seventh, and eleventh, whose subsequent houses, namely the second, eighth, and twelfth, are not Aphetic. These are Ptolemy's Aphetic places. On Apheta: The Chaldeans call the significator and ruler of life to be moderated 'leech', but Ptolemy calls it 'kyrion zoes kai apheten', that is, the 'dimissor', from 'aphetes', because it possesses, as it were, a task from which the threads, once drawn and released, measure the fatal span of human life. Indeed, I believe that the poets' image of the three Fates, which Varro thinks are derived from 'partus' (birth) by a change of one letter, pertains here: for they are thought to bestow good or evil upon men at birth, and to moderate their lives as if spinning them. Lachesis, the spinner, provides the task, from which Clotho draws and twists the threads, which Atropos finally breaks. Therefore, I thought Lachesis signifies the Apheta, Clotho the procession of the Apheta, and Atropos the anaretic place. But as to whom this rulership and dispensation of life should be attributed, the Arabs differ much less from Ptolemy than in the constitution of the Aphetic places. The Arabs transfer the moderation of life to one of these six, namely, to the Sun or Moon, or to the degree of conjunction or prevention, or finally to the Part of Fortune or the Ascendant. But Ptolemy orders five, namely, the Ascendant, the Part of Fortune, and the ruler of these places, which of them it is convenient to choose as the rulers of life according to his opinion, the following descriptions will show clearly enough. In diurnal nativities, look at the Sun, if it is in any of the five said Aphetic places, let it be the Apheta above others. But if the Sun seems unsuitable for prolonging life due to the unsuitability of the place, then consequently, look at the Moon. And if the Moon cannot be attributed this rulership, then... 384. 3. Take the ruler, who has three of the dignities in the three places, namely: 1. The preceding conjunction, which is in the three places. DIFFERENCE: For if such a planetary ruler is in the Aphetic places, it will be given to the luminaries. But if this ruler is found in the Aphetic places, namely in the 3rd place of the Ascendant, then the Aphesis, or as they call it, the 'legium', devolves to the Ascendant. Observe that in diurnal nativities, attention must be paid to the place of the preceding conjunction, even if it immediately preceded and was closer to the nativity. For the Sun is more powerful than the others. In nocturnal nativities: 1. Make the Moon the Apheta, if it is in the Aphetic places. 2. Take the Sun, if it is in those 25 degrees that follow the center of the Ascendant. And if neither luminary can prolong life, then further: 3. Take the ruler, who has three of the five dignities in the three places, namely: 1. The place of the Ascendant. For if such a planet is in the 2nd Aphetic place, it will moderate life; if not, then in the 3rd place. 4. If the conjunction immediately preceded the nativity, take the Ascendant, because it favors the Ascendant. But if the opposition immediately preceded, take the Part of Fortune if it is in an Aphetic place; if not, then the rulership must again be deferred to the Ascendant. It should be noted that in nocturnal nativities, the opposition must be attended to, even when the conjunction was closer to the nativity, because it is sufficient, and has no power. Moreover, the place, as we have warned above, is the place of the luminary which is found above the earth at the time of the opposition. For by its 385. presence, it does not suffer its privilege to be taken away, which is that in a diurnal opposition, its place is preferred to the place of the Sun, unless it is found exactly in the west. Finally, let it be repeated here that by 5 dignities, Ptolemy understands houses, trigon, exaltation, bounds, conjunction or any other aspect, indeed even intuition and rulership, provided they agree exactly, otherwise not. Caution: If both luminaries and the ruler of their own condition (who is he who in diurnal nativities rules in the places of the Sun, the preceding conjunction, and the Ascendant, but in nocturnal nativities rules in the Moon, the preceding conjunction, and the Ascendant) are in Aphetic places, that of the luminaries is to be preferred which is of greater virtue and in a more suitable place. As in nocturnal nativities, if the Moon is in the ninth or seventh, but the Sun in the Ascendant: then the Sun is to be preferred to the Moon, and especially if it is near the degree of the Ascendant or in its dignity, but nevertheless within 25 degrees below the horizon. In diurnal nativities, if the Sun is in the tenth, and the Moon in the ninth, then the Moon will be preferred to the Sun. But if the Sun is in the tenth and the Moon in the eleventh, they will be almost equal by reason of their places: therefore, you will judge that to be preferred which is endowed with a greater prerogative. But if they still do not seem to differ notably enough, consider whether the lord of the place applies to any of them by body or by a benevolent aspect. For if the powerful lord of the Apheta's place sees the same Apheta, and especially with a good aspect, he will make the prolonger much stronger. And this is certainly the reason why the Arabs never attribute the right of moderating life to any single planet, unless another also accedes, whom they call Alcocodes, that is, one who, holding some dignity in the place of the future Apheta, moreover regards the same Apheta. However, the ruler is then finally to be preferred to both luminaries when he has two conditions. The first is that he himself is in a better Aphetic place than the luminaries. The second is that he collects three of the five prerogatives in three places, namely in the place of the Sun, the preceding conjunction, and the Ascendant: And another three in other three places, namely the place of the Moon, the preceding conjunction, and the Ascendant, and then he is called the ruler of both times. This is the law of the prolongers: it remains for us to enumerate the Anaretas in a similar order. On Anaretas: 386. DIFFERENCE. Anaretas, or 'moirai anairetikai', that is, destroying parts, are the bodies and hostile rays of malefics, which, encountering the giver of life in the progressions, cut off the life of the native, or at least portend great dangers to it. For the word 'anaireo' means the same as 'to kill', and 'anairetis' means the same as 'killer' or 'life-cutter'. Hence, they are also commonly, not so ineptly as is thought, called 'abscissor' from 'abscinding life'. However, among Ptolemy's destroying parts, I find two primary kinds: One is that which is of moderation towards the preceding signs, and has only one destroying part, namely the cusp of the western terminator, because it hides the lord of life. But the parts of the stars, either encountering or testifying, at least subtract or add something to those years which were collected by the moderator of life up to the setting, and do not destroy, because they do not impinge on an Aphetic place, but on the contrary, the Apheta is carried to the Anareta. And how much they add or subtract, a matter otherwise somewhat obscure, we will explain below with some example. The other kind of Anaretas is of that direction which is perfected towards the consequent signs, and has 16 principal Anaretas, of which the first six kill by themselves, and are the two bodies of the malefics, and their two opposite aspects, and another two squares. Of the remaining ten Anaretas, who generally do not kill by themselves, but with some condition, the first and most powerful is the square of the Apheta itself proceeding according to the succession of the signs. But the condition or rather the cause why this square kills is that these places, which were initially repugnant, have a contrary nature. From this it is clear that the malefic, encountering the Apheta striking with a square from the beginning, kills more certainly by itself than by a square. The Arabs have taught that neither the bodies of the luminaries nor of the malefics, nor any of their rays, kill when they have taken over the dominion of life. Then follow another four Anaretas, and from the signs hearing or aspecting according to equivalence: As if at the time of birth the Apheta is in the second part of Gemini, but the Anareta is in the 29th part of Cancer: This condition, namely that from the beginning the Anareta is in aspect with the Aphetic place, is necessary here, but not 389. power in the aspects, which we said above kill by themselves: as if the Apheta is transiting Aries, but Saturn the Anareta is in Virgo casting its rays.

[Annual Profection Table and Calculation]
By means of this table, the less experienced will be able to easily determine to which sign any annual profection applies in any given year of age. For example, in our case, in the 41st year of age, which falls in the current year of Christ 1567, the annual profection of the Ascendant will reach 26 degrees 44 minutes of Aquarius, the Moon to 27 degrees 52 minutes of Gemini, the Sun to 8 degrees 54 minutes, the Midheaven to 1 degree 39 minutes, the Part of Fortune to 15 degrees 42 minutes of Scorpio, etc. Next, concerning the finding of the annual progression of aphetic places in days: If, he says, the year of profection reaches the degree of any sign and place, for example, to 17 degrees of Taurus, and if between it and a similar degree of the succeeding sign, that is, 17 degrees of Virgo, which ends the same year, and to which the same progression of the following year will devolve the body or rays of any planet, and it is desired to know the day on which the profection will reach the said planet or its rays; then multiply the degrees and minutes that fall between the degree to which the annual profection arrives and the planet or its rays by 12, that is, you will give to each degree 12 days and 4 hours, and the days will result, which are from the beginning of that year, until the time when the profection will apply to the planet or its rays. For example, in the same example, let the square rays of Saturn be in 5 degrees of Taurus, the arc intercepted between the first part of the sought profection, that is, 17 degrees, and the square rays of Saturn is 18 degrees, which multiplied by 12 produce 219 days of the revolution, at the end of which the progression will enter the rays of Saturn. Furthermore, you will thus calculate the distance or arc from the beginning of the annual profection to the beginning of the succeeding place, about which the question is, in degrees and minutes, if they are present. Take the aspect or other place, about whose application to the annual profection it is asked, and from it subtract the beginning of the annual profection, and the difference between the beginning of the annual profection and the proposed place will remain. For example, the epoch of the profection of the Ascendant in the assumed nativity in the year of Christ 1567, and the 41st year of the native's age, will reach, as we said a little earlier, 26 degrees 44 minutes of Aquarius. It is now asked on what day of the same year this progression will apprehend the square ray of Mars, which falls in 28 degrees 21 minutes of the same Aquarius. First, subtract the beginning of the annual profection from the place of Mars' square, and the middle distance will remain: 1 degree 37 minutes. Mars' square: 3 signs, 28 degrees, 21 minutes. Beginning of annual profection: 3 signs, 26 degrees, 44 minutes. Distance between the beginning of profection and Mars: 0 signs, 1 degree, 37 minutes. Now multiply 12 by the distance of 1 degree 37 minutes, and 19 days will result, at the end of which the profection of the Ascendant in this revolution will pass the square of Mars. Another example: It is desired to know on what day of the said year the profection will reach the square ray of the Sun, which falls in 8 degrees 54 minutes of Pisces. Subtracting the beginning of the annual profection from the Sun's square, 12 degrees 10 minutes remain, which multiplied by 12 produce 148 days, at the end of which the profection of the Ascendant in the said year of age will reach the Sun's square. But the less experienced will be able to calculate the time of annual progressions in days more easily with the help of the appended table. For having known the degrees and minutes by which the beginning of the profection and the succeeding place differ, enter the table with the whole degrees, for opposite it will present itself the time of the sought progression in days, hours, and minutes, to which for any first five minutes, if you add one day, you will have the true time of the profection. As in the previous example, 12 degrees correspond to 146 days, 2 hours, 19 minutes, to which if you add 2 days for 10 minutes, you will have the true time of 148 days, 2 hours, 19 minutes. Now, in order that you may know the month and day of the year into which the found application falls, having found the days of profection, add the days that are counted from the beginning of the year of Christ to the point of nativity or rather of revolution, which is nothing other than the Sun's return to its place in the nativity, for the number of days that arises from this will easily show in the usual table of months, which I have arranged for you here and above in the treatise on the horoscopic apheta, into which day of the month the found application of profection falls. In our example, from the beginning of the year of Christ to the root of the nativity, 141 days, 3 hours, 47 minutes have elapsed. If you wish to know this number more exactly, then by reason of the revolution of the 41st year, you must subtract 21 hours, 12 minutes from the aforesaid time, which done, the exact time of the revolution will remain, namely 140 days, 6 hours, 35 minutes, which time, joining to the found time of profection, that is, 148 days, we will produce 288 days, 6 hours, 35 minutes, from which number of days the next smaller number, namely 274, which is placed opposite September in the table of the bissextile year, being subtracted, leaves 14 complete days, 6 hours, 35 minutes of October, at the end of which the Ascendant will revolve to the square of the Sun. Observe that if by the addition of two times more days arise than a solar year contains, then if the current year was common, 365 days, if bissextile, 366 days, are to be rejected, and what remains is to be referred to the immediately succeeding year of Christ. Furthermore, Ptolemy, near the end of the Quadripartite Construction, teaches that the significators of any nativity progress not only by years, but also by months and days. And the method of annual profections has now been clearly explained. In the monthly profection, however, to each of the profectional months, which are 13 in number, one sign is given, and its lord is the ruler, as we said, so that the sign of any annual profection is the sign of the first profectional month of the same year. One year, therefore, is to be divided into 13 parts, each of which is called a profectional month. In this way, it will happen that in the succeeding revolution, both in the year and in the month, we arrive at the next sign by profection. As in the example above, in the 41st year, the annual profection of the Ascendant reached 26 degrees 44 minutes of Aquarius, which is the same.

[Profectional Months and Days]
The sign of the first profectional month of the same year is ♈; of the second, ♉; of the third, ♊; of the fourth, ♋; of the fifth, ♌; of the sixth, ♍; of the seventh, ♎; of the eighth, ♏; of the ninth, ♐; of the tenth, ♑; of the eleventh, ♒; of the twelfth, ♓; of the thirteenth, ♈; of the fourteenth, ♉, which profectional month is also the beginning of the following year. From this it is clear that the monthly profection has carried the annual rulership from one sign to another through one sign. Since the year is divided into 13 months, it follows that one profectional month contains 28 days, 2 hours, 17 scruples, 14, 37, 24. But Ptolemy omits hours and scruples, both because they could cause little error and because they were easily incorporated into constructed tables. Similarly, for diurnal profection, one profectional month must be divided into 13 equal parts, each of which will have approximately 2 days, 3 hours, and 52 scruples, 14. Moreover, to know how far the profection, both monthly and daily, extends to any given time in the year, calculate the time elapsed from the beginning of the annual revolution of the current year up to the proposed or assumed time, in this manner: First, count the days and the remaining parts of the time, if present, comprised between the beginning of the current usual month and the epoch of the nativity, or, which is the same, the point of revolution, and add this time to the number of days found opposite the immediately preceding usual month, placed in the first series if it was a common year, in the second if it was a bissextile year. The time that arises from this (which is that comprised between the beginning of the Roman or Christian year and the epoch of the Sun in the nativity) keep for the entire Solar year. Then, in the same way we said, learn how much time has elapsed from the beginning of the Roman year up to the proposed time: Finally, subtract the former from the latter, and the time elapsed from the root of the revolution up to the proposed time will remain. This measured time, now found, is to be sought in the table of profectional months, just as is usually done when the time corresponding to the mean motion of any planet is sought. And if you find the time precisely in the area of the table, the number on the left will show you the number of profectional months elapsed from the beginning of the current Solar year. If, however, you do not find your time precisely in the area of the table, take the exact next smaller time, and subtract it from the time you could not put into the table, so that the superfluous days with scruples remain. You will assign one sign to each profectional month, starting from the sign of the annual profection. The superfluous days with the adhering scruples, put into the table of monthly profection, and opposite them will appear the degrees and scruples to be added to the signs and degrees previously noted, and thus you will be led to the place of the zodiac where the profection arrives at the end of the elapsed time. If, in the manner described above, with the superfluous days, you enter the table of diurnal profection, you will extract the number of signs and degrees to be computed from the sign of the monthly profection: knowing these, you will have found the places of all profections. We will make the matter clearer with an exemplary discussion. In the assumed example and in the return of the 41st year, it was shown that the annual profection of the horoscope reached 26 degrees, 44 scruples, 13 of Aquarius, and that on May 20th completed, at 6 hours, 35 scruples, 14. For, from the time of the root, by reason of the present revolution, 21 hours, 12 scruples, 14 had to be removed, as we said a little earlier. Let us now, for example, investigate the places of the profections for the 9th day of July of the same current year. First, the time that elapsed from the beginning of the Roman year to the point of revolution is found to be 141 days, 6 hours, 35 scruples, 14, for the present year is a bissextile year. Then, similarly, the same time that extends from the same beginning to the proposed time is 191 days, from which if the former time is subtracted, namely 141 days, 6 hours, 35 scruples, 14, there will remain 49 days, 17 hours, 25 scruples, 14, which is the time measured from the root of the revolution to the limit of the proposed time. If you put this number of days and scruples of time into the area of the table already described by us, you will find that it corresponds to approximately 5 parts, which you join with 26 degrees, 44 scruples, 14 of Aquarius, making 1 degree, 44 scruples, 14 of Pisces. Therefore, you will declare that the annual progression of the horoscope has proceeded to 1 degree, 44 scruples, 14 of Pisces at the given time. Moreover, for obtaining the monthly profection, that time, namely 49 days, 17 hours, 25 scruples, 14, must be sought in the area of the following table of profectional months. But since it is not found there, subtract from it the next smaller number found there, namely 28 days, 2 hours, 17 scruples, 14, 37, 24, after which there will remain 21 days, 15 hours, 7 scruples, 14, 23, 24, beyond one profectional month. [Planetary Rule and Aphetic Places]
FOURTH 433. The rule of the Moon is transferred from Saturn to Jupiter and the Moon immediately following, which dominates up to the end of Libra, and 121st part of the 1st scruple of Scorpio, with Mars participating in the bounds in both places. For Mars holds the dominion of the bounds in the first six parts of Scorpio, both according to Ptolemy and the Egyptians. From here, a little after the first part of Scorpio, the rule of the rays is transferred from the Moon to Mercury, who projects his trine radiation into the 121st part of the 1st scruple of Scorpio, and by reason of these rays extends his rule up to the 28th part of Scorpio, with Mars participating first on account of the dominion of the bounds, then Jupiter, then Venus, and finally Mercury. From here, in the 28th part, 211th scruple of Scorpio, Mars assumes the most powerful rule of all: For besides the fact that he corporeally occupies the said place in his own house and trine, and being an enemy of the ascendant, he retrogrades in a fixed and venomous sign, with the testimony of the same Mars and Saturn, lords of the bounds of that direction, reaching the beginning of the 41st year, whose annual changes of signs and stellar progressions will be as follows: Annual Progressions. part.scr.1. Horosc. 26 44 ... 27 52 Lot 15 42 M.C. 1 39 Π Stellar progressions. part.scr.r. 8 54 20 3 08 54 Ⅱ 1158 44 46 retro. 22 20 2 550 21 44 13 18 m Another example: Let the horoscoping part be the sixth of Taurus, where there is no planet nor any ray (for if any planet or ray were in the horoscoping part, it would be the first arbiter of times), but nevertheless in the preceding place, that is, in the 4th part of Taurus, is the body of Jupiter, and in the following 12th part is the trine of the Moon, which is immediately followed by the body of Mars in the 12th part of Gemini, because DIFFERENCE 434 Jupiter will first govern life from the sixth part of Taurus, up to the 12th part of the same, where the trine rays of the Moon are: and the lord of the bounds will be its participant, but also powerful herself, for in the same place she has a trine and a house. We assign the first year to the sixth part, and not the fourth of Taurus, which Jupiter occupied near the ascendant, because, as has been said, the direction and the governance of the direction must begin from the place of the Apheta, and not from the place of the governor. Furthermore, from the 12th part of Taurus, up to the end of Taurus, indeed up to the 12th part of Gemini, since there are no other rays or planets in between, the Moon will govern with the lords of the bounds, but in many ways and not in one way. For from the 12th part up to the 24th part of the same, she will be more powerful than the lords of the bounds, because such is the magnitude of the Moon's light, which, the fuller it is, the greater its efficacy is to be judged. But from the 24th part to the end of Taurus, since the Moon has altitude in 8, her forces will be almost equal to the lord of the end of that part. Finally, from the beginning of Gemini to its twelfth part, on account of the distance of the trine rays, and the change of sign, where the Moon has no power, the lord of the end will have greater power than the Moon. In this way, therefore, we will create general arbiters of times. Signifiers. 7. The Aphetic places, or as they are called, illegal places, that is, places which progress, are five, from whose progression we gather what will happen to the native in his entire life. We consider the progression of the Ascendant as the Apheta, to perceive the native's health, what will happen to the body, and at what time useful or useless journeys will be undertaken. Therefore, when benefics or their good rays are led to the ascendant, we will decree good bodily habit and fortunate journeys for the native. But if malefics or their harmful rays occur to the same horoscope, we will predict bodily dyscrasia and unfortunate journeys for the native. Regarding the progressions of the other Aphetic places, we will pronounce in the same way concerning those things which signify fortune or misfortune. These places which are enumerated here, since they are the subjects of all goods, it follows that it is not necessary to proceed with any others besides these five in nativities. For all goods are referred either to the mind, or to the body, or to FOURTH. 435 or to fortune. Goods of the mind are decreed. Goods of the body depend on the ascendant. As for the goods of fortune, those which are more principal, such as dignities, are from: The mediocre ones, however, are taken from the horoscope and the M.C. The same number of places are also enumerated by Ptolemy and Hermes, enunciated 77. Ptolemy says: "The progression of the ascendant for those things which pertain to the body, the part of fortune for those things which are external, the Moon for the connection of the body and soul, the midheaven for actions." 1 2 Table of right ascensions G.G. m. [Lord of the Hour and Annual Predictions]
The lord of the hour signifies the health or illness of the native's body, just as the lord of the ascendant of the radix (nativity) signifies it. You will assign the lord of the second hour from it to the second house from the ascendant in the second year, and through it will be signified the substance in the same year, just as it is signified by the lord of the house of substance. And you will assign the lord of the third hour from it to the third house from the ascendant in the third year, and through it will be signified in the same year the brothers, sisters, and other things, just as it is signified by the lord of the third house. You will assign the lord of the fourth hour to the fourth house from the ascendant in the fourth year, and through its position in the same year will be signified the fathers and those who are signified by the fourth house. You will do similarly with the lords of the hours in succession, that is, you will assign the lord of each hour to a house from the radical houses. And the lord of the 12th hour from the hour of nativity will be the 12th house from the radical ascendant, and the 12th year. And the lord of the 13th hour from the nativity of the radical ascendant will be the 13th year. And the lord of the 14th hour from it will be the house of substance for the 14th year. And the lord of the first hour is called the lord of the ascendant of the hour, the lord of the second hour is called the lord of the house of substance, and the lord of the third hour is called the lord of the house of brothers; and so in others similarly, the lord of each of these hours is named by the name of the house, and is also called the lord of the orb, and is signified by it in every year just as it is signified by the Alcochoden, that is, by the lord of the year. And some astrologers place the lord of the orb, namely the radical ascendant, in the first year, and in the second year the planet that succeeds it, and in the third year the planet that succeeds this one, as has been said concerning the lord of the hour. And from this comes the Alfridaria disposition, that is, when the nativity is diurnal, the Sun will preside over its disposition at the beginning of life, according to the quantity of its Alfridaria years, which are ten. After this, the planet that succeeds the Sun, which is Venus, whose Alfridaria years are eight, and after Venus, the planet that succeeds her, which is Mercury, and its years are thirteen. Then the Moon: its Alfridaria years are nine; then Saturn, and its Alfridaria years are eleven; then Jupiter, and its Alfridaria years are twelve; then Mars, and its Alfridaria years are seven; then the head of the dragon, and its Alfridaria years are three; after this the tail, and its Alfridaria years are two. The years collected together are 75 years. After this, the disposition returns to the Sun; and similarly up to the last of the planets. If, however, the nativity is nocturnal, the disposition begins with the Moon, and it will dispose its Alfridaria years, which are nine. Similarly, planet after planet, as we said before, in the Sun. And when a planet has disposed its Alfridaria years, it will specifically dispose the first seventh alone, that is, the seventh part of its Alfridaria; then the planet that succeeds it participates with it in the second seventh; after this, the third planet, which succeeds the second, participates with it in the third seventh; and so until the planet that is before it participates with it in the last seventh of its Alfridaria years; and each has judgment when it participates with another over the nativity. The astrological elements of the author are now almost all explained, as far as they pertain to obtaining the truth. The rest, however, which follows, except for the chapter on the preeminence of the planets, and the lunar horoscope or part of fortunes, seem to dissent from nature, and to be more consonant with fortune-telling and the fortuitous cases of numbers, and other such trifles, than with true and physical reasons, and not undeservedly. For Ptolemy himself touches upon these very things by name in a few places, and then immediately rejects them as idle and empty: "These things, however," he says, "are probable, but not natural, but rather based on popular opinion." And around the beginning of the third book, he gravely criticizes such sophistical and superstitious astrology with these words: "Those things which many have curiously and petulantly sought, and which bear no verisimilitude, we will relegate to those things which are not conveniently said to be of nature; but those things which can be apprehended by nature, not through lots and numbers, to which no reasons of nature are inherent, but by observing the configurations of familiar places." Therefore, since the following things are also of this nature, we will briefly touch upon them. And from this, in inquiring into the dodecatemoria of the planets, one should attend to the measured spaces of the planets in the signs in which they are found, and having noted these by degrees and minutes, multiply the completed journey by 12, and to the number generated by the multiplication, add the whole that the planet has measured in the signs. Then, from the beginning of the sign in which the planet resides, project the sum collected, giving 30 degrees to each sign, for the end of the projection or numbering will show the dodecatemorium of the planet. For example, if the dodecatemorium of the Sun is to be sought, which is in 8 degrees, 54 minutes of Leo, multiply 8 degrees, 54 minutes by 12, and 60 degrees, 48 minutes will be produced, that is, 3 signs, 16 degrees, 48 minutes, to which if you add 8 degrees, 54 minutes, it will become 3 signs, 25 degrees, 42 minutes. Now give the first sign to Gemini, the second to Cancer, the third to Leo, and finally the dodecatemorium of the Sun will reach 25 degrees, 42 minutes of Virgo. In this way, the Sun placed in 9 degrees, 53 minutes of Libra projects its dodecatemorium into 8 degrees, 26 minutes of Sagittarius. And from this follows the order or series of the nine parts. If you divide an entire sign into 9 parts, each ninth portion, as they call it, will have 3 degrees, 20 minutes. And these parts are divided among the planets in such a way that the lord of the movable sign of the same triplicity presides over the first ninth part; the lord of the sign immediately following the movable sign over the second; and so consequently according to the dominion of the planets in the signs and the natural series of those signs. For example, Mars dominates the first ninth part, for it belongs to the fiery trigon, as they call it, whose movable sign is Aries and its lord is Mars. The ruler of the second ninth part of Leo is Venus, because Taurus, whose ruler is Venus, immediately follows Aries in the order of the signs. The lord of Gemini presides over the third ninth part of Leo. The Moon is the ruler of the fourth. Jupiter is the lord of the fifth. Saturn is the lord of the sixth. Mars is the lord of the eighth. Jupiter is the lord of the ninth, and so on for the rest. Therefore, if in reading Arabic writings, sentences concerning the lord of Anaubarach, or the lord of the luminaries, occur, we are warned in this chapter that they are to be understood concerning the dominion of the ninth part of the heretical light. And from this, the following jurisdiction of the decanates, how much it differs from the decans proposed in the first difference, is quite clear from the example recited here. If the first part of Aries encircles the eastern horizon, then the lord of the ascendant sign will be its decan; and if the second decuria of the same Aries ascends, its decan will be the Sun, the lord of the fifth sign from Aries and the second in the same trigon. Finally, if the third decuria of Aries ascends, then Jupiter will be considered its decan. For Jupiter is the ninth sign from Aries, and the third in the same trigon. Similarly, it is easy to judge concerning the remaining signs. And from this, if at any time it is desired to constitute those whom they call the rulers of the orb, then through what has been taught above in the last chapter of the second difference, diligently inquire into the temporal hour of the nativity, and attribute the horoscope to the lord of that hour, and the first year of the nativity; for it is said to signify in that year the health or illness of the native's body and all other things which the lord of the ascendant is accustomed to bestow. The lord of the following hour will preside over the following year and house, and in the same year is thought to obtain equal power with the lord of the second house. In exactly the same way, you will order the lords of the hours and the succeeding celestial stations, until you reach the significator of the twelfth house. However, with the twelfth year completed, in the following 13th year of the native's life, the first house will revert to the lord of the 13th hour, from which it will proceed in the same manner up to the end of the 24th year according to the order of the houses and planets.

[Method of Horary Judgment]
The second part of the method is about the thing they name. Thus, above the fourth house, it constitutes the significator of the father, which is minimally consistent with Ptolemy's doctrine. And this principle of consideration is, as it were, the matter or subject of what we have proposed to inquire into. Secondly, it must be observed which stars have the power to exercise dominion in these places, according to those whom we mentioned in the first difference, in five ways. And if one star obtains all prerogatives in the place of the significator, and presides in all ways, we must confer upon it all dominion and jurisdiction for determining its outcome. How one star can preside over one place in all ways has been shown in the first difference. But if two or more preside, we will transfer the principal power of decision to those that excel in the number of votes, with the others having fewer prerogatives participating. Since one of the five modes of dominion is aspect or configuration, it is clear that the planet which is constituted in the very place of the question, or shines upon it with its ray, should by no means be neglected. These rulers of places, not without reason, obtain a similarity to the efficient cause. Thirdly, the quality of the thing sought must be inquired into, or, which is the same, the genus of the question must be distinguished by qualities. For example, the matter or genus of the question is riches. This is distinguished by qualities in this way: whether the riches will be in money, or lands, or gifts, or other merchandise, or finally, will be acquired by some other industry and ingenuity. But in order to conjecture what the outcome will be, it is necessary to consider both the natures of the lords themselves, by whose name, as I warned before, we understand at the same time the place and the lords mixed with their rays, and the idiosyncrasies of the signs, the ruling planets, and the principal places they contain. Here also observe that by the name of signs are understood both the asterisms of the eighth sphere and the dodecatemoria of the world. The fourth part of the method is concerning the magnitude of the effect, of which three states are usually described in the art, namely, the highest, the middle, and the lowest. But the intermediate states that fall between those extremes, since they are almost infinite and cannot be comprehended by precepts, pertain to the artful conjecture and sagacity of the learned mathematician. This quantity of effects or decrees is taken from the strength of the ruling stars, which, as we shall show more clearly, God willing, in the following difference, chapter on fortunate and unfortunate places, is gathered from four circumstances, namely, their own nature, their own rays, the places of the heavens in which they are fixed, and finally, their genesis by comparison. The last part of the method pertains to the universal knowledge of the time of the decree. Here two things are observed in the rulers: first, whether they are matutine or vespertine, and this is compared to the horoscope. Those in the quadrants and preceding the horoscope and opposite to them are called matutine; the rest and those following are called vespertine by Ptolemy, as has been explained above. Then it must also be seen whether they are placed in angles or in succedent places. For when they are matutine or constituted in angles, they exert their power more quickly; if vespertine or in succedent places, more slowly. This general method of conjecturing the times of decrees must be taken simply; for their exquisite and exact definition pertains to the directions and other particular progressions to be explained below. Hence, what follows in the text can also be understood, namely, that the occidental signifies extreme old age, but the oriental signifies the beginning of old age; this must be referred to the last part of this method, that is, to the conjecture about the time of future events. For this can be excused in some way if by oriental and occidental Saturn you understand matutine and vespertine; and this, as said before, compared both to the Sun and to the world. But it seems that the author here is not dealing with time, which is taken from the disposition of the significators to the Sun and the angles of the world, but rather understands the seven ages common to all men, each of which, due to a certain disposition, agrees with and is distributed among individual planets. If this is so, he appears to be mistaken in two ways here. First, because he distributes the ages to the wandering stars differently from Ptolemy and less properly, and less consistently with nature, which those who wish to compare this author's opinion on ages with Ptolemy's opinion, which we will soon discuss, and which the author himself will describe at the end of this Difference, will easily understand. Secondly, because he follows a common error in saying that Saturn signifies extreme old age if it is occidental, but the beginning of old age if it is oriental. As if it mattered for this matter whether planets are occidental or oriental, well or ill placed in the geniture, and therefore that congruent effects corresponding to the disposition of the stars attributed to those ages should be expected in each age. For those err who think that the first 4 years (for example) attributed to the Moon, will therefore be happier than the following ten years, to which Mercury is assigned, because the Moon was better affected from the beginning. Just as we have often noted that herbs, plants, trees, animals, stones, metals, parts of the body, and similar forms of things are attributed to certain stars mainly because of their temperament. So also ages, each of which is endowed with a peculiar nature, agree with certain stars especially because of the similarity of their temperaments. For example, that extreme and worn-out age, being cold, dry, earthy, sluggish, trembling, inept, sickly, fearful, and impeded by such evils as follow the temperament of Saturn, is therefore rightly ascribed to Saturn. But this is not because of Saturn's disposition in the geniture, but because of the dyscrasia of this age, which is common to all men. For it is not that this or that man has Saturn ill-disposed at his birth, but all others, to whom it shone favorably, experience a deficiency of natural moisture, in old age. But that some experience old age more mildly or more troublesomely than others, must be referred to other particular causes, namely, to the diverse effects of diverse stars, which, falling into that age, produce such intentions and remissions in the common nature of old age. For since universally the bodies of all old people are more afflicted by the Sun going through the equinoxes due to the consent of disposition in the surrounding air, and conversely are, as it were, recreated in May due to their very humid constitution: who can now doubt that in particular constitutions, those in whose genitures benefic stars are found to show their power in that age will experience a milder old age, even if Saturn was ill-affected at the time of birth. But old age will be utterly afflicted if malefic stars are to assume dominion in it, no matter how well Saturn is placed in the geniture. The same judgment must be made concerning the other ages, which are numbered by Ptolemy to seven, according to the number of wandering stars. Indeed, Ptolemy, at the end of the Quadripartite construction, establishes four divisions of human life in time. The first and most general is into 7 ages, which, as I said, are common to all men, and are distributed among the planets according to their natural order. For the first four complete years, in which excessive humidity, and therefore sudden growth, epilepsy, and instability of health are most prevalent in the body, while in the mind all things are at least nascent and uncorrected, are attributed to the Moon, to whose temperament all these things correspond. This first period is called the age of infancy. From the beginning of the fifth year to the end of the 14th, Mercury's age succeeds the Moon's, which is called the age of childhood. This begins to compose minds for understanding, to implant the seeds of disciplines, to reveal peculiar conditions of morals and studies, and finally to excite the first rudiments of arts. Afterwards, from 14 to the 22nd year, Venus presides, during which time the age of adolescence is comprehended. This begins to move the seminal passages, which first

[The Sun's Beneficence and Ptolemy's Classification]
Lastly, because it is sometimes hindered and cannot help us, when this happens, great evils usually befall those who, turning against it, call it malefic, which is truly undeserved, as no one is better by nature. For it prolongs life, and benignly bestows a healthy body, innate strength, and a sincere and unwavering mind. It confers royal dignities and honors. It presents us with abundant wealth. It is fitting to believe that this is the soul of the entire world, or more plainly, its mind; this is the principal governance and number of nature, estimating its works. For it provides light to things and removes darkness. It conceals the other stars and tempers the most pleasing changes of seasons and the perpetually regenerating year according to nature. It dispels celestial sadness and also brightens the human mind's fog. It lends its light to other stars as well, being brilliant, exceptional, seeing all things, and even hearing all things, as Homer, the prince of letters, pleased, in the Iliad: 'the sun, he says, as they know, shines upon others.' Nazianzen compares it to the divine mind with these words: 'What the sun is to the body, God is to the soul.' There are therefore, to sum up everything, two stars, namely Saturn and Mars, which are harmful; and three, namely Jupiter, Venus, and the Moon, which are beneficial; and finally two, namely the Sun and Mercury, which are of both natures. Finally, it is useful to note that the planets which our astrologers call fortunate, unfortunate, and of both natures, Ptolemy simply names 'benefic,' 'malefic,' and 'intermediate.' His words on this are: 'Since we have distinguished two of the genera and again, two of the nature and manners of each, the unequal of the good and great, and that concerning the nature of each, and the external great ones being diminished. For the planets Jupiter, Venus, and the Moon are simply benefic, and among the intermediate are the Sun and Mercury, as in those concerning the disposition of parents and those in the soul, and those concerning outcomes and things pertaining to matters simply in the planet. For each of them differs in the quality of generation, such as the Sun, Mercury, and Moon. (And each of the others...)

[Planetary Influence on Birth and Soul]
Simply put, it is a benefic, and among those between the Sun and Mercury, as in matters concerning the disposition of parents and those in the soul, and in matters concerning outcomes and those pertaining to affairs, simply on the planet. For each of them differs in the quality of birth, such as the Sun and Mercury, and the Moon. (And each of the other remaining ones is simply a benefic, and among those between the Sun and Mercury, as in matters concerning the disposition of parents and those in the soul, and in matters concerning outcomes and those pertaining to affairs, simply on the planet. For each of them differs in the quality of birth, such as the Sun and Mercury, and the Moon. (And each of the other remaining ones is simply a benefic, and among those between the Sun and Mercury, as in matters concerning the disposition of parents and those in the soul, and in matters concerning outcomes and those pertaining to affairs, simply on the planet. For each of them differs in the quality of birth, such as the Sun and Mercury, and the Moon.

[Sun and Moon in Nativities]
But of the remaining planets, each differs in the quality of the nativity, such as the Sun and the Moon.

[Moon's Quality in Nativities]
The Moon. (Each of the other planets differs in the quality of its nativity, like the Sun and the Moon.)

[Sun and Moon in Nativities]
